Dispute on Pledged Slave Killed and Replaced
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pawned slave destroyed and replaced

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on substitute property (badal) in rahn and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding debt discharge and pawner's options.

Core Idea
The substitute stands in place of the original; the pawner must pay the full debt.

This passage presents a critical intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens when a pawned slave is killed and a substitute of lesser value is given to the mortgagee. Three positions emerge from the early Hanafi imams: Imam Zufar sees a proportional debt discharge, Imam Muhammad grants the pawner a choice, and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) insist on full payment of the original debt. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principles of trust (amanah), substitution (badal), and the prohibition of pre-Islamic debt practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal facts
Read the case carefully: a pawned slave (worth 1000) is killed by another slave (worth 100). The killer is given as substitute to the mortgagee. Note the three parties: pawner (raahin), mortgagee (murthihn), and the substitute slave (badal).
The substitute is the killer slave, not a monetary compensation.
2
Map each imam's ruling
List the three rulings: Zufar says debt reduced to 1/10 (100), substitute pawned for that. Muhammad gives two options (pay full 1000 to take substitute, or leave substitute as pawn for full 1000). Shaykhayn say pay full 1000 to take substitute; no option.
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in what the pawner pays/receives.
3
Analyze the proofs (adilla)
For each imam, identify the underlying legal reasoning: Zufar relies on strengthening of possession upon destruction and proportional discharge; Muhammad analogizes to sale (khiyar) and usurpation (ghasb); Shaykhayn argue the substitute replaces the original in substance, pawn is a trust (amanah) not to be transferred without consent, and that making pawn a substitute for debt is a pre-Islamic practice (abrogated).
Pay special attention to the Shaykhayn's refutation of Zufar and Muhammad.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preponderance)
The text presents the Shaykhayn's position as the relied-upon (mufta bihi). Understand why: the substitute stands exactly in place of the original, so no change occurred; the pawn is a trust; the mortgagee does not become owner; and the practice of making pawn equal to debt is abrogated.
This tarjih is based on usul al-fiqh principles like amanah and naskh.
5
Apply the ruling to a similar scenario
Consider a modern equivalent: car pawned for $10,000, destroyed, insurance pays $1,000 to mortgagee. Apply the Shaykhayn's ruling: the pawner must pay the full $10,000 to retrieve the $1,000 substitute (insurance money).
The substitute stands for the original; the debt remains unchanged.

تشریح راہن نے جو غلام ہزار کے بدلہ میں رہن رکھا تھا مرتہن کے پاس کسی غلام نے مرہون غلام کو قتل کر دیا اور قاتل غلام کی قیمت صرف سو روپے ہے اور محکم شرع یہی غلام قاتل مرہون کے بدلہ میں مرتہن کو دیدیا گیا تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ اس میں اختلاف ہے امام زفر کے نزدیک تو نرخ کی گھٹی مین کا جزو فوت ہونے کے مثل ہے لہذا عین کا ۱۰/ ۹ فوت ہو گیا اور اب مرتہن کا قرض راہن پر کل سوروپے رہا ۱/۱۰ اسی کی بدلہ میں یہ دوسرا غلام رہن مانا جائے گا۔ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ صورت مذکورہ میں را ہن کو دو اختیار ملیں گے۔

را ہن پورا قرض ادا کر کے مرتہن سے یہ دوسر اعلام لے لے۔ را ہن اس دوسرے غلام کو مرتہن کے قرض کے بدلہ میں مرتہن کے پاس چھوڑ دے شیخین نے فرمایا کہ راہن مرتبہن کا پورا قرض ادا کر کے مرہون کے قائم مقام دوسرے غلام کو لیگا اور بس :
امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرتین کا قبضہ قبضہ استیفاء ہوتا ہے اور ہلاکت سے یہ استیفاء مضبوط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور مرہون ہلاک ہو چکا ہے تو پورا قرض ساقط ہونا چاہیے تھا مگر چونکہ مرتہن کو مرہون غلام کا بدل سوروپے مل چکے ہیں جو اصل مرہون کا عشر یعنی ۱/۱۰ ہے تو اسی حساب سے قرض بھی ساقط ہو گا لہذا ۱۰ / ۹ ساقط ہو کر صرف ۱۰/ ۱ یعنی سوروپے قرض رہا جس کے بدلہ میں دوسرا غلام رہن ہے راہن سو روپے دیکر اس دوسرے غلام کو لیگا ۔ امام زفر کی دلیل توڑتے ہوئے ہمارے اصحاب نے کہا کہ اگر پہلا غلام موجود ہوتا اور صرف بھاؤ گھٹنے کی وجہ سے اس کی قیمت سو روپے باقی رہتی تو را ہن پورا قرض اداء کر کے اپنے غلام کو لیتا۔ اور یہاں چونکہ دوسرا غلام صورت اور معنی کے اعتبار سے اول کا قائم مقام ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی یونہی سمجھا جائے گا کہ اول غلام موجود ہے اور اس کی قیمت بھاؤ گھٹنے سے گھٹ گئی لہذا پورا قرض ادا کر کے راہن اس کو لینے کا حقدار ہوگا۔
امام محمد کی دلیل
ولمحمد في الخيار ان المرهون تغير فى ضمان المرتهن فيخير الراهن كالمبيع اذاقتل قبل القبض و المغصوب اذاقتل فى يد الغاصب يخير المشترى والمغصوب منه كذا هذا ترجمہ اور محمد کی دلیل خیار کے اندر یہ ہے کہ مرہون مرتہن کے ضمن میں متغیر ہوا ہے تو راہن مختار ہوگا جیسے مبیع جبکہ اس کو قبضہ ہے پہلے قتل کر دیا جائے اور مغصوب جبکہ اس کو غاصب کے قبضہ میں قتل کر دیا جائے تو مشتری اور مغصوب منہ کو اختیار دیا جاتا ہے تو ایسے ہی ہے۔ تشریح یہ امام محمد کی دلیل ہے فرماتے ہیں کہ مرہون میں جو تغیر پیدا ہوا ہے یہ مرتہن کے زیر ضمان داخل ہوتے ہوئے ہوا ہے لہذا راہن کو اختیار ملنا چاہیئے کیوں؟ کیونکہ اگر مبیع پر مشتری نے ابھی قبضہ نہیں کیا کہ اس کو کسی غلام نے قتل کر دیا جس کی وجہ سے قاتل غلام مبیع غلام کے عوض میں دید یا تو اب مشتری کو اختیار ہوتا ہے خواہ پورے شمن کے بدلے میں اس دوسرے غلام کو لے لے خواہ بیع کو فسخ کر دے تو اسی طرح یہاں بھی راہن کو اختیار ملنا چاہئے ۔ اسی طرح اگر غاصب قبضہ میں مغصوب غلام کو کسی غلام نے قتل کر دیا تھا جس کی وجہ سے قاتل غلام مقتول غلام کے عوض میں دیا گیا تو مغصوب منہ کو اختیار ہے خواہ اس دوسرے غلام کو لے لے اور خواہ غاصب سے اپنے غلام کی قیمت لے لے اسی طرح یہاں بھی راہن کو اختیار ملنا چاہیئے۔
شیخین کی دلیل
ولهما ان التغير لم يظهر فى نفس العبد لقيام الثانى مقام الاول لحما ودما كما ذكرناه مع زفر وعين الرهن امانة عندنا فلا يجوز تمليكه منه بغیر رضاه ولان جعل الرهن بالدين حكم جاهلى وانه منسوخ بخلاف البيع لان الخيار فيه حكمه الفسخ وهو مشروع وبخلاف الغصب لان تملكه باداء الضمان مشروع ترجمہ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تغیر نفس غلام میں ظاہر نہیں ہوا گوشت اور خون کے اعتبار سے ثانی کے اول کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ ہم اس کو ذکر کر چکے ہیں زفر کے ساتھ ( گفتگو میں ) اور عین رہن امانت ہے ہمارے نزدیک تو جائز نہیں ہے راہن کا مرتہن کو بغیر مرتین کی رضامندی کے مالک بنا دینا اور اس لئے کہ رہن کو قرض کے بدلہ میں کرنا حکم جاہلی ہے اور یہ منسوخ ہے بخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ بیچ میں خیار کا حکم فسخ کا ہے اور یہ مشروع ہے اور بخلاف غصب کے اس لئے کہ ادا ضمان سے غاصب کا مالک ہو جانا مشروع ہے تشریح یہ شیخین کی دلیل ہے کہ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم ابھی امام زفر سے گفتگو کرتے ہوئے بتا چکے ہیں کہ دوسرا غلام اول کا قائم مقام ہے لہذا انفس غلام مرہون میں تغیر نہیں ہوا تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ پہلا غلام موجود ہے اور اس کی قیمت گھٹی ہے اس صورت میں یہ جائز نہیں ہوتا کہ غلام کو بغیر مرتہن کی رضا مندی کے مرتہن کو دیدیا جائے ۔ نیز اوائل کتاب الرہن میں گزر چکا ہے کہ مین مرہون امانت ہے اور امانت میں بھی جائز نہیں ہوتا کہ بغیر رضاء اس کو مودع پر تھوپ دیا جائے۔
نیز رہن کو قرض کا بدل قرار دینا زمانہ جاہلیت کا حکم ہے جس کو شریعت نے منسوخ کر دیا ہے لہذا منسوخ پر عمل کے کیا منی ؟ کہ را ہن کو اختیار ہے کہ غلام ثانی قرض کے بدلہ میں مرتہن کو دیدے اور آپ نے امام محمد جو اس کو بیع اور غصب پر قیاس کیا ہے تو یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیوں؟
اس لئے کہ بیچ میں جو خیار ملا ہے اس کا مقصد فتح ہے اور فسخ بیچ میں جائز ہے اور رہن میں جائز نہیں تو پھر قیاس کیسا؟ نیز غاصب اداء ضمان کی وجہ سے مغصوب کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے اور مرتهن قرض کی وجہ سے مرہون کا مالک نہیں ہوتا تو پھر قیاس کیسا جبکہ علت جامعہ مفقود ہے۔
Explanation: A pawner had pawned a slave for one thousand. With the mortgagee, a slave killed the pawned slave, and the killer slave's value is only one hundred rupees. The court gave this killer slave to the mortgagee in exchange for the pawned slave. What is the ruling? It was said there is disagreement. According to Imam Zufar, it is like a loss of part of the substance due to price drop, so 9/10 of the substance was lost, and now the mortgagee's debt on the pawner remains one hundred rupees, and this second slave is considered pawned in exchange for 1/10. Imam Muhammad said: In this case, the pawner will have two options: 1) The pawner pays the entire debt and takes this second slave from the mortgagee. 2) The pawner leaves this second slave with the mortgagee in exchange for the debt. The Shaykhayn said: The pawner pays the entire debt to the mortgagee and takes the second slave, which stands in place of the pawned slave, and nothing more. Imam Zufar's proof: The mortgagee's possession is a possessory right, and destruction strengthens this right. Since the pawned slave is destroyed, the entire debt should be discharged. But because the mortgagee received the substitute of the pawned slave worth one hundred, which is 1/10 of the original, the debt is also discharged proportionally, so 9/10 is discharged, leaving only 1/10, i.e., one hundred rupees, as debt, and the second slave is pawned for that. The pawner pays one hundred and takes the second slave. Refuting Imam Zufar, our companions said: If the first slave were present and its price had dropped to one hundred, the pawner would pay the full debt and take his slave. Here, since the second slave is the substitute of the first in form and meaning, it is as if the first slave is still there with its price reduced, so the pawner is entitled to take it by paying the full debt. Imam Muhammad's proof: For Muhammad, there is an option because the pawned slave changed while in the mortgagee's guarantee, so the pawner has a choice, like a sold item killed before delivery, or a usurped item killed in the usurper's hand – the buyer and the owner of the usurped item have a choice. So here, the pawner should have a choice. The Shaykhayn's proof: The change did not appear in the essence of the slave because the second slave stands in place of the first in flesh and blood, as mentioned with Zufar. Moreover, the pawned item is a trust with us, so it is not permissible to transfer ownership of it to the mortgagee without his consent. Also, making the pawn a replacement for the debt is a pre-Islamic custom and is abrogated. This differs from sale because the option in sale leads to rescission, which is legitimate, and differs from usurpation because the usurper becomes owner by paying the guarantee, which is legitimate.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a pawned slave killed by another slave, with the killer given as compensation. The issue: the original pawned slave was worth 1000, but the killer is worth only 100. The court gives the killer to the mortgagee. Three positions emerge. Imam Zufar treats the price drop as partial destruction of the pawn: since the substitute is 1/10 of the original value, only 1/10 of the debt remains, and the substitute is pawned for that fraction. Imam Muhammad grants the pawner two options: pay the full debt to release the substitute, or leave the substitute as pawn for the full debt. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rule that the pawner must pay the full debt to retrieve the substitute, as the substitute stands in the place of the original, so no change occurred in the actual pawn; the mortgagee's right to the debt remains intact. The commentary then details each imam's proof. Imam Zufar's proof: the mortgagee's possession becomes stronger upon destruction, so the debt should be discharged proportionally to the value received. The Hanafi majority refute this by analogizing to a price drop without destruction. Imam Muhammad analogizes to sale and usurpation, where the buyer and owner have options when the item is destroyed before delivery. The Shaykhayn refute this: in sale, rescission is allowed, but in pawn it is not; in usurpation, the usurper becomes owner by paying the value, but the mortgagee does not become owner of the pawn. Also, making the pawn a substitute for the debt is an abrogated pre-Islamic practice. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Shaykhayn, as it aligns with the principles that the pawn remains a trust and cannot be transferred without consent, and that the pawn is not a sale of the debt.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract by which property is held as security for a debt; the pawn.
مرهون (marthun): The property that is pawned (the pawned slave).
راهن (rahin): The person who pawns the property (the debtor).
مرتهن (murthihn): The person who receives the pawn (the creditor).
قیمت (qimat): Market value or price of a commodity (here, the slave).
بدل (badal): Substitute or compensation (the killer slave given in place of the pawned slave).
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; the mortgagee's guarantee over the pawn.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): Option or choice given to a contracting party (here, the pawner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) in this passage, what must the pawner (raahin) do to take possession of the substitute slave?
A) Pay only the reduced value of the original slave (100 rupees).
B) Pay the full original debt (1000 rupees).
C) Choose between paying 100 rupees or leaving the substitute as pawn.
D) Nothing; the substitute automatically becomes the mortgagee's property.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi ruling: when a pawned item is destroyed and replaced, the substitute takes the place of the original; the pawner must pay the full debt to retrieve it, and no option or proportional discharge applies.

Replacement of a Depreciated Mortgaged Slave: Imam Muhammad vs. Shaykhayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on replacement of mortgaged slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding replacement of a mortgaged slave whose value has decreased, and explain the key difference in their qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
The mortgagee cannot take a replacement for a depreciated collateral without the mortgagor's consent, because the collateral is a trust and qiyas to sale or usurpation is flawed.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a mortgaged item loses value and is destroyed, can the mortgagee demand a replacement without the owner's permission? This passage reveals an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), rooted in different analogies. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate qiyas and recognize the limits of analogical reasoning in muamalat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
A mortgaged slave's value decreases, then he is killed by another slave of equal current value. The killer is offered as replacement. The question: can the mortgagee (murtahin) take this replacement without the mortgagor's (rahin) consent?
The core is whether the mortgagee can unilaterally substitute the collateral.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and his qiyas
Imam Muhammad allows the replacement by analogy to sale (right of rescission) and usurpation (ownership by paying guarantee). He sees the replacement as compensating the loss in value.
His qiyas equates the situation to cases where substitution is permitted.
3
State the Shaykhayn's position and their objections
The Shaykhayn reject the analogy. They argue: (1) the replacement stands in place of the original, so no real change; (2) the mortgaged property is a trust (amanah), so cannot be forced on the mortgagee; (3) rahn as substitute for debt is a pre-Islamic practice, abrogated; (4) in sale rescission is legitimate, in rahn it is not; (5) in usurpation, ownership comes by paying guarantee, but the mortgagee does not own by the debt.
They emphasize that the 'illa (effective cause) of the analogies does not apply to rahn.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
According to Imam Muhammad, the mortgagee can take the replacement. According to the Shaykhayn, he cannot; the mortgagor retains control and must consent to any transfer.
Practical difference: who bears the risk of value fluctuation?
5
Note the tarjih and its basis
The text presents the Shaykhayn's reasoning in detail and implies it is stronger. The mention of an objection from the author of Nata'ij suggests their view is relied upon. The mortgagee cannot unilaterally take the replacement.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice follows the Shaykhayn.

Source Text

کے عوض میں دیا گیا تو مغصوب منہ کو اختیار ہے خواہ اس دوسرے غلام کو لے لے اور خواہ غاصب سے اپنے غلام کی قیمت لے لے اسی طرح یہاں بھی راہن کو اختیار ملنا چاہیئے۔ شیخین کی دلیل ولهما ان التغير لم يظهر فى نفس العبد لقيام الثانى مقام الاول لحما ودما كما ذكرناه مع زفر وعين الرهن امانة عندنا فلا يجوز تمليكه منه بغیر رضاه ولان جعل الرهن بالدين حكم جاهلى وانه منسوخ بخلاف البيع لان الخيار فيه حكمه الفسخ وهو مشروع وبخلاف الغصب لان تملكه باداء الضمان مشروع ترجمہ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تغیر نفس غلام میں ظاہر نہیں ہوا گوشت اور خون کے اعتبار سے ثانی کے اول کے قائم مقام ہونے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ ہم اس کو ذکر کر چکے ہیں زفر کے ساتھ ( گفتگو میں ) اور عین رہن امانت ہے ہمارے نزدیک تو جائز نہیں ہے راہن کا مرتہن کو بغیر مرتین کی رضامندی کے مالک بنا دینا اور اس لئے کہ رہن کو قرض کے بدلہ میں کرنا حکم جاہلی ہے اور یہ منسوخ ہے بخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ بیچ میں خیار کا حکم فسخ کا ہے اور یہ مشروع ہے اور بخلاف غصب کے اس لئے کہ ادا ضمان سے غاصب کا مالک ہو جانا مشروع ہے تشریح یہ شیخین کی دلیل ہے کہ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم ابھی امام زفر سے گفتگو کرتے ہوئے بتا چکے ہیں کہ دوسرا غلام اول کا قائم مقام ہے لہذا انفس غلام مرہون میں تغیر نہیں ہوا تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ پہلا غلام موجود ہے اور اس کی قیمت گھٹی ہے اس صورت میں یہ جائز نہیں ہوتا کہ غلام کو بغیر مرتہن کی رضا مندی کے مرتہن کو دیدیا جائے ۔ نیز اوائل کتاب الرہن میں گزر چکا ہے کہ مین مرہون امانت ہے اور امانت میں بھی جائز نہیں ہوتا کہ بغیر رضاء اس کو مودع پر تھوپ دیا جائے۔ نیز رہن کو قرض کا بدل قرار دینا زمانہ جاہلیت کا حکم ہے جس کو شریعت نے منسوخ کر دیا ہے لہذا منسوخ پر عمل کے کیا منی ؟ کہ را ہن کو اختیار ہے کہ غلام ثانی قرض کے بدلہ میں مرتہن کو دیدے اور آپ نے امام محمد جو اس کو بیع اور غصب پر قیاس کیا ہے تو یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ بیچ میں جو خیار ملا ہے اس کا مقصد فتح ہے اور فسخ بیچ میں جائز ہے اور رہن میں جائز نہیں تو پھر قیاس کیسا؟ نیز غاصب اداء ضمان کی وجہ سے مغصوب کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے اور مرتهن قرض کی وجہ سے مرہون کا مالک نہیں ہوتا تو پھر قیاس کیسا جبکہ علت جامعہ مفقود ہے۔ غلام مرہون کی قیمت پہلے زیادہ تھی بعد میں کم ہو گئی اس کو کسی غلام نے قتل کر دیا جس کی قیم [؟] میرسون کی فی الحال قیمت کے برابر ہے تو قاتل غلام مرتہن کو دیا جائے گا یا نہیں ولو كان العبد تراجع سعره حتى صار يساوى مائة ثم قتله عبد يساوى مائة فدفع به فهو على لهذا الخلاف . ترجمہ اور اگر غلا کم بھاؤ گھٹ گیا ہوتو یہاں تک کہ وہ سو کے برابر ہو گیا پھر اس کو ایسے غلام نے قتل کر دیا جو سو کے برابر ہے پس قاتل اس کے بدلہ میں دیا گیا تو وہ بھی اسی اختلاف پر ہے، تشریح غلام مرہون کی قیمت ہزار روپے تھی مگر بھاؤ کے پلٹا کھانے کی وجہ سے اب اس کی قیمت سوروپے رہ گئی اب اس کو کسی غلام نے قتل کیا جس کی قیمت بھی سو روپے ہے پھر قاتل غلام مرتہن کو دیا گیا تو اس میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے جو مذکور ہوا باقی تفصیل ظاہر ہے اس پر صاحب نتائج کا اشکال بھی ہے جو حاشیہ میں موجود ہے۔
If [the replacement slave] was given in exchange, then the victim of usurpation (maghsub minhu) has the option: either take that other slave or take the price of his slave from the usurper. Similarly here, the rahin should have the option. The proof of the Shaykhayn: And for them, the change did not appear in the slave itself because the second takes the place of the first in flesh and blood, as we mentioned with Zufar. And the mortgaged object (ayn al-rahn) is a trust (amanah) with us, so it is not permissible to make the murtahin its owner without his consent. Also because making the rahn in exchange for a debt is a pre-Islamic practice and it is abrogated. Unlike sale, because the right of option in it is for rescission, and that is legitimate. And unlike usurpation, because the usurper becomes owner by paying the guarantee. Explanation: This is the proof of the Shaykhayn. The gist: we already explained with Imam Zufar that the second slave stands in place of the first, so there is no change in the mortgaged slave. Thus it is as if the first slave exists but its price decreased; in this case it is not permissible to give the slave to the murtahin without his consent. Also it passed earlier in the beginning of Kitab al-Rahn that the mortgaged object is a trust, and in a trust it is not permissible to burden the depositee without his consent. Also making the rahn a substitute for debt is a pre-Islamic practice abrogated by Shari'ah, so how can it be acted upon? That the rahin has the option to give the second slave to the murtahin for the debt, and Imam Muhammad's analogy to sale and usurpation is a flawed analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). Because in sale, the option aims at rescission, and rescission is permissible in sale but not in rahn. Also the usurper becomes owner due to payment of guarantee, while the murtahin does not become owner of the mortgaged object due to the debt, so how can the analogy hold when the shared effective cause is missing? The value of the mortgaged slave was higher then decreased; if he is killed by a slave of equal current value, should the killer be given to the murtahin? And if the slave's price receded until it became equal to 100, then a slave worth 100 killed him, and the killer is handed over as compensation, then it is subject to this same disagreement. Translation: And if the price of the slave decreased until it became equal to 100, then a slave worth 100 killed him, then the killer was given in exchange, then it is subject to this same disagreement. Explanation: The mortgaged slave was worth 1000 rupees but due to price fluctuation became 100; then a slave worth 100 killed him; then the killer is given to the murtahin, and the same disagreement applies as mentioned. The rest of the detail is apparent, and there is an objection from the author of Nata'ij in the marginal note.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The issue: if a mortgaged slave's value decreases and then he is killed by another slave of equal value, may the killer be given to the mortgagee (murtahin) as a replacement without the mortgagor's (rahin) consent? Imam Muhammad analogizes to sale (where the seller has the right to cancel) and usurpation (where the usurper becomes owner by paying compensation) and thus allows the murtahin to take the replacement. The Shaykhayn reject this analogy, arguing: (1) there is no actual change in the slave because the replacement stands in place of the original in essence; (2) the mortgaged property is a trust (amanah) in the murtahin's hands, so he cannot be forced to accept ownership; (3) making the rahn a substitute for debt is a pre-Islamic practice abrogated by Islam; (4) in sale, the right of option is for rescission, which is legitimate, but in rahn rescission is not allowed; (5) in usurpation, the usurper becomes owner by paying guarantee, while the murtahin does not become owner merely by the debt. Hence, the Shaykhayn require the rahin's consent for any transfer. The passage then applies this dispute to a case where the value drops and a slave of equal value kills the mortgaged slave: the same disagreement applies.

Key Terms
راهن (rahin): The pledgor/mortgagor who gives the collateral.
مرتهن (murtahin): The person who receives the collateral (mortgagee/pledgee).
عين الرهن (ayn al-rahn): The specific property that is pawned/mortgaged.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy where the effective cause (illa) differs between the original and new case, rendering it invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), why cannot the mortgagee (murtahin) take a replacement slave without the mortgagor's consent?
A) Because the mortgagee already owns the slave.
B) Because the mortgaged object is a trust (amanah) and the mortgagee cannot be forced to own it.
C) Because the slave's value increased.
D) Because the mortgagor has no right to the replacement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi rahn, the collateral remains a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hands; unilateral substitution without the mortgagor's consent is not permitted, as the Shaykhayn's reasoning demonstrates.

Liability for Accidental Murder by Mortgaged Slave
States ruling that mortgagee bears diyah and cannot hand over the slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability of the mortgagee and mortgagor when a mortgaged slave commits accidental murder, and apply the rule to determine who pays the blood money and the consequences.

Core Idea
The mortgagee bears the blood money for the slave's accidental crime; he cannot hand over the slave, only pay.

This passage from Kitab al-Rahn presents a specific ruling regarding torts committed by a mortgaged slave. Understanding the allocation of liability between mortgagee and mortgagor is essential for correctly applying the law of security (rahn). The ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that the possessor (mortgagee) is responsible for damages arising from the property in his custody.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the event
The case involves a mortgaged slave (al-`abd al-marhun) who accidentally kills someone. Identify the parties: mortgagee (murtahin) who holds possession, and mortgagor (rahin) who owns the slave.
Accidental killing (khatā) means no intent, so it is a tort, not a crime requiring qisas.
2
State the primary ruling
The primary ruling is that liability (daman) for the blood money (diyah/fidyah) is upon the mortgagee. He must pay and cannot hand over the slave to the victim's family.
Why can't he hand over? Because he is not the owner; the mortgagor retains ownership.
3
Analyze the consequence of payment by mortgagee
If the mortgagee pays, the slave becomes purified (the victim's claim is satisfied), the debt remains, and the mortgagee cannot recover the payment from the mortgagor.
The rationale is that the crime occurred under the mortgagee's liability (daman), so he must bear the cost.
4
Evaluate the scenario if mortgagee refuses
If the mortgagee refuses to pay, the responsibility shifts to the mortgagor (owner), who has two options: hand over the slave (which cancels the debt) or pay the blood money himself (which also cancels the debt).
Both options effectively terminate the mortgage, because the slave is lost or redeemed.
5
Identify the underlying legal principle
The ruling is based on the principle that the person in possession (mortgagee) is liable for torts of the property, and the owner (mortgagor) ultimately bears the risk if the mortgagee defaults.
This is consistent with the Hanafi maxim 'al-ghurm bi al-ghunm' (liability accompanies benefit).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قتل الـعبــد الرهن قتيلا خطا فضمان الجناية على المرتهن وليس له ان يدفع لانه لا يملك التمليك ولو فدى طهر المحل فبقى الدين على حاله ولا يرجع على الراهن بشئى من الفداء لان الجناية حصلت في ضمانه فكان عليه اصلاحها ترجمہ اور جب کہ خطا مرہون غلام نے کسی شخص کو قتل کر دیا تو جنایت کا ضمان مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوگا اور مرتہن کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ وہ غلام دیدے اس لئے مرتین مالک بنانے کا مالک نہیں ہے اور اگر مرتہن نے فدیہ ادا کر دیا تو محل ( مرہون ) پاک ہو گیا تو قرض اپنے حال پر باقی رہا اور مرتہن فدیہ میں سے کچھ راہن سے کچھ نہیں لے گا اس لئے کہ جنایت مرتبہن کے ضمان میں حاصل ہوتی ہے تو مرتہن ہی پر ، سلاح جنایت واجب ہوگی۔ تشریح مرتہن کے پاس رہتے ہوئے مرہون غلام نے خطا کسی شخص کوقتل کر دیا تو ضمان مرتہن پر لازم ہوگا۔ اور یہاں ضمان کی صرف ایک ہی صورت ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مرتبین مقتول کا فدیہ ادا کر دے اور جب مرتہن نے فدیہ ادا کر دیا تو مرہون پر جو جنایت تھی وہ ختم ہوگئی اور مرتہن کا قرض بدستور را ہن پر برقرار رہا۔ اب اگر مرتہن چاہے کہ میں نے جو ضمان ادا کیا ہے وہ راہن سے واپس لے لوں تو نہیں لے سکتا کیونکہ غلام نے یہ جنایت مرتہن کے زیر ضمان داخل رہتے ہوئے کی ہے جس کی ذمہ داری مرتہن پر ہوتی ہے لہذا اس نے اپنی ذمہ داری کے ماتحت غلام مرہون کو جنایت سے پاک کر دیا تو یہ ضمان راہن سے نہیں لے سکتا۔ بہر حال یہاں مرتہن کو صرف فدیدینے کا اختیار ہے اگر وہ غلام کو منمان میں دینے لگے تو اس کا اس کو حق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مرتہن غلام کا مالک نہیں ہے جب وہ خود ہی مالک نہیں ہے تو دوسرے کو کیسے مالک بنا سکتا ہے۔ مرتهن فدیہ دینے سے انکار کر دے تو کیا حکم ہے ولو أبى المرتهن ان يفدى قيل للراهن ادفع العبد او افده بالدية لان الملك في الرقبة قائم له وانما الى المرتهن الفداء لقيام حقه فاذا امتنع عن الفداء يطالب الراهن بحكم الجناية ومن حكمها التخيير بين الدفع والفداء فان اختار الدفع سقط الدين لانه استحق لمعنى فى ضمان المرتهن فصار کالهلاک و کذالک ان فدى لان العبد كالحاصل له بعوض كان على المرتهن وهو الفداء
And if the mortgaged slave kills a person accidentally, then liability for the crime is upon the mortgagee, and he does not have the right to hand over [the slave] because he does not own the right to transfer ownership. And if he pays the ransom (fidyah), the mortgaged property becomes purified, the debt remains as it was, and he does not claim anything of the ransom from the mortgagor because the crime occurred under his (the mortgagee's) liability, so it was upon him to rectify it. Explanation: While in the mortgagee's possession, if the mortgaged slave accidentally kills someone, the liability (daman) is incumbent on the mortgagee. And here there is only one form of liability: the mortgagee pays the ransom of the victim. When he pays, the crime is removed from the slave, and the mortgagee's debt remains against the mortgagor. If the mortgagee wants to recover what he paid as ransom from the mortgagor, he cannot, because the slave committed the crime while under the mortgagee's liability, so he is responsible. Therefore, he clears the slave of the crime at his own expense, and cannot claim from the mortgagor. In any case, the mortgagee only has the option to pay ransom; if he attempts to hand over the slave instead, he has no right, because he is not the owner. How can he transfer ownership? If the mortgagee refuses to pay ransom, then the mortgagor is told: hand over the slave or pay the blood money (diyah), because ownership of the slave's corpus remains with him, and the mortgagee's right is only to pay ransom due to his lien. So if he refuses, the mortgagor is addressed by the law of the crime, which gives the choice between handing over and paying ransom. If he chooses to hand over, the debt is cancelled because it is as if the slave perished under the mortgagee's liability; similarly if he pays ransom, because the slave becomes as if acquired by him in exchange for what was on the mortgagee, i.e., the ransom.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Rahn explains the ruling when a mortgaged slave commits accidental murder (qatl khatā). The mortgagee (murtahin) is liable for the blood money (diyah/fidyah) because the slave is in his custody and the crime occurs under his responsibility. He cannot hand over the slave to the victim's family because he does not own the slave; the mortgagor (rahin) retains ownership. If the mortgagee pays the ransom, the slave becomes 'pure' (free from the claim of the victim's family), the debt remains on the mortgagor, and the mortgagee cannot recover the ransom from the mortgagor because the liability was his own. If the mortgagee refuses to pay, then the responsibility returns to the mortgagor (owner), who is given the option: either hand over the slave to the victim's family (which cancels the debt) or pay the blood money himself (which also cancels the debt, as the slave is effectively redeemed). The rationale is that the debt is considered replaced by the value of the slave, similar to destruction under the mortgagee's liability.

Key Terms
جنایت خطا (jināyat khaṭā): Accidental killing or injury caused by the slave without intent.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom or blood money paid to free the slave from the liability of the crime.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or responsibility for loss or damage; here the mortgagee's liability for acts of the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged slave accidentally kills someone and the mortgagee refuses to pay the blood money, what option does the mortgagor have?
A) The mortgagor must also refuse and the slave is executed.
B) The mortgagor can either hand over the slave (cancelling the debt) or pay the blood money himself.
C) The mortgagor can force the mortgagee to pay by taking the slave back.
D) The debt becomes void automatically.

Key Takeaway
When a mortgaged slave causes accidental harm, the mortgagee bears the blood money, cannot hand over the slave, and if he refuses, the mortgagor may choose to surrender the slave or pay, both cancelling the debt.

Liability for Accidental Killing by a Mortgaged Slave
Ruling on when a mortgaged slave kills someone by mistake

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mortgaged slave accidentally kills someone and explain why the mortgagee cannot hand over the slave.

Core Idea
The mortgagee must pay the diyah for a slave's accidental killing because the slave is in his guarantee; he cannot hand over what he does not own.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario in the contract of rahn (mortgage/pledge): what happens if the mortgaged slave commits accidental homicide while in the mortgagee's possession? The ruling clarifies that the mortgagee bears financial liability, not the mortgagor, and cannot simply transfer the slave as compensation. The reasoning hinges on the fact that the mortgagee holds the slave as a trust (amanah) but does not own him, so he cannot transfer ownership.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the parties and the event
Identify the mortgagor (rahin), mortgagee (murtahin), and the mortgaged slave (marhun). The event is an accidental killing (qatl khata) by the slave.
The slave is in the possession of the mortgagee but owned by the mortgagor.
2
2. Determine who is liable for the diyah
According to the text, the guarantee (daman) of the crime falls on the mortgagee, not the mortgagor. This is because the slave is under the mortgagee's guarantee during the period of possession.
3
3. Examine the mortgagee's options
The mortgagee cannot hand over the slave to the victim's heirs because he does not own the slave and therefore cannot transfer ownership. His only option is to pay the ransom (fida) himself.
The text states: 'he does not own the ability to transfer ownership.'
4
4. Understand the consequences of payment
Once the mortgagee pays the ransom, the slave is purified from the crime, and the original debt remains unchanged. The mortgagee cannot recover the payment from the mortgagor.
The crime occurred in the mortgagee's guarantee, so he is responsible for rectifying it.
5
5. Summarize the ruling's rationale
The rationale (talil) is that possession creates a guarantee (daman yad). Since the slave was in the mortgagee's possession, the damage is attributed to him, not the owner.
This principle is consistent with broader Hanafi rules on liability for possessions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہون غلام کسی کو خطا فیل کر دے جنایت کا ضمان کس پر لازم ہے
واذا قتل الـعبــد الرهن قتيلا خطا فضمان الجناية على المرتهن وليس له ان يدفع لانه لا يملك التمليك ولو فدى طهر المحل فبقى الدين على حاله ولا يرجع على الراهن بشئى من الفداء لان الجناية حصلت في ضمانه فكان عليه اصلاحها
ترجمہ اور جب کہ خطا مرہون غلام نے کسی شخص کو قتل کر دیا تو جنایت کا ضمان مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوگا اور مرتہن کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ وہ غلام دیدے اس لئے مرتین مالک بنانے کا مالک نہیں ہے اور اگر مرتہن نے فدیہ ادا کر دیا تو محل ( مرہون ) پاک ہو گیا تو قرض اپنے حال پر باقی رہا اور مرتہن فدیہ میں سے کچھ راہن سے کچھ نہیں لے گا اس لئے کہ جنایت مرتبہن کے ضمان میں حاصل ہوتی ہے تو مرتہن ہی پر ، سلاح جنایت واجب ہوگی۔ تشریح مرتہن کے پاس رہتے ہوئے مرہون غلام نے خطا کسی شخص کوقتل کر دیا تو ضمان مرتہن پر لازم ہوگا۔ اور یہاں ضمان کی صرف ایک ہی صورت ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مرتبین مقتول کا فدیہ ادا کر دے اور جب مرتہن نے فدیہ ادا کر دیا تو مرہون پر جو جنایت تھی وہ ختم ہوگئی اور مرتہن کا قرض بدستور را ہن پر برقرار رہا۔
اب اگر مرتہن چاہے کہ میں نے جو ضمان ادا کیا ہے وہ راہن سے واپس لے لوں تو نہیں لے سکتا کیونکہ غلام نے یہ جنایت مرتہن کے زیر ضمان داخل رہتے ہوئے کی ہے جس کی ذمہ داری مرتہن پر ہوتی ہے لہذا اس نے اپنی ذمہ داری کے ماتحت غلام مرہون کو جنایت سے پاک کر دیا تو یہ ضمان راہن سے نہیں لے سکتا۔
بہر حال یہاں مرتہن کو صرف فدیدینے کا اختیار ہے اگر وہ غلام کو منمان میں دینے لگے تو اس کا اس کو حق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مرتہن غلام کا مالک نہیں ہے جب وہ خود ہی مالک نہیں ہے تو دوسرے کو کیسے مالک بنا سکتا ہے۔
If the mortgaged slave kills a person by mistake, then the guarantee of the crime is upon the mortgagee, and he does not have the right to hand over (the slave) because he does not own the ability to transfer ownership. If he pays the ransom, the pledged property becomes pure, so the debt remains as it was, and he does not recover anything from the mortgagor from the ransom, because the crime occurred in his guarantee, so it was upon him to rectify it. Commentary: When the mortgaged slave kills someone by mistake while in the possession of the mortgagee, the guarantee becomes obligatory on the mortgagee. There is only one form of guarantee here: the mortgagee pays the ransom for the slain. When he pays the ransom, the crime on the mortgaged property is removed, and the mortgagee's debt against the mortgagor remains as before. If the mortgagee wants to recover from the mortgagor what he paid as guarantee, he cannot, because the slave committed the crime while under the mortgagee's guarantee, so the responsibility lies on him. Therefore, he cleansed the mortgaged slave from the crime under his own responsibility, so he cannot recover this guarantee from the mortgagor. In any case, the mortgagee only has the option to pay the ransom; if he tries to hand over the slave, he has no right, because the mortgagee is not the owner. When he himself is not the owner, how can he make another owner?
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for when a mortgaged slave (marhun) commits an accidental killing (qatl khata) while in the possession of the mortgagee (murtahin). The key point is that the mortgagee is liable for the diyah (blood money) because the slave is in his guarantee (daman). However, the mortgagee cannot hand over the slave as compensation because he is not the owner; only the mortgagor (rahin) has ownership. The mortgagee must pay the ransom (fida) himself. After payment, the pledge is purified (the slave is no longer liable for the crime), and the original debt remains unchanged. The mortgagee cannot recover this payment from the mortgagor because the crime happened under the mortgagee's guarantee. The commentary elaborates that the mortgagee's only option is to pay; he cannot unilaterally hand over the slave. This ruling applies to the mortgagee's liability arising from his possession.

Key Terms
مرهون (marhun): The slave or property that is pledged as collateral for a debt.
مرتهن (murtahin): The creditor who holds the pledge as security for the debt.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; here it refers to the mortgagee's responsibility for acts committed by the mortgaged slave while in his possession.
فداء (fida): Ransom or blood money paid to free the slave from liability for homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the mortgagee's obligation when a mortgaged slave accidentally kills someone?
A) Hand over the slave to the victim's heirs
B) Pay the ransom and cannot recover from the mortgagor
C) Force the mortgagor to pay the ransom
D) Keep the slave and do nothing

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee bears liability for accidental killing by a mortgaged slave because possession entails guarantee (daman); he must pay the ransom and cannot recover from the mortgagor.

Mortgagor's Options When Mortgagee Refuses Ransom
Ruling when mortgagee refuses to pay diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mortgagee refuses to pay the ransom for a mortgaged slave's accidental killing and apply the qiyas to destruction to determine the effect on the debt.

Core Idea
Mortgagor chooses to hand over or pay; debt drops because the slave's loss is like destruction in the mortgagee's guarantee.

When a mortgaged slave commits an accidental killing, the mortgagee is expected to pay the ransom (diyah) due to his interest in the property. If he refuses, the law turns to the mortgagor, who remains the owner. This lesson unpacks the two options given to the mortgagor and the reasoning that the debt is cancelled in both cases, grounded in the analogy of the slave becoming like destroyed property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Context
The act is a mortgagor's response to the mortgagee's refusal to pay the ransom for a slave's accidental killing. Recognize that the mortgagee's refusal triggers a new legal duty for the mortgagor.
The mortgagee's right was only to demand ransom; he cannot hand over the slave.
2
State the Two Options
The law gives the mortgagor a choice (takhyir): (1) hand over the slave to the victim's heirs, or (2) pay the ransom himself. Both options are wajib for the mortgagor once the mortgagee refuses.
The mortgagor's ownership of the slave's body (raqaba) remains intact.
3
Consequence of Handing Over the Slave
If the mortgagor hands over the slave, the mortgagee's debt is completely cancelled. The reason is that the slave became due (istihqaq) for a cause that occurred under the mortgagee's guarantee, making it akin to destruction (halak).
The slave is considered like destroyed property because the mortgagor loses the slave due to the mortgagee's failure.
4
Consequence of Paying the Ransom
If the mortgagor pays the ransom, the slave remains with him, but the debt is also cancelled. Here, the slave is considered obtained in exchange for the ransom that was due from the mortgagee, so the value offsets the debt.
The mortgagor effectively acquires the slave free of the debt, but not for nothing—it is a swap.
5
Understand the Qiyas Reasoning
The ruling uses qiyas (analogical reasoning): the slave's loss through istihqaq is equated to physical destruction. The common element (illa) is that in both cases the mortgagor loses the slave without receiving its value, and the mortgagee's right to the slave as security is extinguished.
This reasoning is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may view the debt differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتهن فدیہ دینے سے انکار کر دے تو کیا حکم ہے
ولو أبى المرتهن ان يفدى قيل للراهن ادفع العبد او افده بالدية لان الملك في الرقبة قائم له وانما الى المرتهن الفداء لقيام حقه فاذا امتنع عن الفداء يطالب الراهن بحكم الجناية ومن حكمها التخيير بين الدفع والفداء فان اختار الدفع سقط الدين لانه استحق لمعنى فى ضمان المرتهن فصار کالهلاک و کذالک ان فدى لان العبد كالحاصل له بعوض كان على المرتهن وهو الفداء
ترجمہ اور اگر مرتبین نے فدیہ دینے سے انکار کیا تو راہن سے کہا جائے گا کہ غلام دے دو یا د ی سے اس کا فدیہ دید و اس لئے رقبہ غلام میں راہین کی ملک قائم ہے اور مرتبہن کی جانب فدیہ دینا ہے اس کے حق کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے پس جب کہ مرتہن فدیہ دینے سے رک جائے تو راہن سے حکم جنایت کا مطالبہ کیا جائے گا اور جنایت کا حکم غلام کو دینے اور فدیہ دینے کے درمیان اختیار دینا ہے پس اگر راہن نے غلام دینا اختیار کیا ہو تو مرتہن کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا اس لئے غلام مرہون ایسے سبب (قتل) سے مستحق بنا ہے جو مرتہن کے ضمان میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو یہ (استحقاق ) ہلاکت کے مثل ہو گیا اور ایسے ہی اگر راہن نے فدیہ دیا ہو اس لئے راہن کو غلام ایسے عوض کے بدلہ میں حاصل ہوا ہے جو مر تہن کے اوپر ہے اور وہ عوض فدیہ دینا ہے۔
تشریح اگر مرتین فدیہ ادا نہ کرے تو اب مطالبہ راہن سے ہو گا تو اس کو اختیار ملیں گے۔
- غلام ہی کو مقتول کے ورثاء کے حوالہ کر دے کیونکہ وہ مالک ہے اور یہ حق مرتہن کو اس لئے نہیں ملا تھا کہ وہ مالک نہیں تھا۔ غلام کو اپنے پاس رکھ لے اور اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے بہر حال جو بھی صورت اختیار کر دی گئی ہو بہر صورت مرتین کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں جو ا سے غلام دینا پڑا ہے وہ اس حرکت کی بناء پر دینا پڑا ہے جو اس نے مرتین کے زیر منمان رہتے ہوئے حرکت کی ہے تو یہ ہلاکت کے درجہ میں ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اگر چہ غلام راہن کے پاس ہے مگر مفت میں نہیں بلکہ اس عوض کے بدلہ میں ہے جس عوض کی ادائیگی مرتبین کے ذمہ تھی۔
خلاصہ کلام را ہن کو دو حق ملکیت کی ادائیگی کی وجہ سے ملے ہیں اور مرتبین مالک نہیں بلکہ اس کا مرہون میں حق ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو صرف فدیہ دینے کا حکم ہے نہ کہ غلام دینے کا ۔
And if the mortgagee refuses to pay the ransom, it is said to the mortgagor: Hand over the slave or pay the ransom (diyah) for him, because ownership of the slave's body (raqaba) remains with him, and it is upon the mortgagee to pay the ransom due to his right. So when he refrains from paying the ransom, the mortgagor is addressed by the law of the crime, and its law is the choice between handing over and paying the ransom. If he chooses to hand over, the debt drops because the slave became due (istahaqqa) for a reason that occurred in the mortgagee's guarantee, so it is like destruction. Similarly, if he pays the ransom, because the slave is considered as obtained by him in exchange for what was upon the mortgagee, namely the ransom. Commentary: If the mortgagee does not pay the ransom, then the demand is made to the mortgagor. He will have two choices: hand over the slave to the victim's heirs (because he is the owner) – the mortgagee did not have this right because he was not the owner; or keep the slave and pay his ransom. In either case, the mortgagee's debt is dropped. In the first case, the slave is given away due to his act committed while under the mortgagee's guarantee, so it is akin to destruction. In the second case, although the slave remains with the mortgagor, it is not free; rather, it is in exchange for the ransom that was due from the mortgagee. Summary: The mortgagor has these two rights due to ownership, while the mortgagee is not an owner but has a right over the pledge; hence he is only ordered to pay the ransom, not to hand over the slave.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the mortgagee (murtahin) refuses to pay the diyah for the accidental killing committed by the mortgaged slave. In such a case, the law turns to the mortgagor (rahin). The mortgagor is given two options: (1) hand over the slave to the victim's heirs, or (2) pay the ransom himself. The reasoning is that ownership of the slave remains with the mortgagor; the mortgagee only has a security interest. If the mortgagor hands over the slave, the mortgagee's debt is cancelled because the slave has been taken away (like destruction) due to an action occurring while in the mortgagee's guarantee. If the mortgagor pays the ransom, the slave remains with him, but it is considered as if the slave was acquired by the mortgagor in exchange for the ransom that was due from the mortgagee; thus, the debt is also dropped because the value of the slave offsets the debt. The commentary emphasizes that the mortgagee cannot hand over the slave because he is not the owner; only the mortgagor has that right. The ruling ensures that the victim's heirs receive justice without allowing the mortgagee to escape liability.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): The slave becoming due (to be given) to the victim's heirs due to the crime.
تخيير (takhyir): The opportunity given to the mortgagor to choose between handing over or paying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The debt remains unchanged
B) The debt is reduced by the value of the slave
C) The debt is completely dropped
D) The debt is transferred to the mortgagee

Key Takeaway
When the mortgagee refuses to pay the ransom, the mortgagor must choose to hand over the slave or pay; in either case the debt is cancelled by analogy to destruction.

Liability for Offspring of a Mortgaged Slave
Contrasting ruling: offspring of mortgaged slave not in mortgagee's guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for torts committed by the offspring of a mortgaged slave and explain why the mortgagee is not liable.

Core Idea
The offspring of a mortgaged slave is part of the pledge but not in the mortgagee's guarantee.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from the chapter of Rahn (Mortgage). The question arises: if a slave-girl is mortgaged and she gives birth to a child, who bears liability if that child commits a crime? The Hanafi school provides a clear distinction: while the offspring becomes part of the pledged property, it does not fall under the mortgagee's guarantee (daman). Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly assigning responsibility in such contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The act is a tort (killing or destruction of property) committed by the offspring of a mortgaged slave-girl. The parties are the mortgagor (rahin), mortgagee (murtahin), and the victim or his heirs.
The offspring is considered part of the pledge but is distinct from the mother slave.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on initial liability
The mortgagor is addressed first: he must either hand over the offspring to the victim or pay ransom (fidya). The mortgagee is not initially liable.
The ruling is based on the principle that the offspring is not in the mortgagee's guarantee.
3
Understand the reasoning: offspring not in guarantee
The offspring, though part of the pledge, is not in the mortgagee's guarantee (ghayr mamnoon ala al-murtahin). Hence the mortgagee does not bear responsibility for its torts.
This contrasts with the mother slave, who is in the mortgagee's guarantee.
4
Trace the consequences of the mortgagor's choices
If the mortgagor hands over the offspring, it leaves the pledge and the debt remains unchanged. If he pays ransom, the offspring stays pledged with its mother.
The debt is unaffected because the offspring was not part of the initial guarantee.
5
Contrast with the mother slave's liability
The commentary hints that the mother slave herself is in the mortgagee's guarantee, creating a contrast with the offspring's case.
This contrast reinforces the principle that guarantee does not automatically extend to offspring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہون کا بچہ کسی انسان کو قتل کر دے یا مال ہلاک کر دے تو ضمان کس پر ہو گا
بخلاف ولد الرهن اذا قتل انسانا او استهلک مالا حيث يخاطب الراهن بالدفع والفداء في الابتداء لانه غير مضمون على المرتهن فان دفع خرج من الرهن ولم يسقط شئ من الدين كما لو هلك في الابتداء وان فدى فهو رهن مع امه على حالهما
ترجمہ بخلاف مرہون کے بچہ کے جبکہ اس نے کسی انسان کو قتل کر دیا یا مال ہلاک کر دیا اس حیثیت سے کہ را ہن مخاطب ہوگا بچہ کو دینے یا فدیہ دینے کا پہلے ہی سے اس لئے کہ بچہ مرہون مرتہن پر مضمون نہیں ہے پس اگر راہن نے بچہ دیدیا ( صاحب حق کو ) تو وہ رہن سے خارج ہو گیا اور قرض میں سے کچھ مساقط نہ ہو گا جیسا کہ اگر ابتداء ہی میں ہلاک ہو جاتا اور اگر فدیہ دیا ہوتو وہ بچہ اپنی ماں کے ساتھ پہلے کی طرح رہن ہوگا۔
تشریح راہن نے ایک باندی رہن رکھی جو کسی کی بیوی بھی ہے اور حاملہ ہے مرتہن کے پاس اس نے بچہ دیا۔ بچہ کچھ دنوں کا ہوا کہ وہ پر سے گر گیا جس کی وجہ سے کوئی آدمی مر گیا اور بچہ ٹھیک ٹھاک رہا تو ضمان کس پر ہو گا ؟
تو فرمایا کہ اب ضمان مرتبین پر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کا بچہ اگر چہ مرتبہن کے پاس رہن تو ہوتا ہے لیکن وہ مضمون
Contrary to the offspring of the mortgaged (slave) when he kills a person or destroys property, for the mortgagor is addressed with handing over or paying the ransom in the beginning, because the offspring is not in the guarantee of the mortgagee. If he hands over, it leaves the pledge and nothing drops from the debt, as if it perished in the beginning. And if he pays the ransom, then it remains as a pledge with its mother in their original state. Commentary: The mortgagor pawned a slave-girl who is someone's wife and pregnant; she gave birth to a child at the mortgagee's. The child grew a few days and then fell from a height, causing a person to die, while the child remained unharmed. So on whom is the guarantee? It is said that the guarantee is not on the mortgagee, because it has passed before that the offspring of the mortgaged (slave) is considered a pledge with the mortgagee, but it is not in his guarantee (mamnoon).
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage distinguishes the case of the offspring (walad) of a mortgaged female slave. While the offspring itself becomes part of the pledge (marhun) when born, it is not in the guarantee (daman) of the mortgagee. Therefore, if the offspring kills someone or destroys property, the mortgagee is not initially liable. Instead, the mortgagor (rahin) is addressed directly. The mortgagor has two options: hand over the offspring to the victim's heirs, or pay the ransom. If he hands over, the offspring leaves the pledge and the original debt remains unchanged (like the offspring perished from the beginning). If he pays the ransom, the offspring remains a pledge along with its mother as before. The commentary gives an example of a slave-girl pawning; her offspring falls and kills someone. The ruling is that the mortgagee is not liable because the offspring, though part of the pledge, is not guaranteed by the mortgagee (i.e., the mortgagee does not bear responsibility for its actions). This contrasts with the earlier case of the mother slave herself, where the mortgagee is liable.

Key Terms
ولد الرهن (walad al-rahn): The offspring born to a mortgaged female slave during the period of the pledge.
مضمون (mamnoon): Guaranteed; here, the offspring is not in the mortgagee's guarantee of liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
The offspring of a mortgaged slave is a part of the pledge but not in the mortgagee's guarantee, so the mortgagor bears initial liability for its torts.

Mortgaged Slave Commits Murder: Effect on the Pledge and Debt
States ruling on mortgaged slave murder and effect on debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mortgaged slave commits murder and the mortgagee refuses to pay the ransom, and explain why the mortgage debt is extinguished in both scenarios.

Core Idea
If the mortgagee refuses ransom, the mortgagor must choose: hand over the slave or pay ransom—both wipe out the mortgage debt.

In Hanafi law, a mortgage (rahn) gives the mortgagee a right to hold the pledge but not ownership. When a mortgaged slave commits murder, the mortgagee is first asked to pay the ransom (fidyah) because the slave is in his custody. If he refuses, the responsibility shifts to the mortgagor, who is the true owner. This lesson explains the mortgagor's options and the legal consequence for the mortgage debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and trigger
The ruling involves a mortgagor (rahin) and a mortgagee (murtahin). The trigger is the mortgagee's refusal to pay the fidyah for the slave's murder.
The fidyah is a ransom paid to the victim's heirs to free the slave from execution.
2
Recognize the mortgagee's obligation
Initially, the mortgagee is commanded to pay the fidyah because the slave is under his guarantee (daman). If he pays, the debt remains.
3
Consequence of mortgagee's refusal
When the mortgagee refuses, the obligation transfers to the mortgagor. He is given a choice: hand over the slave to the victim's heirs or pay the fidyah himself.
4
Analyze the extinguishment of debt
In both cases the mortgage debt is completely cancelled. If the slave is surrendered, it is treated as destruction (halak) because the liability arose under the mortgagee's guarantee. If the mortgagor pays, he redeems the slave with an amount that was the mortgagee's responsibility.
The debt falls entirely; it is not merely reduced.
5
Reason from ownership and guarantee
The mortgagor is the owner, so he can dispose of the slave. The mortgagee only has a possessory right, not ownership, hence he cannot be forced to surrender the slave; only to pay the fidyah if he wishes to keep the pledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور اگر مرتبین نے فدیہ دینے سے انکار کیا تو راہن سے کہا جائے گا کہ غلام دے دو یا د ی سے اس کا فدیہ دید و اس لئے رقبہ غلام میں راہین کی ملک قائم ہے اور مرتبہن کی جانب فدیہ دینا ہے اس کے حق کے قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے پس جب کہ مرتہن فدیہ دینے سے رک جائے تو راہن سے حکم جنایت کا مطالبہ کیا جائے گا اور جنایت کا حکم غلام کو دینے اور فدیہ دینے کے درمیان اختیار دینا ہے پس اگر راہن نے غلام دینا اختیار کیا ہو تو مرتہن کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا اس لئے غلام مرہون ایسے سبب (قتل) سے مستحق بنا ہے جو مرتہن کے ضمان میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو یہ (استحقاق ) ہلاکت کے مثل ہو گیا اور ایسے ہی اگر راہن نے فدیہ دیا ہو اس لئے راہن کو غلام ایسے عوض کے بدلہ میں حاصل ہوا ہے جو مر تہن کے اوپر ہے اور وہ عوض فدیہ دینا ہے۔
تشریح اگر مرتین فدیہ ادا نہ کرے تو اب مطالبہ راہن سے ہو گا تو اس کو اختیار ملیں گے۔
- غلام ہی کو مقتول کے ورثاء کے حوالہ کر دے کیونکہ وہ مالک ہے اور یہ حق مرتہن کو اس لئے نہیں ملا تھا کہ وہ مالک نہیں تھا۔ غلام کو اپنے پاس رکھ لے اور اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے بہر حال جو بھی صورت اختیار کر دی گئی ہو بہر صورت مرتین کا قرض ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں جو ا سے غلام دینا پڑا ہے وہ اس حرکت کی بناء پر دینا پڑا ہے جو اس نے مرتین کے زیر منمان رہتے ہوئے حرکت کی ہے تو یہ ہلاکت کے درجہ میں ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اگر چہ غلام راہن کے پاس ہے مگر مفت میں نہیں بلکہ اس عوض کے بدلہ میں ہے جس عوض کی ادائیگی مرتبین کے ذمہ تھی۔
خلاصہ کلام را ہن کو دو حق ملکیت کی ادائیگی کی وجہ سے ملے ہیں اور مرتبین مالک نہیں بلکہ اس کا مرہون میں حق ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو صرف فدیہ دینے کا حکم ہے نہ کہ غلام دینے کا ۔
Translation: And if the mortgagee refuses to pay the ransom, then the mortgagor will be told: give the slave or pay his ransom. Because the ownership of the slave's remains with the mortgagor, and on the mortgagee's side is to pay the ransom due to his right being established. So when the mortgagee refrains from paying, the mortgagor will be addressed with the ruling of the crime. And the ruling of the crime is to give him an option between handing over the slave and paying the ransom. So if the mortgagor chooses to hand over the slave, the mortgagee's debt falls, because the mortgaged slave became due (liable) due to a cause (murder) that occurred while under the mortgagee's guarantee, so this (liability) is like destruction. And similarly, if the mortgagor pays the ransom, because the mortgagor obtained the slave in exchange for a consideration that was upon the mortgagee, and that consideration is to pay the ransom.
Explanation: If the mortgagee does not pay the ransom, then the claim will be against the mortgagor, and he will have options:
- Hand over the slave to the victim's heirs, because he is the owner, and this right was not given to the mortgagee because he was not the owner.
- Keep the slave and pay his ransom.
In any case, whichever option is chosen, the mortgagee's debt falls. Because in the first case, the slave had to be given due to an act that occurred while under the mortgagee's custody, so it is in the category of destruction. In the second case, although the slave remains with the mortgagor, it is not free but in exchange for the consideration which was due from the mortgagee.
Conclusion: The mortgagor has two rights due to ownership, and the mortgagee is not the owner but has a right in the pledge, so he is only commanded to pay the ransom, not to hand over the slave.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling when a mortgaged slave commits murder. The mortgagee is first asked to pay the ransom (fidyah) because the slave is in his custody. If he refuses, the mortgagor is given the option to either hand over the slave to the victim's heirs or pay the ransom himself. In either case, the mortgagee's debt is completely extinguished. The reasoning is that the slave's value was under the mortgagee's guarantee (daman) while in his possession; the slave becoming subject to execution due to the crime is considered like destruction (halak), which cancels the debt. If the mortgagor pays the ransom, it is considered as if he redeemed the slave with an amount that was the mortgagee's responsibility, so the debt falls. This ruling emphasizes that the mortgagee has only a right to hold the pledge, not ownership, so he cannot be forced to hand over the slave; his obligation is limited to paying the ransom if he chooses to keep the slave.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract where property is given as security for a debt.
راهن (rahin): The debtor who gives the pledge.
مرتهن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pledge.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom paid to free a slave from liability for a crime.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; liability for loss or damage while in one's custody.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what happens to the mortgage debt if the mortgagor chooses to hand over the slave to the victim's heirs after the mortgagee refuses to pay the fidyah?
A) The debt is reduced by the value of the slave.
B) The debt is completely extinguished.
C) The debt remains and the mortgagor must also pay the fidyah.
D) The debt is transferred to the victim's heirs.

Key Takeaway
When a mortgaged slave commits murder and the mortgagee refuses to pay the ransom, the mortgagor can surrender the slave or pay the ransom, and in both cases the mortgage debt is fully cancelled.

Offspring of Mortgaged Property Committing Crime
States ruling when offspring of mortgaged property kills or destroys property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the offspring of a mortgaged female slave commits a crime and explain why the mortgagee is not liable.

Core Idea
Offspring of a pledged slave is not under the mortgagee's guarantee; only the mortgagor is initially liable.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario within the chapter of rahn (pledge): what happens when the offspring of a mortgaged female slave causes harm? The passage you are about to read clarifies that the offspring is legally distinct from the original slave in terms of guarantee. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assigning liability in pledge-related crimes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject
First, recognize that the ruling concerns the offspring (walad) of a mortgaged female slave (um al-walad or regular slave). The offspring is itself part of the pledge but not automatically guaranteed by the mortgagee.
The offspring is considered a separate entity in terms of guarantee.
2
Contrast with the Original Slave
Compare this to the ruling for the original mortgaged slave: in that case, the mortgagee is first addressed regarding compensation, and only if he refuses does the option shift to the mortgagor. Here, the mortgagee is never addressed because the offspring is not under his guarantee.
This contrast is explicitly given in the preceding text (not quoted here).
3
Determine the Mortgagor's Options
The mortgagor has two options: (1) hand over the offspring to the victim (or heirs), which removes it from the pledge but does not reduce the debt; or (2) pay ransom (fidya), in which case the offspring remains as a pledge with its mother until the debt is paid.
Both options preserve the debt in full.
4
Apply the Principle to Other Acts
The same ruling applies if the offspring destroys property instead of killing a person. The mortgagor is still initially addressed because the offspring is not mḍmūn (guaranteed) by the mortgagee.
The text explicitly mentions killing a person or destroying property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف ولد الرهن اذا قتل انسانا او استهلک مالا حيث يخاطب الراهن بالدفع والفداء في الابتداء لانه غير مضمون على المرتهن فان دفع خرج من الرهن ولم يسقط شئ من الدين كما لو هلك في الابتداء وان فدى فهو رهن مع امه على حالهما
ترجمہ بخلاف مرہون کے بچہ کے جبکہ اس نے کسی انسان کو قتل کر دیا یا مال ہلاک کر دیا اس حیثیت سے کہ را ہن مخاطب ہوگا بچہ کو دینے یا فدیہ دینے کا پہلے ہی سے اس لئے کہ بچہ مرہون مرتہن پر مضمون نہیں ہے پس اگر راہن نے بچہ دیدیا ( صاحب حق کو ) تو وہ رہن سے خارج ہو گیا اور قرض میں سے کچھ مساقط نہ ہو گا جیسا کہ اگر ابتداء ہی میں ہلاک ہو جاتا اور اگر فدیہ دیا ہوتو وہ بچہ اپنی ماں کے ساتھ پہلے کی طرح رہن ہوگا۔
تشریح راہن نے ایک باندی رہن رکھی جو کسی کی بیوی بھی ہے اور حاملہ ہے مرتہن کے پاس اس نے بچہ دیا۔ بچہ کچھ دنوں کا ہوا کہ وہ پر سے گر گیا جس کی وجہ سے کوئی آدمی مر گیا اور بچہ ٹھیک ٹھاک رہا تو ضمان کس پر ہو گا ؟
تو فرمایا کہ اب ضمان مرتبین پر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کا بچہ اگر چہ مرتبہن کے پاس رہن تو ہوتا ہے لیکن وہ مضمون نہیں ہوتا لہذا مرتہن پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔
بلکہ ضمان صرف راہن پر ہوگا اور راہن کو اختیار ہوگا کہ چاہے تو وہی بچہ مقتول کے ور تلہ کو دیدے اور چاہے تو اس کا فدیہ دیدے جو بھی صورت اختیار کرے گا مرتہن کا قرض بدستور رہے گا اور اگر اس نے فدیہ دیا ہو تو قرض تو باقی رہے گا ہی یہ بچہ بھی اداء دین تک اپنی ماں کے ساتھ مرہون رہے گا۔
عبارت: Unlike the offspring of the pledge when it kills a person or destroys property, where the mortgagor is initially addressed to hand over or pay ransom, because the offspring is not under the mortgagee's guarantee. So if the mortgagor hands over (to the claimant), it exits the pledge and nothing of the debt falls, just as if it had perished initially. And if he pays ransom, it remains as a pledge with its mother as before.
Translation: Unlike the offspring of the pledged property when it has killed a person or destroyed property, in that the mortgagor will be addressed to hand over the offspring or pay ransom from the beginning, because the pledged offspring is not under the mortgagee's guarantee. So if the mortgagor hands over the offspring (to the right-holder), it exits from the pledge and nothing of the debt is dropped, as if it had perished initially. And if he pays ransom, that offspring with its mother remains as pledge as before.
Explanation: A mortgagor mortgaged a female slave who is also someone's wife and is pregnant. She gave birth to a child at the mortgagee's house. The child grew a few days old, then fell from a height causing a person to die, while the child remained safe. Then whose liability is it? He said: Now liability will not be on the mortgagee because it has passed before that the child of the pledge, although it is with the mortgagee as a pledge, is not under guarantee, so liability will not be on the mortgagee. Rather, liability will be solely on the mortgagor, and the mortgagor will have the option: either to hand over that child to the victim's heirs or to pay its ransom. Whichever option he chooses, the mortgagee's debt will remain as it is. And if he pays ransom, the debt remains, and the child remains as a pledge with its mother until the debt is paid.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage contrasts the ruling for the offspring of a mortgaged property with that for the original mortgaged slave. The key difference is that the offspring is not considered under the mortgagee's guarantee (damān). Therefore, when the offspring commits a crime (murder or property destruction), the mortgagor is directly addressed from the start, not the mortgagee. If the mortgagor hands over the offspring, it merely leaves the pledge with no effect on the debt; if he pays ransom, the offspring remains as part of the pledge with its mother. In contrast, for the original slave, the mortgagee is first approached, and his refusal leads to the mortgagor's option that extinguishes the debt. This distinction highlights that the mortgagee's guarantee applies only to the original pledged property, not to its subsequent offspring.

Key Terms
ولد الرهن (walad al-rahn): Offspring born to a pledged female slave during the period of pledge.
مضمون (mamun): Under guarantee; the mortgagee is liable for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the offspring of a mortgaged female slave commits a crime, who is initially addressed regarding handing over or ransom?
A) The mortgagee
B) The mortgagor
C) Both jointly
D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
The offspring of a mortgaged slave is not under the mortgagee's guarantee; the mortgagor directly bears liability and has the option to hand over the offspring or pay ransom without affecting the debt.

Ruling on a Mortgaged Slave Destroying Property of Full Value
States ruling when mortgaged slave destroys property worth whole value or more

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mortgaged slave destroys property worth his entire value and apply the rule that the slave's debt takes precedence over the mortgagee's debt.

Core Idea
A slave's debt from destroying property is paid before the mortgagee's claim, even if the slave is collateral.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a specific but important scenario in the chapter of mortgage (rahn): what happens when a mortgaged slave destroys property that is worth his full value or more? The ruling establishes a hierarchy of claims that gives priority to the slave's personal liability over the mortgagee's security interest. Understanding this priority is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi rules on debt and collateral.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Initial Options
The passage addresses a mortgaged slave who destroys property worth an amount that 'engulfs his entire value' (yastaghriq raqabatahu). The mortgagee has two choices: pay the slave's debt himself or refuse to pay.
The slave's value here means the price he would fetch in the market.
2
Consequences of Mortgagee Paying the Slave's Debt
If the mortgagee voluntarily pays the debt owed by the slave (to the property owner), his own mortgage debt against the mortgagor remains intact. This is analogous to the ransom (fida) case where paying preserves the original obligation.
The mortgagee's debt is unaffected because he has discharged the slave's liability out of choice.
3
Consequences of Mortgagee Refusing to Pay
If the mortgagee refuses, the mortgagor is asked to either pay the slave's debt himself or sell the slave. If the mortgagor pays, the mortgagee's debt is voided. If the slave is sold, the proceeds go to the property owner (the slave's creditor), not to the mortgagee.
The mortgagee's debt falls because the slave's liability has consumed the collateral's value.
4
Prioritize Claims When Slave is Sold
The key principle: 'Dain al-‘abd muqaddamun ‘ala dain al-murtahin' – the slave's debt takes precedence over the mortgagee's debt. This applies even if a crime victim's guardian also has a claim.
The slave's debt is a personal liability attaching to his person, while the mortgagee's claim is on the value.
5
Generalize the Rule
The same priority holds if the slave commits a crime (e.g., homicide). The slave's debt from the crime is prioritized over any claim of the mortgagee or the victim's guardian. The slave must be sold and the proceeds go first to the slave's creditor.
This reflects the Hanafi view that the slave's own obligations attach to his physical existence, independent of his master's debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استهلك العبد المرهون مالا يستغرق رقبته فان ادى المرتهن الدين الذى لزم العبد فدينه على حاله كما في الفداء وان ابى قيل للراهن بعه في الدين الا ان يختار ان يؤدى عنه فان ادى بطل دين المرتهن كما ذكرنا فى الفداء وان لم يود وبيع العبد فيه ياخذ صاحب دين العبد دينه لان دين العبد مقدم على دين المرتهن وحق ولى الجناية لتقدمه على حق المولى
ترجمہ اور اگر مرہون غلام نے اتنا مال ہلاک کر دیا کہ اس کی گردن کو گھیرے ہوئے ہو پس اگر مرتہن نے وہ قرض ادا کر دیا جو غلام پر لازم ہوا ہے تو مرتین کا قرض اپنے حال پر ہے ( باقی ہے ) جیسے فدیہ دینے میں اگر وہ انکار کر دے تو راہن سے کہا جائے گا کہ مرہون کو قرض میں بیچ دے مگر یہ کہ راہن اس کی جانب سے فدیہ ادا کرنا اختیار کرے پس اگر راہن نے فدیہ ادا کر دیا تو مرتین کا قرض باطل ہو گیا جیسے ہم اس کو فدیہ دینے میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر راہن نے ادا نہیں کیا اور راس میں غلام بھیج دیا گیا تو غلام پر قرض لے لے اس لئے غلام کا قرض مرتہن کے قرض اور ولی جنایت کے حق پر مقدم ہے اس کے (دین عبد کے ) مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے مولیٰ کے حق پر ۔
تشریح مرہون غلام نے بجائے کسی کو قتل کرنے کے کسی کا مال ضائع کر دیا اور اتنا مال ہلاک کیا جو غلام مرہون کی قیمت سے کم نہیں ہے بلکہ برابر یا زیادہ ہے تو یوں سمجھیں گے کہ جس کا مال ہلاک کیا ہے اس کا اتنا ہی قرض غلام کے ذمہ ہے تو اگر اس قرض کو مرتہن نے ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہے اور مرتین کا قرض علی حالہ باقی رہے گا اور اگر مرتہن نے قرض دینے سے انکار کر دیا تو اب راہن سے مطالبہ ہو گا تو اگر وہ چاہے تو قرض ادا کر دے ورنہ اس کو حکم ہوگا کہ اس غلام کو فروخت کیا جائے اور دونوں صورتوں میں مرتہن کا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ بہر حال جب اس کو بیچ دیا گیا ہو تو اس کے شمن سے وہ شخص جس کا غلام پر قرض شمار کیا گیا ہے. سے اپنا ثمن وصول کرے۔ سوال اس میں سے کچھ مرتہن کو بھی تو ملنا چاہیئے ؟ جواب نہیں کیونکہ یہ غلام پر ذاتی قرض ہے اور مرتبہن کا قرض راہن پر ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو قرض غلام پر ہوتا ہے وہ مرتبین کے قرض سے مقدم ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اگر غلام مرہون نے کوئی اور بھی جنایت کی ہو تو اس کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے گالیکن پھر اس کو حکم ہو گا کہ اس کو فروخت کرو اور صاحب دین کا قرض ادا کرو اس میں بھی صاحب دین کا حق ولی جنایت کے حق سے مقدم رکھا گیا ہے۔
عبارت: And if the mortgaged slave destroys property that engulfs his entire value, then if the mortgagee pays the debt that became due on the slave, his debt remains as it is, as in the case of ransom. If he refuses, the mortgagor is told to sell the slave for the debt unless he chooses to pay on its behalf. If he pays, the mortgagee's debt is voided as mentioned in the case of ransom. If he does not pay and the slave is sold, the owner of the slave's debt takes his debt, because the slave's debt takes precedence over the mortgagee's debt and the right of the victim's guardian due to its precedence over the rights of the master.
Translation: And if the mortgaged slave destroys property that engulfs his entire value, then if the mortgagee pays the debt that became due on the slave, his debt remains, as in the ransom case. If he refuses, the mortgagor is told to sell the slave for the debt, unless he chooses to pay ransom on its behalf. If he pays, the mortgagee's debt becomes void as we mentioned in the ransom case. If he does not pay and the slave is sold, the owner of the slave's debt takes his debt, because the slave's debt is prioritized over the mortgagee's debt and the right of the victim's guardian due to its precedence over the rights of the master.
Explanation: Instead of killing someone, the mortgaged slave destroyed someone's property to an extent not less than his own value, either equal or more. So understand that the person whose property was destroyed has a claim of that amount against the slave. If the mortgagee pays that claim, it is permissible and the mortgagee's debt remains as before. If the mortgagee refuses to pay, then the mortgagor is called upon. If he wishes, he can pay the claim; otherwise, he is ordered to sell the slave. In both cases, the mortgagee's debt falls. When the slave is sold, the proceeds are given to the person who had a claim on the slave. Question: Shouldn't the mortgagee get something from that? Answer: No, because this is a personal debt of the slave, and the mortgagee's debt is against the mortgagor. The rule is that the debt owed by the slave takes precedence over the mortgagee's debt. Similarly, if the mortgaged slave commits any other crime, he is handed over to the guardian of the crime, but then he is ordered to sell the slave and pay the claim owner, and in this also the claim owner's right is prioritized over the guardian's right.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where the mortgaged slave destroys property worth the entirety or more of his value. The rule distinguishes between the slave's own debt (owed to the property owner) and the mortgagee's debt (owed by the mortgagor). The mortgagee has the option to pay the slave's debt and keep his own debt intact. If he refuses, the mortgagor pays or the slave is sold. The proceeds go entirely to the property owner (the slave's creditor) because the slave's debt is given precedence over the mortgagee's debt. This is based on the principle that the slave's liability attaches to his person and takes priority over the mortgagee's right of retention. The passage emphasizes that the slave's debt is a personal liability ('dayn dhimmah) that must be satisfied first before any claim of the mortgagee or even a crime victim's guardian.

Key Terms
استهلاك (istihlak): Destruction of property, incurring liability for the value.
يستغرق رقبته (yastaghriq raqabatahu): Engulfs his entire value; the claim equals or exceeds the slave's price.
دين العبد (dayn al-'abd): Debt incurred by the slave due to acts like destroying property.
حق المولى (haqq al-mawla): The master's right over the slave (including mortgagee's right).
المقدم (al-muqaddam): That which takes precedence; the slave's debt is muqaddam over the mortgagee's debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are divided equally between the mortgagee and the property owner.
B) They go entirely to the mortgagee to satisfy his debt.
C) They go entirely to the property owner (the slave's creditor).
D) They go to the victim's guardian.

Key Takeaway
The slave's debt arising from destroying property is a personal liability that takes precedence over the mortgagee's security interest, even if the slave is the subject of the mortgage.
