Mortgaged Slave Destroys Property of Equal or Greater Value
Ruling on options when mortgaged slave's destruction of property consumes his entire value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to the mortgagee and rahin when a mortgaged slave destroys property worth his entire value, and explain the priority of the slave's debt over the mortgagee's claim.

Core Idea
The slave's personal debt takes priority over the mortgagee's right, potentially voiding the mortgage.

This lesson explores a specific scenario in Hanafi mortgage law: a mortgaged slave destroys property owned by a third party, and the value of the destroyed property equals or exceeds the slave's own price. The passage outlines the legal options for both the mortgagee (creditor) and the rahin (debtor/owner of the slave), and establishes a key principle about the priority of debts attached to the slave's person. Understanding this ruling illuminates how Hanafi fiqh balances competing claims on a single asset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize that the case involves a mortgaged slave who destroys property (not through killing) with a value equal to or greater than the slave's own price. This triggers a personal debt on the slave (dīn al-‘abd) that attaches to his raqabah (person).
The condition 'equal or greater value' distinguishes this from cases of lesser destruction.
2
Understand the Mortgagee's Option
The mortgagee (murtahin) may choose to pay the slave's debt himself. If he does so, his own mortgage debt remains intact. This is analogized to fidā’ (ransom) where paying a captive's ransom preserves the captor's rights.
The mortgagee's payment is voluntary, not obligatory.
3
Examine the Rahin's Option
If the mortgagee refuses to pay, the rahin is given a choice: either pay the slave's debt (which invalidates the mortgagee's debt entirely) or consent to selling the slave to satisfy the slave's debt.
If the rahin pays, the mortgagee's claim on the slave's raqabah is extinguished.
4
Analyze the Priority of Debts
If the slave is sold, the proceeds go entirely to the slave's personal creditor (the one whose property was destroyed), not to the mortgagee. This is because the slave's debt (dīn al-‘abd) is prior to the mortgagee's debt and even to the master's (mawlā) rights.
The rule: 'dīn al-‘abd muqaddam 'alā dīn al-murtahin' – the slave's debt precedes the mortgagee's debt.
5
Apply the Analogy of Ransom
The ruling is grounded in analogy (qiyās) to the case of a captive (fidā’): paying a ransom frees the captive and extinguishes previous claims. Similarly, paying the slave's debt frees the slave from that liability and affects the mortgagee's rights accordingly.
This analogy shows the internal consistency of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اگر مرہون غلام نے اتنا مال ہلاک کر دیا کہ اس کی گردن کو گھیرے ہوئے ہو پس اگر مرتہن نے وہ قرض ادا کر دیا جو غلام پر لازم ہوا ہے تو مرتین کا قرض اپنے حال پر ہے ( باقی ہے ) جیسے فدیہ دینے میں اگر وہ انکار کر دے تو راہن سے کہا جائے گا کہ مرہون کو قرض میں بیچ دے مگر یہ کہ راہن اس کی جانب سے فدیہ ادا کرنا اختیار کرے پس اگر راہن نے فدیہ ادا کر دیا تو مرتین کا قرض باطل ہو گیا جیسے ہم اس کو فدیہ دینے میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر راہن نے ادا نہیں کیا اور راس میں غلام بھیج دیا گیا تو غلام پر قرض لے لے اس لئے غلام کا قرض مرتہن کے قرض اور ولی جنایت کے حق پر مقدم ہے اس کے (دین عبد کے ) مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے مولیٰ کے حق پر ۔
تشریح مرہون غلام نے بجائے کسی کو قتل کرنے کے کسی کا مال ضائع کر دیا اور اتنا مال ہلاک کیا جو غلام مرہون کی قیمت سے کم نہیں ہے بلکہ برابر یا زیادہ ہے تو یوں سمجھیں گے کہ جس کا مال ہلاک کیا ہے اس کا اتنا ہی قرض غلام کے ذمہ ہے تو اگر اس قرض کو مرتہن نے ادا کر دیا تو جائز ہے اور مرتین کا قرض علی حالہ باقی رہے گا اور اگر مرتہن نے قرض دینے سے انکار کر دیا تو اب راہن سے مطالبہ ہو گا تو اگر وہ چاہے تو قرض ادا کر دے ورنہ اس کو حکم ہوگا کہ اس غلام کو فروخت کیا جائے اور دونوں صورتوں میں مرتہن کا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ بہر حال جب اس کو بیچ دیا گیا ہو تو اس کے شمن سے وہ شخص جس کا غلام پر قرض شمار کیا گیا ہے. سے اپنا ثمن وصول کرے۔ سوال اس میں سے کچھ مرتہن کو بھی تو ملنا چاہیئے ؟ جواب نہیں کیونکہ یہ غلام پر ذاتی قرض ہے اور مرتبہن کا قرض راہن پر ہے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو قرض غلام پر ہوتا ہے وہ مرتبین کے قرض سے مقدم ہوتا ہے اسی طرح اگر غلام مرہون نے کوئی اور بھی جنایت کی ہو تو اس کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے گالیکن پھر اس کو حکم ہو گا کہ اس کو فروخت کرو اور صاحب دین کا قرض ادا کرو اس میں بھی صاحب دین کا حق ولی جنایت کے حق سے مقدم رکھا گیا ہے۔
وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ صاحب دین کا حق مولی کے حق سے بھی مقدم ہے تو مرتہن اور وبی جنایت کے حق سے بدرجہ اولیٰ صاحب دین کا حق مقدم ہوگا۔
And if the mortgaged slave destroys property that does not consume his entire value: if the mortgagee pays the debt that became incumbent on the slave, then his debt remains as it was, as in the case of ransom. And if he refuses, the rahin is told to sell him for the debt, unless he chooses to pay on his behalf. If he pays, the mortgagee's debt is invalidated, as we mentioned in the chapter of ransom. And if he does not pay, and the slave is sold, the creditor of the slave takes his debt because the slave's debt has priority over the mortgagee's debt and over the right of the guardian of the injury, due to its priority over the right of the master. Translation: And if the mortgaged slave has destroyed property that envelopes his neck, then if the mortgagee pays the debt that became incumbent on the slave, his debt remains as it was, like in paying ransom. If he refuses, the rahin is told to sell the mortgagee in the debt unless the rahin chooses to pay on his behalf. If the rahin pays, the mortgagee's debt is invalidated as we explained in ransom. If he does not pay and the slave is sold, the creditor of the slave takes his debt because the slave's debt is prior to the mortgagee's debt and the right of the guardian of the injury, due to its priority over the master's right. Commentary: The mortgaged slave destroyed someone's property instead of killing, and he destroyed property that is not less than his price, rather equal or more. So understand that the one whose property was destroyed has a debt equal to that on the slave. If the mortgagee pays this debt, it is permissible and the mortgagee's debt remains. If the mortgagee refuses to pay, then the rahin is called upon. If he wishes, he pays the debt, otherwise he is ordered to sell the slave. In both cases, the mortgagee's debt falls. In any case, when the slave is sold, the person whose debt is on the slave receives his price from the proceeds. Question: Shouldn't the mortgagee also get something from this? Answer: No, because this is a personal debt of the slave, and the mortgagee's debt is on the rahin. The rule is that the debt that is on the slave takes priority over the debt of the mortgagee. Similarly, if the slave committed any other injury, he is handed over to the guardian of the injury, but then he is ordered to sell him and pay the creditor's debt. In this, the right of the creditor is also given priority over the right of the guardian of the injury. Reason: The right of the creditor is even prior to the right of the master, so it is even more prior over the rights of the mortgagee and the guardian of the injury.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a specific scenario in the chapter of mortgage (al-rahn): a mortgaged slave destroys property (not through killing) and the value of the destroyed property is equal to or greater than the slave's own price. The ruling, as explained by the commentator, provides multiple options. The core principle is that the slave's personal debt (dīn al-‘abd) incurred by the destruction takes priority over both the mortgagee's debt (dīn al-murtahin) and the rights of an injury guardian (walī al-jināyah). This priority is because the slave's debt is attached to his person (raqabah) and precedes even the master's (mawlā) rights. The passage details the sequence: If the mortgagee pays the slave's debt on his own, the mortgagee's own debt remains intact. If the mortgagee refuses, the rahin is given the option to either pay the slave's debt (in which case the mortgagee's debt becomes void) or sell the slave. If sold, the proceeds go entirely to the slave's creditor, not to the mortgagee, because the slave's debt is prior. The same priority applies if the slave committed a criminal injury (jināyah) – the creditor's right over the slave's value precedes the guardian's right. This ruling is based on legal reasoning (ta‘līl) that the slave's debt is like a prior lien on his person.

Key Terms
العبد المرهون (al-‘abd al-marhūn): A slave that has been given as collateral for a debt.
دين العبد (dīn al-‘abd): The debt incurred by the slave due to destroying someone's property; it attaches to his person.
رقبة (raqabah): The slave's physical person, which is the subject of both the mortgage and the personal debt.
فداء (fidā’): Ransom payment; here it refers to the mortgagee or rahin paying the slave's debt to free him or preserve rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The mortgagee's debt becomes void and the sale proceeds go entirely to the slave's creditor.
C) The mortgagee's debt is reduced by the amount the slave's creditor receives.
D) The mortgagee's debt is transferred to the rahin and must be paid immediately.

Key Takeaway
The slave's personal debt from destroying property takes priority over the mortgagee's claim on the slave, and either party may pay to affect their rights.

Leftover Sale Price and When Slave's Debt Is Less
Ruling on distribution of sale proceeds and effect on mortgagee's debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for distributing sale proceeds of a mortgaged slave and determine when the mortgagee's debt is reduced or voided.

Core Idea
A mortgaged slave's personal debt can void or reduce the mortgagee's debt by analogy to destruction.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario in mortgage (rahn) law: when a mortgaged slave incurs a personal debt (e.g., for property destruction), and the slave is sold. How should the sale proceeds be distributed, and how does the slave's debt affect the mortgagee's claim? The Hanafi ruling applies the principle that the slave's person (raqabah) becomes legally entitled to the creditor, analogous to physical destruction, which extinguishes or reduces the mortgage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and debts
Recognize the three parties: the rahin (owner/mortgagor), the murtahin (mortgagee), and the slave's personal creditor. Note the amounts of each debt.
The slave's debt is for property destruction (dīn istihlāk).
2
Compare the slave's debt to the mortgagee's debt
Determine whether the slave's debt is equal to, greater than, or less than the mortgagee's debt.
3
Apply the ruling for equality or excess
If the slave's debt equals or exceeds the mortgagee's debt, the mortgagee's entire debt becomes void, and any surplus from the sale goes to the rahin.
The justification is qiyas: the slave's person is entirely unavailable to the mortgagee, like destruction.
4
Apply the ruling for lesser slave debt
If the slave's debt is less than the mortgagee's debt, the mortgagee's debt is reduced by the amount of the slave's debt, and the slave remains as mortgage for the remaining balance. If the mortgagee's debt has matured, he can take the slave; otherwise, he holds it until maturity.
If the sale price does not cover the slave's debt, the creditor takes the price and the balance is postponed until emancipation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح اس غلام کو بیچنے میں جو شمن ملا ہے اگر صاحب دین کا قرض ادا کر کے کچھ بچ جائے اور اتفاق تحریم اور مرتہن کا قرض برابر ہیں یا عزیم کا زیادہ ہے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں عزیم کا قرض ادا کر کے جو بچ جائے تو وہ راہن کا امور مرتہن کا قرض باطل ہو چکا ہے ، وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ مرتہن کے زیر ضمان پورا غلام دوسرے کا مستحق ہو چکا تھا۔ اور یہ استحقاق ہلاکت کے درجہ میں ہے تو جیسے بصورت ہلاکت قرض ساقط ہو جاتا ہے یہاں بھی ساقط ہو جائیگا۔ غلام کا قرض مرتہن کے قرض سے کم ہو تو مرتہن کا قرض غلام کے قرض کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گا
وان كان دين العبد اقل سقط من دين المرتهن بقدر دين العبد وما فضل من دين العبد يبقى رهنا كما كان ثم ان كان دين المرتهن قد حل اخذه به لانه من جنس حقه وان كان لم يحل امسكه حتى يحل وان كان ثمن العبد لا يفى بدين الغريم اخذ الثمن ولم يرجع بما بقى على احد حتى يعتق العبد لان الحق في دين الاستهلاك يتعلق برقبته وقد استوفيت فيتاخر الى ما بعد العتق ثم اذا ادى بعده لا يرجع على احد لانه وجب عليه بفعله
ترجمہ اور اگر غلام کا قرض مرتہن کے قرض سے کم ہو تو مرتہن کا قرض غلام کے قرض کے بقدر ساقط ہو جائے گا اور غلام کے قرض میں سے جو بچ گیا وہ علی حالہ رہن باقی رہے گا پھر اگر مرتہن کے قرض کی ادائیگی کا وقت آ گیا ہو تو مرتہن اس کو اپنے قرض کے بدلہ میں لے لے اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے حق کی جنس ہے اور اگر ادائیگی کا وقت نہ آیا ہو تو وہ اس کو روکے رکھے یہاں تک کہ وقت آجائے اور اگر غلام کا شمن قرض خواہ کے قرض کو پورا نہ کرے تو قرض خواہ شمن لے لے اور جو باقی رہ گیا اس کو کسی سے واپس نہیں لے گا ۔ یہاں تک کہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے اس لئے کہ حق دین استہلاک میں غلام کی گردن سے متعلق ہوتا ہے اور گردن وصول کی جا چکی ہے تو حق مؤخر ہو گا عتق کے بعد تک پھر جب غلام نے ادا کر دیا حق کے بعد تو وہ کسی پر رجوع نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ وہ اس پر اس کے فعل سے واجب ہوا ہے۔
If there remains something and the debt of the slave's creditor is like the mortgagee's debt or more, then the surplus is for the rahin and the mortgagee's debt becomes void because the slave's person became entitled to a meaning that is under the mortgagee's guarantee, so it resembles destruction. Translation: So if there remains something, and the slave creditor's debt is equal to or more than the mortgagee's debt, then the surplus is for the rahin, and the mortgagee's debt becomes void because the slave's person became entitled due to a meaning that is under the mortgagee's guarantee, so it resembles destruction. Commentary: From the sale of this slave, if after paying the creditor's debt something remains, and the mortgagee's debt is equal or greater, then in both cases after paying the remainder, the mortgagee's debt has become void. The reason is that the entire slave had become entitled to another under the mortgagee's guarantee, and this entitlement is like destruction; just as in the case of destruction the debt falls, here too it falls. And if the slave's debt is less than the mortgagee's debt, then the mortgagee's debt falls to the extent of the slave's debt, and what remains of the slave's debt remains as mortgage as before. Then if the mortgagee's debt has matured, he can take it because it is of the same nature as his right; if it has not matured, he holds it until it matures. And if the slave's price does not cover the creditor's debt, the creditor takes the price and does not claim the remainder from anyone until the slave becomes free because the right in a debt of destruction is attached to his person, and it has been fulfilled, so it is postponed until after emancipation. Then when he pays after emancipation, he does not return upon anyone because it became obligatory by his own action.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the mortgaged slave who has a personal debt from property destruction. It addresses two sub-scenarios: (1) When the sale proceeds yield a surplus after paying the slave's debt, and (2) when the slave's debt is less than the mortgagee's debt. In the first scenario, if the slave's debt equals or exceeds the mortgagee's debt, any leftover from the sale after paying the slave's creditor goes to the rahin (owner), and the mortgagee's entire debt becomes void. The legal reasoning (qiyas) is that the slave's person (raqabah) has become entirely entitled to the slave's creditor, effectively like the slave's destruction; thus the mortgagee's claim ends, similar to the case where the slave dies or is destroyed. In the second scenario, if the slave's debt is less than the mortgagee's debt, the mortgagee's debt is reduced proportionally by the amount of the slave's debt. The remaining portion of the slave's debt continues as a mortgage. The mortgagee may take possession of the slave to recover his debt if it has matured; if not, he retains it until maturity. If the sale price does not fully satisfy the slave's creditor, the creditor takes the price and can only claim the balance after the slave's emancipation, because the debt is attached to the slave's person and was partially fulfilled by the sale.

Key Terms
فضل (faḍl): Surplus from the sale price after paying the slave's personal debt.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Entitlement; here, the slave's person becomes entitled to the creditor's claim.
هلاك (halāk): Physical destruction of the pledged asset; used analogically to describe loss of access.
عتق (‘itq): Emancipation of the slave; after which the remaining debt can be collected from the freedman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mortgagee's debt is paid first, so he receives 120 dirhams.
B) The slave's creditor receives 100 dirhams, and the remaining 20 goes to the mortgagee, reducing his debt to 130.
C) The mortgagee's debt is reduced by 100 dirhams, and the remaining 50 stays as a mortgage on any leftover.
D) The entire sale price goes to the slave's creditor, and the mortgagee's debt is voided completely.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on a mortgaged slave with a personal debt treats the slave's entitlement as equivalent to destruction, voiding or reducing the mortgagee's claim accordingly.

Sale of Pledged Slave to Pay Third-Party Debt
Rulings on distributing sale proceeds among mortgagee and third-party creditor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the priority of a third-party creditor's claim over a mortgagee's right when a pledged slave is sold to pay an istihlak debt, and explain the qiyas analogy used.

Core Idea
A third-party creditor's claim on a slave's neck overrides the mortgagee's security interest by analogy with destruction.

This passage from the commentary on the Hidayah expands on the rulings for a pledged slave who owes a debt for consumption (istihlak). The key legal question is: when the slave is sold to satisfy that debt, how are the proceeds distributed between the mortgagee and the third-party creditor? The Hanafi school resolves this using a powerful qiyas (analogy) that prioritizes the neck-based liability over the security interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a pledged slave to pay a third-party debt. The ruling specifies several distribution scenarios based on the amounts of the mortgage debt and the slave's debt.
The sale itself is valid; we are dealing with the distribution of proceeds.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a qiyas: 'because the slave's neck has been acquired for a meaning that is in the guaranty of the mortgagee, so it resembles destruction' (لأن الرقبة استحقت لمعنى هو في ضمان المرتهن فاشبه الهلاك).
The analogy is between the acquisition of the slave's neck (for the istihlak debt) and the destruction of the pledged property.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Just as destruction of the collateral voids the mortgagee's right to take it, so the acquisition of the slave's neck for the istihlak debt (which is a prior claim) voids the mortgagee's security interest. The mortgagee's right is contingent on the property remaining intact; here, the neck is legally 'taken' for another claim.
This is a crucial step: understanding why the analogy is drawn.
4
Apply the rulings to the three scenarios
Scenario 1: If the slave's debt equals or exceeds the mortgage debt, the mortgagee's debt is entirely voided, and any surplus goes to the pledgor. Scenario 2: If the slave's debt is less, the mortgagee's debt is reduced by that amount, and the balance remains as a pledge. Scenario 3: If the sale price does not cover the slave's debt, the third-party takes the entire price but cannot seek recourse until the slave is freed.
Each scenario follows from the analogy.
5
Note the consequence
The third-party creditor's claim takes priority because it attaches to the slave's neck (physical liability), which is considered prior to the mortgagee's security interest.
This priority is specific to Hanafi fiqh and is based on istihsan and qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان فضل شئى و دين غريم العبد مثل دين المرتهن او اكثر فالفضل للراهن وبطل دين المرتهن لأن الرقبة استحقت لمعنى هو في ضمان المرتهن فاشبه الهلاك. وان كان دين العبد اقل سقط من دين المرتهن بقدر دين العبد وما فضل من دين العبد يبقى رهنا كما كان ثم ان كان دين المرتهن قد حل اخذه به لانه من جنس حقه وان كان لم يحل امسكه حتى يحل وان كان ثمن العبد لا يفى بدين الغريم اخذ الثمن ولم يرجع بما بقى على احد حتى يعتق العبد لان الحق في دين الاستهلاك يتعلق برقبته وقد استوفيت فيتاخر الى ما بعد العتق ثم اذا ادى بعده لا يرجع على احد لانه وجب عليه بفعله
Then if something remains and the debt of the slave's creditor equals the debt of the mortgagee or is more, then the surplus is for the pledgor and the mortgagee's debt becomes void, because the slave's neck has been acquired for a meaning that is in the guaranty of the mortgagee, so it resembles destruction. And if the slave's debt is less, then from the mortgagee's debt an amount equal to the slave's debt drops, and what remains of the slave's debt (i.e., the surplus) remains as a pledge as it was. Then if the mortgagee's debt has become due, he takes it because it is of the same type as his right; and if it has not become due, he withholds it until it becomes due. And if the price of the slave does not cover the creditor's debt, he takes the price and does not seek recourse for what remains from anyone until the slave is freed, because the right in a debt for consumption attaches to his neck, and the neck has been taken, so it is deferred until after freedom. Then when he pays afterwards, he does not seek recourse from anyone because it became obligatory upon him by his own action.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from a commentary on the Hidayah, expanding the rulings regarding a pledged slave who has an istihlak debt (a debt arising from consumption, e.g., the slave incurred a liability). The author discusses the distribution of the sale price when the slave is sold to satisfy that debt. The Hanafi position is that the third-party creditor's right is stronger than the mortgagee's because it attaches to the slave's neck (physical liability). Therefore, if the slave's debt equals or exceeds the mortgagee's debt, the mortgagee's debt is voided (like destruction of the collateral) and any surplus goes to the pledgor. If the slave's debt is less, the mortgagee's debt is reduced proportionally, and the remaining slave's debt (the surplus from the sale after paying the third party) remains pledged. If the sale price does not fully cover the slave's debt, the third-party creditor takes the entire price but cannot pursue the balance until the slave is freed, because the debt rests on his neck. After freedom, the slave pays but cannot recover from anyone. The reasoning is based on analogy with destruction: the slave's neck being taken for the meaning (the debt) is like the object being destroyed, so the mortgagee loses his security.

Key Terms
دين الاستهلاك (dayn al-istihlak): A debt arising from the slave's consumption or liability, such as when the slave commits a tort or is sold to pay a creditor.
مرتہن (mur'tahin): The mortgagee (creditor who holds the pledge).
راہن (rahin): The pledgor (debtor who gives the pledge).
غريم (gharim): The third-party creditor of the slave (e.g., someone to whom the slave owes a debt).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledged slave owes an istihlak debt of 800 and the mortgage debt is 1000, and the slave is sold for 1000, what happens to the mortgagee's right?
A) The mortgagee takes the entire 1000 and his right is unaffected.
B) The mortgagee's right is voided entirely, and the pledgor gets the surplus.
C) The mortgagee's right is reduced by 800, and the remaining 200 remains as a pledge.
D) The mortgagee keeps the slave and the third-party creditor gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives priority to a third-party creditor's claim (istihlak debt) over the mortgagee's security interest, based on the analogy that the slave's neck has been taken for the debt, similar to destruction of the collateral.

Crime by a Pledged Slave: Apportioning Ransom
Ruling on distribution of ransom when a pledged slave commits a crime.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine how ransom is apportioned between the pledgor and mortgagee when a pledged slave worth more than the debt commits a crime, and identify the preferred remedy when they disagree.

Core Idea
When a pledged slave's value exceeds the debt, ransom is split proportionally; the one willing to pay is preferred to preserve the other's right.

This lesson explores a nuanced scenario in rahn (pledge) where the pledged property (a slave) is worth more than the loan. If the slave commits a crime, both the pledgor and mortgagee have financial interests at stake. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling on how the ransom (fidya) is distributed and how to resolve disagreements between the parties, ensuring fairness and protecting contractual rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interests
Separate the slave's value into the portion equal to the debt (mazmun, under guarantee) and the excess (amanah, trust).
In the example, the slave is worth 2000, debt 1000, so half is mazmun and half amanah.
2
Determine ransom liability
The mortgagee pays ransom for the mazmun portion; the pledgor pays for the amanah portion.
This matches the principle that each party bears loss in proportion to their responsibility.
3
Consider the option to hand over the slave
If both agree, they can surrender the slave to the victim, which voids the mortgagee's debt.
Actual possession belongs to the mortgagee, so handing over is effectively consent from him.
4
Resolve disagreement
If they disagree, the party willing to pay ransom is given preference, because paying ransom does not void the other's right, while handing over would void the mortgagee's claim.
The mortgagee's option to pay ransom is protected to avoid loss of his security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت قيمة العبد الفين وهو رهن بالف وقد جنى العبد يقال لهما افديا لان النصف منه مضمون والنصف امانة والفداء في المضمون على المرتهن وفى الامانة على الراهن فان اجمعا على الدفع دفعاه وبطل دين المرتهن والدفع لا يجوز فى الحقيقة من المرتهن لما بيناه وانما منه الرضی به فان تشاحا فالقول لمن قال ان افدى راهنا كان او مرتهنا اما المرتهن فلانه ليس فى الفداء إبطال حق الراهن وفى الدفع الذى يختاره الراهن ابطال حق المرتهن
And if the value of the slave is two thousand and he is a pledge for one thousand, and the slave commits a crime, it is said to both of them: 'Pay ransom,' because half of him is under guaranty and half is a trust. The ransom for the part under guaranty is upon the mortgagee, and for the trust part upon the pledgor. Then if they both agree to hand over (the slave), they hand him over and the mortgagee's debt becomes void. But handing over is not actually valid from the mortgagee according to what we explained; rather from him it is consent to it. Then if they disagree, the word is for whoever says 'I will pay ransom,' whether pledgor or mortgagee. As for the mortgagee, because in paying ransom there is no voiding of the pledgor's right, while in handing over which the pledgor chooses, there is voiding of the mortgagee's right.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a pledged slave is worth more than the loan. It is the property of the pledgor, but partially is collateral (mazmun) and partially is a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hands. If the slave commits a crime (jinayat) that requires payment of ransom (fidya) or surrender of the slave, both the pledgor and mortgagee are told to pay ransom proportionate to their share. The mortgagee pays for the portion under guaranty (in this case, half), and the pledgor pays for the trust portion (half). If they both agree to hand over the slave instead, they can do so, and the mortgagee's debt becomes void. However, in reality, the mortgagee cannot actually hand over the slave because he only has a possessory right; his 'handing over' is effectively consent. If they disagree, the one willing to pay the ransom is given preference because paying ransom preserves the right of the other party, whereas handing over would void the mortgagee's right entirely. Thus, the mortgagee's option to pay ransom is preferred to protect his security interest.

Key Terms
مضمون (mazmun): The part of the slave's value that is collateral for the loan, i.e., the portion equal to the debt.
امانت (amanah): The part of the slave's value exceeding the loan, which remains a trust in the mortgagee's possession.
فداء (fidya): The ransom paid to the victim of the slave's crime to avoid surrendering the slave.
دفع (daf'): Handing over the slave to the victim as satisfaction for the crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave pledged for 500 is worth 1000. The slave commits a crime. Who pays the ransom for the portion that is trust?
A) The mortgagee pays half, the pledgor pays half.
B) The pledgor pays for the entire ransom.
C) The pledgor pays for the portion that is trust (the excess).
D) The victim takes the slave and both lose their rights.

Key Takeaway
When a pledged slave’s value exceeds the debt, the ransom for a crime is split proportionally, and the party willing to pay ransom is preferred over handing over the slave.

6 min
Liability for a Pledged Slave's Crime When Value Exceeds Debt
Determining fidyah liability for a pledged slave's crime

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for dividing liability for a pledged slave's crime and apply it to determine who pays fidyah when the value exceeds the debt.

Core Idea
A pledged slave's value is split into collateral (mazmun) and trust (amanah); fidyah for each part falls on the party whose interest it protects.

When a pledged slave commits a crime, the liability for compensation is not a simple matter. The Hanafi school, ever precise in proportioning rights and obligations, divides the slave's value based on the debt secured. This lesson unpacks that division and the resulting duties of the pledgor (rahin) and the pledgee (murtahin).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
We have a slave whose value exceeds the debt (e.g., 2000 value vs 1000 debt). The slave commits a crime that requires compensation (fidyah) or handing over the slave to the victim's guardian.
The excess over the debt is not part of the collateral.
2
Apply the proportional division
The slave is divided: the part equal to the debt is collateral (mazmun) and belongs to the murtahin's security interest; the remainder is trust (amanah) in the murtahin's possession but belongs to the rahin.
This division is qiyas-based: the pledge only covers the debt amount.
3
Determine fidyah obligations
Fidyah for the collateral part is wajib upon the murtahin; fidyah for the trust part is wajib upon the rahin. If both agree, they can hand over the slave to cancel the debt.
Handing over by the murtahin is not valid independently; it requires the rahin's action.
4
Analyze the dispute resolution
If they disagree (one wants to pay fidyah, the other to hand over), the one who offers to pay fidyah prevails. Reason: paying fidyah does not nullify the other's right, whereas handing over nullifies the murtahin's debt.
This is a tarjih based on preserving rights and preventing harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایسے غلام کو رہن رکھا جس کی قیمت قرض سے زیادہ تھے نصف مضمون مبقیہ نصف امانت ہے
وان كانت قيمة العبد الفين وهو رهن بالف وقد جنى العبد يقال لهما افديا لان النصف منه مضمون والنصف امانة والفداء في المضمون على المرتهن وفى الامانة على الراهن فان أجمعا على الدفع دفعاه وبطل دين المرتهن والدفع لا يجوز فى الحقيقة من المرتهن لما بيناه وانما منه الرضی به فان تشاحا فالقول لمن قال ان افدى راهنا كان او مرتهنا اما المرتهن فلانه ليس فى الفداء إبطال حق الراهن وفى الدفع الذى يختاره الراهن ابطال حق المرتهن
ترجمہ اور اگر غلام کی قیمت دو ہزار ہو اور وہ ہزار کے عوض رہن ہو اور غلام نے کوئی جنایت کی تو ان دونوں سے ( راہن اور مرتہن سے کہا جائے گا کہ فدیہ ادا کرو اس لئے کہ اس کا نصف مضمون ہے اور نصف امانت ہے اور مضمون کا فدیہ مرتہن پر ہے اور امانت کا فدیہ راہن پر ہے پس اگر وہ دونوں ( راہن و مرتہن ) غلام دینے پر اتفاق کر لیں تو وہ غلام دیدیں اور مرتہن کا قرض ختم ہو جائے گا اور ہماری مذکورہ دلیل سے حقیقت میں مرتہن کی جانب سے دینا جائز نہیں ہے اس کی جانب سے تو دینے پر رضامندی ہے پس اگر یہ دونوں اختلاف کریں تو اس کا قول معتبر ہوگا جو یوں کہے کہ میں فدیہ دوں گا وہ راہن ہو یا مرتہن بہر حال مرتین پس اس لئے کہ فدیہ دینے میں حق راہن کا ابطال نہیں ہے اور اس دفع غلام میں جس کو راہن اختیار کرتا ہے مرتہن کے حق کا ابطال ہے۔ تشریح زید نے خالد کے پاس ہزار روپے قرض کے عوض جو غلام رکھا ہے اس کی دو ہزار روپے ہے اور اس صورت میں خالد کے پاس اس کا نصف تو مضمون ہے اور باقی نصف امانت ہے ( کمامر )
بہر حال یہاں ان دونوں پر ضمان جنایت واجب ہوگا یا تو اسی غلام کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیں خواہ اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دیں اور مضمون کا فدیہ ادا کرنا مرتہن کا فریضہ ہوگا اور امانت کا فدیہ ادا کرنا راہن کا فریضہ ہوگا اور اگر بجائے فدیہ کے دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ یہ غلام ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دو تو جائز ہے لیکن مرتہن کا قرض باطل ہو جائے گا۔
سوال آپ تو ماقبل میں بیان فرما کر آئے ہیں کہ غلام جنایت میں دنیا اس کام کو راہن تو کر سکتا ہے مرتہن نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ وہ مالک نہیں ہے اور یہاں آپ نے کیسے فرمادیا کہ اگر وہ دونوں غلام دیدیں؟
جواب یہ بر بناء مسامحت ہے ورنہ دینا مرتین کا کام نہیں البتہ اس کی رضا ضروری ہے اس کی رضاء کو تسامحا دفع سے تعبیر کر دیا۔
سوال اور اگر راہن اور مرتہن دونوں میں اختلاف ہو جائے مثلاً را ہن کہے کہ میں تو فدیہ دونگا اور مرتہن کہے کہ میں تو غلام ولی جنایت کو دونگا یا اس کے برعکس تو کیا حکم ہے؟
جواب جو فدیہ دینے کو کہے اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا خواہ راہن ہو یا مرتبہن کیونکہ اگر مرتہن فدیہ کو کہے تو اس میں راہن کا کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے اور اس کے حق کا کوئی ابطال نہیں ہے لہذا فدیہ دلایا جائے۔ اور اگر راہن دفع غلام پر اصرار کرے تو چونکہ اس میں حق مرتہن کا ابطال ہے کیونکہ اب غلام کا مالک ولی جنایت بن جائے گا اور مرتہن کا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
Such a slave was pledged whose value was more than the debt: half is collateral, the other half is trust. And if the value of the slave is two thousand and he is pledged for one thousand, and the slave commits a crime, it is said to both (pledgor and pledgee): 'Redeem (pay fidyah)' because half of him is collateral and half is trust. The fidyah for the collateral part is upon the pledgee, and for the trust part upon the pledgor. If they both agree to hand over (the slave), they hand him over, and the pledgee's debt becomes void. In reality, handing over from the pledgee is not permissible according to what we explained; rather, it is only his consent to it. If they dispute, the statement of the one who says 'I will pay fidyah' is accepted, whether pledgor or pledgee. This is because in paying fidyah there is no nullification of the pledgor's right, whereas in handing over (the slave) which the pledgor chooses, there is nullification of the pledgee's right. Translation: And if the slave's value is two thousand and he is pledged for one thousand, and the slave commits a crime, then both (pledgor and pledgee) will be told: 'Pay fidyah' because half of him is collateral and half is trust. Fidyah for the collateral is upon the pledgee, and for the trust upon the pledgor. So if both agree to hand over the slave, they hand him over, and the pledgee's debt is extinguished. Based on our mentioned proof, in reality handing over by the pledgee is not permissible; from his side it is only consent. So if these two disagree, the statement of whoever says 'I will pay fidyah' will be accepted, whether pledgor or pledgee. This is because in paying fidyah there is no nullification of the pledgor's right, whereas in handing over the slave which the pledgor chooses, there is nullification of the pledgee's right. Commentary: Zayd has pledged a slave with Khalid for a loan of one thousand rupees, and the slave's value is two thousand rupees. In this situation, half of that with Khalid is collateral, and the remaining half is trust (as per the ruling). In any case, here both are liable for the guarantee of the crime: either they hand over that slave to the guardian of the crime or they pay his fidyah. Paying fidyah for the collateral part is the duty of the pledgee, and paying fidyah for the trust part is the duty of the pledgor. And if instead of fidyah both agree to hand over this slave to the guardian of the crime, it is permissible, but the pledgee's debt becomes void. Question: You have stated earlier that in the crime of the slave, only the pledgor can hand him over, the pledgee cannot, because he is not the owner. So how have you said here that if both hand over the slave? Answer: This is based on leniency; otherwise, handing over is not the pledgee's action, but his consent is necessary. His consent is figuratively called 'handing over'. Question: And if the pledgor and pledgee disagree, for example, the pledgor says 'I will pay fidyah' and the pledgee says 'I will hand over the slave to the guardian of the crime', or vice versa, what is the ruling? Answer: The statement of the one who says 'I will pay fidyah' will be accepted, whether pledgor or pledgee, because if the pledgee says fidyah, there is no harm to the pledgor and no nullification of his right; therefore fidyah will be effected. And if the pledgor insists on handing over the slave, then since it involves nullification of the pledgee's right (because now the guardian becomes owner of the slave and the pledgee's debt is extinguished), it will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from Al-Hidayah dealing with a pledged slave whose value exceeds the debt and who commits a crime (jinayat). The ruling: The slave is divided proportionally between murtahin (pledgee) and rahin (pledgor). The part equivalent to the debt is collateral (mazmun) and the remainder is trust (amanah). Hence, liabilty for the crime's compensation (fidyah) is split accordingly: the murtahin pays for the collateral portion, the rahin for the trust portion. Both parties have the option to either pay fidyah or hand over the slave to the victim's guardian. If they agree to hand him over, it is permissible, but the murtahin's debt is void. If they disagree, the one who prefers to pay fidyah prevails because fidyah does not nullify the other's right, whereas handing over by the rahin nullifies the murtahin's right (debt). The commentary clarifies that the murtahin cannot actually hand over the slave (as he is not owner), but his consent is needed. The Hanafi position is clear: the muta'bih (relied-upon) view is that the one willing to pay fidyah is preferred. No intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned here; the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مضمون (mazmun): The part of the pledged slave that is collateral for the debt, equal in value to the debt.
امانت (amanah): The part of the pledged slave's value exceeding the debt, held as trust by the murtahin without liability for loss.
فدیہ (fidyah): Compensation paid to the victim (or guardian) to redeem the slave from the consequences of the crime.
دفع (daf'): Handing over the slave to the victim's guardian, which cancels the murtahin's debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledged slave worth 2000 dirhams is pledged for a debt of 1000 dirhams and commits a crime, who pays the fidyah for the portion of the slave that exceeds the debt?
A) The murtahin (pledgee) pays for the entire fidyah because the slave is in his possession.
B) The rahin (pledgor) pays for the excess portion because it is amanah (trust) and he is the owner.
C) The murtahin pays for the excess portion because he benefits from the slave's services.
D) The rahin pays for the entire fidyah because he is the owner.

Key Takeaway
Liability for a pledged slave's crime is divided proportionally between pledgor and pledgee based on their respective interests in the slave's value.

Ruling on Crime Committed by Child of Pledged Slave
Determining liability for crime of a pledged slave's child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the murtahin's right to pay fidyah for a crime committed by the child of a pledged slave and identify that the murtahin cannot claim reimbursement from the rahin because he is considered a volunteer (mutatawwi').

Core Idea
The murtahin may pay fidyah for the child's crime, but he acts as a volunteer and cannot recover from the rahin.

When the child of a pledged slave commits a crime, two parties are involved: the rahin (pledgor) and the murtahin (pledgee). The rahin may want to hand over the child to the victim, but the murtahin has a legitimate interest in preserving the pledge. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling that allows the murtahin to pay compensation (fidyah) even against the rahin's wish, but clarifies that he cannot later ask the rahin to reimburse him. The reasoning hinges on the child being 'mahbus' (held for the debt) but not 'mazmun' (collateral), and the murtahin being a volunteer for the trust portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Determine the rahin (owner), murtahin (creditor-pledgee), and the child of the pledged slave who commits a crime. The child is part of the pledge but not fully collateral.
The child is considered mahbus, not mazmun.
2
Understand the legal status of the child
The child is held (mahbus) for the debt but is not fully collateral (mazmun). This means the murtahin has custody but not ownership; the child remains the rahin's property.
This distinction is key to the ruling.
3
Apply the rule: murtahin's right to pay fidyah
The murtahin has the right to pay fidyah to ransom the child, even if the rahin prefers to hand over the child. This is because the murtahin has a valid interest (gharad sahih) in preserving the pledge and there is no harm to the rahin.
The murtahin cannot force the rahin to accept fidyah; he only has the option to pay.
4
Consequence: no recourse to the rahin
When the murtahin pays fidyah, he is considered a volunteer (mutatawwi') for the portion of the child's value that exceeds the debt (the trust portion). Therefore, he cannot claim reimbursement from the rahin.
This is based on one narration from Abu Hanifa; another narration may differ.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There are two sayings attributed to Abu Hanifa: one that the murtahin has no recourse when the rahin is present (the view followed in this passage), and another that may allow recourse. The mufta bihi is the no-recourse position.
The text indicates the second saying will be discussed later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہون بچہ کی جنایت کا ضمان مرتہن پر لازم نہیں
وكذا فى جناية ولد الرهن اذا قال المرتهن انا افدى له ذالك وان كان المالك يختار الدفع لانه ان لم يكن مضموناً فهو محبوس بدينه وله فى الفداء غرض صحيح ولا ضرر على الراهن فكان له ان يفدى واما الراهن فلانه ليس للمرتهن ولاية الدفع لما بينا فكيف يختاره ويكون المرتهن في الفداء متطوعاً في حصة الامانة حتى لا يرجع على الراهن لانه يمكنه ان لا يختاره فيخاطب الراهن فلما التزمه والحالة هذه كان متبرعا وهذا على ماروى عن ابي حنيفة انه لا يرجع مع الحضور وسنبين القولين ان شاء الله تعالى
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی اگر مرہون کے بچہ کی جنایت میں جبکہ مرتہن نے کہا کہ میں فدیہ دونگا تو اس کو یہ حق ہوگا اگر چہ مالک را ہن ) بچہ کو دینا اختیار کرے اس لئے کہ بچہ اگر چہ مضمون نہیں پس وہ اس کے قرض کے عوض محبوس ہے اور مرتہن کی فدیہ دینے میں صحیح غرض ہے اور راہن کا کوئی ضر نہیں ہے تو مرتہن کو فدیہ دینے کا حق ہوگا اور بہر حال راہن پس اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو دینے کی ولایت نہیں ہے اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں تو مرتہن اس کو ( دفع کو) کیسے اختیار کر سکتا ہے اور مرتہن حصہ امانت سے فدیہ دینے میں متبوع ہوگا یہاں تک کہ وہ راہن پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے کہ مرتہن کو ممکن ہے کہ وہ فدیہ دینا اختیار نہ کرے پس راہن مخاطب ہوتا پس جب مرتہن نے فدیہ کا التزام کیا اور حالت یہ تھی (یعنی راہن مخاطب ہوتا ) تو مرتہن متبرع ہوگا اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کی ایک روایت کے مطابق ہے کہ متبرع راہن کے موجود ہونے کی صورت میں رجوع نہیں کرے گا اور ہم انشاء اللہ دونوں قوالوں کو عنقریب ذکر کر رہے ہیں۔
The liability for the crime of the pledged slave's child is not incumbent upon the murtahin. And likewise in the case of the crime of the child of a pledged thing, when the murtahin says 'I will pay fidyah for it', he has that right even if the owner (rahin) chooses to hand over (the child). This is because although the child is not collateral (mazmun), it is held (mahbus) for the debt, and the murtahin has a valid interest in paying fidyah, and there is no harm to the rahin. Therefore, he has the right to pay fidyah. As for the rahin, the murtahin does not have the authority to hand over (the child) as we have explained; so how can he choose it? And the murtahin in paying fidyah is a volunteer (mutatawwi') with respect to the trust portion, so that he cannot claim recourse from the rahin. This is because he (the murtahin) could have chosen not to pay fidyah, and then the rahin would be addressed (to pay). Since he undertook it in this state, he is a benefactor. This is according to what is narrated from Abu Hanifah that he does not have recourse in the presence of the rahin. We will mention the two sayings, insha'Allah. Translation: And similarly, if in the crime of the pledged child, when the murtahin says 'I will pay fidyah', he has this right even if the owner (rahin) chooses to hand over the child. This is because although the child is not collateral, it is held in lieu of the debt, and the murtahin has a valid interest in paying fidyah, and there is no harm to the rahin. Therefore, the murtahin has the right to pay fidyah. As for the rahin, the murtahin does not have authority to hand over (the child) due to the reason we have already mentioned, so how can he choose it? And the murtahin in paying fidyah is a volunteer in the trust portion, so that he cannot claim recourse from the rahin, because the murtahin could have chosen not to pay fidyah, and then the rahin would be addressed. When he undertook it in this state, he is a benefactor. And this is according to a narration from Abu Hanifah that he does not have recourse in the presence of the rahin. We will mention the two sayings soon, insha'Allah.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling when the child (or offspring) of a pledged slave commits a crime. The key point: The murtahin (pledgee) has the right to pay fidyah to ransom the child, even if the rahin (pledgor-owner) prefers to hand over the child to the victim. This is because the child is not fully collateral (mazmun) — it is only held (mahbus) for the debt, meaning it is in the murtahin's possession as part of the pledge. The murtahin has a legitimate interest in paying fidyah to preserve the value of the pledge, and doing so does not harm the rahin. The murtahin cannot hand over the child (since he lacks ownership authority), so he chooses fidyah. However, when paying fidyah, the murtahin is considered a volunteer (mutatawwi') regarding the portion of the child that exceeds the debt (the trust portion). Consequently, he cannot claim reimbursement from the rahin. This is based on one narration from Abu Hanifah that if the rahin is present, the murtahin has no recourse. The text indicates there is another view (perhaps that he can seek recourse), which will be discussed later. The ruling is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah, and the mufta bihi position is that the murtahin has the right to pay fidyah but cannot recover from the rahin.

Key Terms
ولد الرهن (walad al-rahn): The child or offspring of a female pledged slave (or the young of a pledged animal) that is included in the pledge.
محبوس (mahbus): Held or detained; the child is held in the murtahin's possession as part of the pledge but not as collateral (mazmun).
متبرع / متطوع (mutabarri' / mutatawwi'): Volunteer or benefactor; someone who pays a liability without the right to reimbursement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The murtahin can claim full reimbursement from the rahin.
B) The murtahin becomes a volunteer and cannot claim reimbursement for the trust portion.
C) The rahin must reimburse the murtahin for the full amount.
D) The murtahin must hand over the child to the victim.

Key Takeaway
The murtahin has the right to pay fidyah for a crime committed by the child of a pledged slave, but he does so as a volunteer for the trust portion and cannot claim reimbursement from the rahin.

Mortgagee Paying Ransom: Volunteer or Compelled?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mortgagee paying ransom for mortgaged slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's distinction regarding the mortgagee's right to reclaim ransom and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
The mortgagee's payment of ransom is volunteering unless the mortgagor is absent, making it a necessity.

In this lesson, we explore an intra-Hanafi dispute about a mortgagee who pays the entire ransom for a mortgaged slave (half mortgaged, half held in trust). The question is whether he can reclaim the portion due on the mortgagor. Abu Hanifa draws a sharp line based on the mortgagor's proximity, while the Sahibayn see no difference. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze cases where one party acts without explicit consent.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A slave is half mortgaged (madhmun) and half trust (amanah). A ransom is demanded. Half the ransom is due on the mortgagor, half on the mortgagee. The mortgagee pays the entire ransom. Does he have a right to reclaim the portion due on the mortgagor?
This is the specific factual setting being debated.
2
Identify the dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that if the mortgagor is present, the mortgagee is a volunteer (mutabarri') and cannot reclaim. If the mortgagor is absent, the mortgagee is not a volunteer and can reclaim. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Hasan, Zufar) hold that the mortgagee is always a volunteer and cannot reclaim in either case.
The core ikhtilaf is whether the mortgagee's act is voluntary or compelled when the mortgagor is absent.
3
Analyze the proofs
The Sahibayn analogize to a stranger (ajnabi): paying for another's property without command is volunteering. Abu Hanifa counters: when the mortgagor is present, he can be addressed, so paying is like a stranger. When absent, addressing is impossible, and the mortgagee must pay to preserve the mortgaged property; he cannot preserve the mortgaged part without also preserving the trust part, so he is compelled, not volunteering.
The distinction hinges on the possibility of addressing the mortgagor.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the mortgagee can reclaim when the mortgagor is absent. Under the Sahibayn, he can never reclaim. The practical consequence is the existence of a right to reimbursement.
This thamarah directly affects the mortgagee's financial rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان المرتهن فدى والراهن حاضر فهو متطوع وان كان غائبا لم يكن متطوعا ولهذا قول أبي حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد والحسن وزفر المرتهن متطوع فى الوجهين لانه فدى ملک غیره بغیر امره فاشبه الاجنبى وله انه اذا كان الراهن حاضراً امكنه مخاطبته فاذا افداه المرتهن فقد تبرع کالا جنبي فاما اذا كان الراهن غائباً تعذر مخاطبه والمرتهن يحتاج الى اصلاح المضمون ولا يمكنه ذالك الا باصلاح الامانة فلا يكون متبرعا تشریح پہلے والے مسئلہ میں جب کہ نصف مضمون اور نصف امانت تھا اور آدھا فدیہ را ہن پر اور آدھا مرتہن پر واجب ہوا تھا لیکن مرتہن نے پورا فدیہ ادا کر دیا اب اس کو واپسی کا حق ہے یا نہیں تو فرمایا کہ اس میں اختلاف ہے امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد اور امام حسن بن زیاد اور امام زفر کا، یہ چاروں حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ مرتہن متبرع ہے اب واپسی کا حق نہ ہوگا کیونکہ امانت کا ضمان اس پر واجب نہیں تھا پھر بھی اس نے بغیر حکم کے ادا کر دیا تو یہ اجنبی کے مثل ہے لہذا واپس لینے کا حق نہ ہوگا، امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس میں تفصیل ہے کہ اگر راہن یہیں موجود ہے تو مرتہن کا فعل تبرع ہے واپسی کا حق نہیں ہے اور اگر راہن غائب ہے تو تبرع نہیں ہے لہذا اب واپسی کا حق ہوگا
And if the mortgagee paid the ransom while the mortgagor is present, he is a volunteer. And if [the mortgagor] was absent, he is not a volunteer. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Hasan, and Zufar said: The mortgagee is a volunteer in both cases, because he paid ransom for the property of another without his command, so he resembles a stranger. And his [Abu Hanifa's] proof is that when the mortgagor is present, it is possible to address him. So when the mortgagee paid his ransom, he volunteered like a stranger. But when the mortgagor is absent, addressing him is impossible, and the mortgagee needs to rectify the mortgaged property, and he cannot do that except by rectifying the trust, so he is not a volunteer. Explanation: In the previous issue, when half was mortgaged and half was trust, half the ransom was due on the mortgagor and half on the mortgagee. But the mortgagee paid the entire ransom. Now, does he have the right to reclaim [from the mortgagor] or not? He said: There is a dispute. Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad, and Imam Zufar — these four say the mortgagee is a volunteer, so he has no right to reclaim, because the guarantee of the trust was not obligatory on him, yet he paid without command, so this is like a stranger, so no right to reclaim. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is a detail: if the mortgagor is present, the mortgagee's act is a volunteer, no right to reclaim; if the mortgagor is absent, then it is not a volunteer, so he has the right to reclaim.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mortgagee who pays the entire ransom for a mortgaged slave when half the slave was mortgaged and half was held in trust (amanah). The issue is whether the mortgagee can reclaim from the mortgagor the portion of the ransom that was due on the mortgagor (i.e., the half corresponding to the trust portion). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), along with al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Zufar, hold that the mortgagee is a volunteer (mutabarri') in all circumstances. Their reasoning is that the mortgagee paid for the property of another without being commanded to do so, thus he resembles a stranger (ajnabi) who has no right to reimbursement. Abu Hanifa, however, distinguishes based on the presence or absence of the mortgagor. If the mortgagor is present, the mortgagee could have addressed him and demanded payment; by choosing to pay himself, he becomes a volunteer with no claim. But if the mortgagor is absent, the mortgagee is compelled to pay because he needs to preserve the mortgaged property (madhmun) and cannot do so without also preserving the trust (amanah) portion. In that case, he is not a volunteer and can reclaim the amount due on the mortgagor. The Hanafi madhhab mufta bihi likely follows Abu Hanifa's view, as it is more nuanced and gives the mortgagee recourse when the mortgagor is absent.

Key Terms
متبرع (mutabarri'): A volunteer who does an act without legal compulsion or expectation of reimbursement.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom paid to free a captive slave, here referring to the payment due to release a mortgaged slave who has been seized for a crime.
مضمون (madhmun): That which is guaranteed or secured; here it refers to the portion of the slave that is mortgaged (the debt security).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is the mortgagee who pays the ransom for a mortgaged slave not considered a volunteer?
A) When the mortgagor is present
B) When the mortgagor is absent
C) When the slave is fully mortgaged
D) When the ransom equals the debt

Key Takeaway
A mortgagee who pays ransom without command is a volunteer only if the mortgagor was present; if absent, he can reclaim.

Executor Sells Mortgaged Property to Repay Debt
Ruling on executor selling mortgaged property to repay debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an executor selling mortgaged property after the mortgagor's death and identify the condition of mortgagee's permission.

Core Idea
The executor stands in the place of the deceased and may sell the mortgaged property with the mortgagee's permission to repay the debt.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. When a mortgagor dies, his executor is authorized to sell the mortgaged property to repay the debt, but only with the permission of the mortgagee. If no executor exists, the judge appoints one. This ruling underscores the executor's role as representative and the mortgagee's continued right over the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the mortgagor (raahin), mortgagee (murtahin), and executor (wasi) in the scenario.
2
State the ruling
The executor must sell the mortgaged property and use the proceeds to repay the debt. This is an obligation (wajib) on the executor.
The ruling is found in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Note the condition
The executor's sale requires the permission of the mortgagee, because the mortgagee has a lien on the property.
Without permission, the sale may be invalid or subject to the mortgagee's right.
4
Identify the alternative
If the deceased left no executor, the judge (qadi) appoints one and orders the sale.
The judge acts as guardian of Muslim interests.
5
Understand the legal basis
The executor stands in the place of the deceased (qa'im maqam). Just as the mortgagor could sell with permission while alive, so can his executor.
This is a direct qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا مات الراهن باع وصيه الرهن وقضى الدين لان الوصى قائم مقامه ولو تولى الموصى حيا بنفسه كان له ولاية البيع باذن المرتهن فكذا لوصيه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب راہن مر جائے تو اس کا وصی مرہون کو بیچ دے اور قرض ادا کر دے اس لئے کہ وہی راہن کا قائم مقام ہے اور اگر زندگی کی حالت میں موصی ( راہن) خود متولی ہوتا تو اس کے لئے مرتبہن کی اجازت سے بیع کی ولایت تھی پس ایسے ہی اس کے وصی کیلئے ہے۔ تشریح راہن کے مرنے کے بعد اس کا وصی مرہون کو بیچ کر مرتہن کا قرض ادا کر دے کیونکہ پھرا ہن کا نائب اور اس کا قائم مقام ہے اور اگر اس کام کو راہن خود کرتا تو جائز تھا مگر مرتہن کی اجازت سے، لہذا اسی طرح یہ ولایت اس کے قائم مقام کو ملے گی۔ راہن کا کوئی وصی نہ ہو تو قاضی اس کا وصی مقرر کر دے اور مرہون کی بیع کا حکم کرے وان لم يكن له وصى نصب القاضى له وصيا وامره ببيعه لان القاضى نصب ناظراً لحقوق المسلمين اذا عجز واعن النظر لانفسهم والنظر في نصب الوصى ليؤدى ما عليه لغيره ويستوفى ماله من غيره
He (al-Quduri) said: And when the mortgagor dies, his executor sells the mortgaged property and repays the debt, because the executor stands in his place. And if the deceased had done it himself while alive, he had the authority to sell with the permission of the mortgagee, so likewise for his executor. Explanation: After the death of the mortgagor, his executor should sell the mortgaged property and repay the mortgagee's debt, because the executor is his deputy and representative. And if the mortgagor himself did this, it would be permissible with the mortgagee's permission, so similarly this authority is given to his representative. And if he has no executor, the judge appoints an executor for him and orders him to sell it, because the judge is appointed as overseer of the rights of Muslims when they are unable to look after their own affairs. And the benefit in appointing an executor is that he may pay what is due from him to others and collect what is due to him from others.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar: upon the death of a mortgagor, his executor (wasi) is authorized to sell the mortgaged property and use the proceeds to repay the debt owed to the mortgagee. The legal basis is that the executor is the representative (qa'im maqam) of the deceased. Just as the mortgagor during his lifetime could sell the property with the mortgagee's permission, so too can his executor. If the deceased left no executor, the judge (qadi) appoints one to carry out the sale, as the judge is the general guardian of Muslim interests. This ruling is straightforward and memorization-worthy for students of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): An executor appointed by the deceased or by the judge to manage the estate and fulfill obligations.
قاضی (qadi): The judge appointed by the Muslim ruler to oversee legal matters, including appointing executors when none exist.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The mortgagee directly.
B) The executor with the mortgagee's permission.
C) Any heir of the mortgagor.
D) The judge without conditions.

Key Takeaway
The executor of a deceased mortgagor must obtain the mortgagee's permission before selling the mortgaged property to repay the debt, ensuring the mortgagee's lien is respected.

Executor's Authority to Sell Pledged Property
Ruling on executor selling pledged property to repay debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the executor may sell the pledged property after the pledgor's death and explain the qiyas (analogy) that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
The executor stands in the place of the pledgor, so his authority to sell mirrors the pledgor's own authority.

When a person dies leaving debts and has pledged property, who can sell that pledge to repay the creditors? The executor, if appointed, has the authority to do so. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling and its proof through clear analogical reasoning (qiyas jaliy).

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act and its ruling: the executor sells the pledged property and repays the debt. The hukm is wajib (obligatory) because it is a trust duty.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The author cites a qiyas: the executor is the representative (qaim maqam) of the pledgor. If the pledgor were alive, he could sell with the pledgee's permission; thus the executor has the same authority.
The dalil is Qiyas, not a direct text from Quran or Sunnah.
3
Analyze the qiyas structure
Break down the analogy: asl (original case) = pledgor alive selling with permission; hukm = permissibility; illa = authority/representation; far' (new case) = executor after death; the same illa applies, so the same hukm.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the effective cause is explicit.
4
Note the practical application
If no executor exists, the judge appoints one because the judge is the general guardian of Muslims' rights. The appointed executor then fulfills the same role.
This shows the system ensures debts are paid even without prior appointment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا مات الراهن باع وصيه الرهن وقضى الدين لان الوصى قائم مقامه ولو تولى الموصى حيا بنفسه كان له ولاية البيع باذن المرتهن فكذا لوصيه
وان لم يكن له وصى نصب القاضى له وصيا وامره ببيعه لان القاضى نصب ناظراً لحقوق المسلمين اذا عجز واعن النظر لانفسهم والنظر في نصب الوصى ليؤدى ما عليه لغيره ويستوفى ماله من غيره
He said: When the pledgor dies, his executor sells the pledge and repays the debt because the executor is his representative. Had the testator (the pledgor) himself undertaken it while alive, he would have had the authority to sell with the permission of the pledgee; likewise for his executor. And if he has no executor, the judge appoints an executor for him and orders him to sell it, because the judge is appointed as a supervisor over the rights of Muslims when they are incapable of looking after themselves. The consideration in appointing an executor is that he may pay what is due from him to others and recover what is due to him from others.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri: after the pledgor's death, his executor may sell the pledged item and repay the debt. The proof is that the executor is the representative of the pledgor, so he has the same authority the pledgor would have had if alive—selling with the pledgee's permission. This is a clear qiyas (analogy). The commentary further explains that if there is no executor, the judge appoints one because the judge is the general guardian of Muslim interests when individuals cannot manage themselves. The appointed executor then handles the sale and also settles other rights owed to or by the deceased.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): The executor appointed by the deceased or by the judge to manage the estate.
رهن (rahn): The item given as security for a debt; the pledge.
قائم مقام (qaim maqam): One who stands in the place of another, with the same legal authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the executor's authority to sell the pledged property after the pledgor's death?
A) The executor owns the property.
B) The executor is the representative of the pledgor, so he has the same authority.
C) The judge orders the sale directly.
D) The pledgee has the right to sell.

Key Takeaway
The executor of a deceased pledgor may sell the pledged property to repay a debt because he is the legal representative (qaim maqam) of the pledgor, by analogy to the pledgor's own authority.

Executor Pawning to One Creditor: Constructive Preference
Ruling on executor pawning estate to one creditor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an executor pawning estate to one creditor when multiple creditors exist and explain the rationale of constructive payment (al-ifa' al-hukmi).

Core Idea
Pawning to one creditor is invalid because it is constructive payment, giving unjust preference over other creditors.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn addresses a common scenario in estate administration: the deceased has multiple creditors, and the executor pawns part of the estate to just one of them. The Hanafi ruling is that such a pawn is initially invalid, as it grants the creditor a preferential security interest, analogous to paying him outright. However, if the executor subsequently pays off the other creditors before they cancel the pawn, the obstacle is removed and the pawn becomes valid. When only one creditor exists, pawning is permissible from the outset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the executor pawning part of the deceased's estate to one creditor when there are multiple creditors. The initial ruling is 'not permissible' (lam yajuz).
The default assumption in Hanafi law is that creditors must be treated equally.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The evidence is a qiyas (analogy) to actual payment: pawning is considered a constructive payment (ifa' hukmi), and giving preference to one creditor via actual payment is invalid. Therefore, pawning is also invalid.
The text says: 'because he preferred some creditors through constructive payment, so it resembles preference through actual payment.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy is based on the common illa (cause) of granting an advantage to one creditor over others. Actual payment gives the creditor his due, while pawning gives him a security interest. Both result in preference, which is not allowed when multiple creditors are entitled to equal treatment.
The text explicitly says 'fashbaha al-ithar bi al-ifa' al-haqiqi' (it resembles preference through actual payment).
4
Note the exception (zawal al-mani')
If the executor pays off the other creditors before they cancel the pawn, the pawn becomes valid. The hindrance (the preference) is removed because the other creditors' rights have been satisfied.
This shows that the invalidity is conditional on the persistence of the preference, not inherent to the contract.
5
Note the second scenario (single creditor)
If the deceased had only one creditor, pawning is valid from the start. Actual payment to that creditor would have been permissible, so constructive payment via pawn is also permissible by analogy.
This reinforces that the prohibition is due to the existence of multiple creditors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان على الميت دين فرهن الوصى بعض التركة عند غريم من غرمائه لم يجز وللاخرين ان يردوه لانه اثر بعض الغرماء بالايفاء الحكمى فاشبه الايثار بالايفاء الحقيقى فان قضي دينهم قبل ان يردوه جاز لزوال المانع لوصول حقهم اليهم ولو لم يكن للميت غريم آخر جاز الرهن اعتبارا بالايفاء الحقيقي وبيع في دينه لانه يباع فيه قبل الرهن فكذا بعده
And if there is a debt upon the deceased, and the executor pawns part of the estate to one of his creditors, it is not permissible, and the other creditors have the right to cancel it, because he preferred some creditors through a constructive payment, so it resembles preference through actual payment. If he pays their debt before they cancel it, it becomes permissible due to the removal of the hindrance, because their right has reached them. And if the deceased had no other creditor, the pawn is permissible by analogy to actual payment, and it is sold for his debt, because it could be sold for the debt before the pawn, likewise after it.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn discusses the case where the deceased has multiple creditors and the executor pawns part of the estate to only one of them. This is invalid because pawning to one creditor gives him a preferential right (through constructive payment) over others, which is analogous to paying off one creditor's debt preferentially—which is not allowed. However, if the executor later pays off the other creditors before they cancel the pawn, the hindrance is removed and the pawn becomes valid. If there is only one creditor, pawning is valid because actual payment to that creditor would have been valid, and constructive payment (through pawn) follows the same rule.

Key Terms
غريم (gharim): A creditor of the deceased.
إيفاء حكمي (ifa' hukmi): Constructive payment; a transaction that effectively transfers value to the creditor, like pawning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the pawn to one creditor become permissible if there are multiple creditors?
A) Immediately after the pawn contract is signed.
B) After the other creditors agree to the pawn.
C) After the executor pays off the other creditors before they cancel the pawn.
D) It never becomes permissible.

Key Takeaway
Pawning to one creditor when multiple creditors exist is initially invalid as constructive preference, but becomes valid if the preference is removed by paying the others or if only one creditor exists.
