اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۴
جس کے مقابلہ پر شمن نہیں ہوتا لیکن اگر تابع مقصود بن جائے تو اب اس کے مقابلہ پر شمن ہو گا مثلاً اسی مثال مذکور میں قبل القبض بھینس مرگئی اور بچہ باقی ہے جس کو مشتری لینا چاہتا ہے تو اس کے حصہ میں جتنا من بیٹھتا ہو وہ ثمن ادا کر کے بچہ کو لے سکتا ہے چونکہ اب یہ مقصود بالقبض ہو گیا ہے ، اس تفصیل کے بعد سمجھئے کہ پہلے مسئلہ میں تو نماء ہلاک ہوا تھا یہاں اس کے برعکس ہے یعنی نماء بڑھوتری باقی ہے اور اصل ہلاک ہو گیا تو چونکہ اب نماء جو تابع ہے مقصود بن گیا کیونکہ راہن اس پر قبضہ کا قصد کرتا ہے تو اس کے مقابلہ میں مال ہوگا۔
جس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ زید نے خالد کے پاس نو سو روپے قرض کے بدلہ ایک بھینس رہن رکھی اس نے بچہ دیا ( لوارا ) بھینس کی قیمت ہزار روپے ہے اور اب بچہ کی قیمت پانچ سوروپے تو اصل کی قیمت تابع کی قیمت سے دوگنی ہے اب بھینس ہلاک ہو جاتی ہے اور بچہ باقی ہے اب راہن بچہ کو چھڑانا چاہتا ہے تو اس کا طریقہ یہ ہو گا کہ دونوں کی قیمت میں تناسب دیکھے یعنی ہزار اور پانچ سو میں تناسب دیکھے جب دیکھا تو معلوم ہوا کہ ہزار پانچ سو سے دو گنا ہے تو اس حساب سے قرض میں سے وہ مقدار جو بھینس کی قیمت بیٹھتی ہو اس کو نکال دیا جائے یعنی اتنا قرض ساقط ہو گیا اور جو مقدار بچہ کے حصہ میں آئے وہ راہن مرتہن کو دے کے بچہ کو مرتہن کے پاس سے چھڑائے ۔ لہذا صورتِ مذکورہ میں قرض کے تین حصے کئے جائیں گے جن میں سے چھ سو بھینس کے مقابل ہوں گے اور تین سو بچہ کے مقابل ہوں گے، لہذا چھ سوبھینس کی ہلاکت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گئے اور تین سو باقی ہیں جو بچہ کے مقابل ہیں لہذا را ہن تین سودے کر بچہ کو چھڑائے گا۔
دوسری مثال اگر صورت مذکورہ میں بھینس کی قیمت بھی ہزار ہو اور بچہ کی قیمت بھی ہزار ہو اور قرض مثلاً پانچ سو ہو تو بھینس کے حصہ کے پانچ سو روپے ساقط ہو جائیں گے اور بچہ کو پانچ سو دے کر چھڑائے گا۔ یہ بھی ذہن نشین رہے کہ بھینس کی وہ قیمت لگائی جائے گی جو اس کی قبضہ کے دن تھی اور بچہ کی قیمت وہ لگے گی جو آج چھڑانے کے دن ہے کیونکہ بھینس قبضہ کے دن سے مضمون ہے اور بچہ چھڑانے کی وجہ سے مقصود بنا ہے اور یہ ساری تفصیل اس وقت جب کہ چھڑانے کے وقت تک بچہ موجود ہو اور پہلے مر جائے تو پورا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور پورا قرض بھینس کا تقابل ہوگا بچہ کے مقابل کچھ نہ ہو گا کیونکہ وہ مقصود بننے سے پہلے ہی مر چکا ہے۔
سیہ قاعدہ کلیہ کئی مسائل کے حل میں معاون ہے
وصور المسائل على هذا الاصل تخرج وقد ذكرنا بعضها فى كفاية المنتهى وتمامه في الجامع والزيادات ترجمہ اور اس قاعدہ کلیہ پر مسائل کی بہت صورتوں کی تخریج ہوتی ہے اور ان میں بعض کو ہم کفایہ انٹی میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور اس کی پوری بحث جامع کبیر اور زیادات میں ہے۔ تشریح یہ ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ ہے جس پر بہت کی جزئیات متفرع ہوتی ہیں جس کی تفصیلی بحث تو جامع کبیر اور زیادات میں ہے ان میں سے کچھ جزئیات ہم نے کفایتہ المنتہی میں ذکر کر دی ہیں۔
Book of Pledge. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 14. 'Because it is subordinate to it, and the pledge is a binding right, so it extends to it. If it perishes, it perishes without anything, because the subordinates have no share in what is against the original, because they did not enter the contract as intended, since the wording does not include them.' Translation: al-Quduri said: 'And the increase of the pawned item is the pawner's, like the child, fruit, milk, and wool, because the increase arises from the pawner's ownership, and the increase is pledged along with the original because it is subordinate to it. And the pledge is a binding right, so it extends to the subordinate. Thus if it (the increase) perishes, it perishes without anything, because the subordinates have no share of this debt that is against the original, because the subordinates did not enter the contract intentionally, since the wording of the contract does not include them.' Explanation: If the pawned item has an increase like fruit, milk, wool, or a child, its owner is the pawner, because all these are products of his ownership. But they are kept pawned along with the original, because the right (of pledge) is a confirmed, binding right; if the pawner wants to cancel it, he cannot. And such a binding right extends also to the subordinates of the pawned item. These subordinates, though pawned, are not liable (madmin). So if they perish in the possession of the pledgee, he is not liable for them, nor does the debt drop, because the debt is really against the original; the subordinates have no share of the debt, because the wording of the contract did not include them; their being under the contract is not intentional but incidental. Whatever is subordinate, as long as it is merely subordinate, no price is in exchange for it. 'And if the original perishes and the increase remains, the pawner redeems it with its share: the debt is divided by the value of the pledge on the day of seizure and the value of the increase on the day of redemption, because the pledge becomes liable (madmin) by seizure, and the increase becomes intended by redemption if it remains until its time. And the subordinate has something in exchange when it becomes intended, like the child of a sold item. What reaches the original drops from the debt because the original is in exchange for it intentionally, and what reaches the increase the pawner redeems it for the reason we mentioned.' Translation: And if the original perishes and the increase remains, the pawner redeems it (the increase) with its share: the debt is divided by the value of the pawn on the day of seizure and the value of the increase on the day of redemption, because the pledge becomes liable by seizure, and the increase becomes intended by redemption if it remains until its time. And the subordinate has a share of the price in exchange when it becomes intended, like the child of a sold item. So whatever amount of debt is allocated to the original drops, because the debt is intentionally in exchange for the original, and whatever amount is allocated to the increase, the pawner redeems the increase with it for the reason we mentioned. ... Explanation: Whatever is subordinate, as long as it remains merely subordinate, no price is in exchange for it. For example, a person bought a buffalo that was giving milk, but before the buyer took possession, her calf died. Then the price is not reduced at all, because what died was merely subordinate, for which there is no price in exchange. But if the subordinate becomes intended, then there is a price in exchange for it. For example, in the same example, before possession, the buffalo died and the calf remains, which the buyer wants to take. Then he can take the calf by paying whatever portion of the price is allocated to it. Because now it has become intended for possession. After this detail, understand that in the first case the increase perished; here it is the opposite: the increase remains and the original perished. So because the increase, which is subordinate, has become intended (since the pawner intends to take possession of it), there is a price in exchange for it. The form of this is: Zaid pawned a buffalo with Khalid for a debt of nine hundred rupees. The buffalo gave a calf. The value of the buffalo is one thousand rupees, and the value of the calf is five hundred rupees. So the original's value is double that of the subordinate. Now the buffalo perishes and the calf remains. The pawner wants to redeem the calf. The method is to see the proportion between the two values: between one thousand and five hundred, one thousand is double. So from the debt, the amount that corresponds to the buffalo's value is removed: that much debt drops. And the amount that corresponds to the calf's share, the pawner gives to the pledgee and redeems the calf. Therefore, in this case, the debt is divided into three shares: six hundred correspond to the buffalo and three hundred correspond to the calf. So six hundred drop due to the buffalo's destruction, and three hundred remain corresponding to the calf. So the pawner redeems the calf by paying three hundred. Second example: If in the mentioned case both the buffalo and calf are valued at one thousand each, and the debt is five hundred, then the buffalo's share of five hundred drops, and the pawner redeems the calf by paying five hundred. Also keep in mind that the buffalo's value is taken as on the day of seizure, and the calf's value is taken as on the day of redemption, because the buffalo became liable from the day of seizure, and the calf became intended due to redemption. And all this detail applies if the calf is present at the time of redemption. If it dies before that, the entire debt drops, and the entire debt was in exchange for the buffalo, nothing for the calf, because it died before becoming intended. This general principle (qa'ida kulliyya) helps in solving many issues. 'And many forms of issues derive from this principle; we have mentioned some of them in Kifayat al-Muntaha, and the complete discussion is in al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat.' Translation: And many forms of issues are derived from this general principle, and we have mentioned some of them in Kifayat al-Muntaha, and its complete discussion is in al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat. Explanation: This is such a general principle upon which many particular issues branch. Its detailed discussion is in al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat, and some of those particular issues we have mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the ruling on the increase (nama') of a pawned item (marhun). The commentator begins by quoting al-Quduri's matn: the increase belongs to the pawner (rahn), but it is also included in the pledge along with the original item. The reason is that the increase arises from the pawner's ownership, yet it is subordinate (tabi') to the original. Since the pledge contract is a binding right (haqq lazim), it extends to the subordinate as well. Therefore, if the increase perishes while in the pledgee's possession, the pawner loses the increase without any compensation: the pledgee is not liable, nor does the debt reduce. This is because the increase was not the primary object of the contract; it was merely incidental. The debt is only against the original. The commentator then illustrates with an analogy from sale: if a buyer purchases an animal but before taking possession the animal's offspring dies, the price is not reduced because the offspring was merely a subordinate. However, if the original perishes and the increase remains, the pawner can redeem the increase by paying a proportionate share of the debt. The division is based on the values of the original at the time of seizure and the increase at the time of redemption. This is because the original becomes liable (madmin) upon seizure, while the increase becomes intended (maqsud) only at redemption. The commentator provides numerical examples: if a buffalo worth 1000 and its calf worth 500 are pawned for a debt of 900, then 2/3 of the debt (600) corresponds to the buffalo and drops; the remaining 1/3 (300) must be paid to redeem the calf. The general principle (qa'ida kulliyya) is that a subordinate has no value in exchange as long as it remains subordinate, but once it becomes intended, it does. This principle is applied in many other cases, detailed in works like al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat.

Key Terms
نماء (nama'): The increase or yield of a pawned item, e.g., fruit, milk, wool, offspring.
فكاك (fakak): Redemption; the release of the pawned item by paying the debt.
قاعدة كلية (qa'ida kulliyya): A general legal principle that governs many particular cases; here: a subordinate has no exchange value as long as it remains subordinate, but gains value when it becomes intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Zaid pawns a cow for a debt of 1000. The cow dies, but her calf survives. At seizure, the cow was worth 800; at redemption, the calf is worth 400. How much must Zaid pay to redeem the calf?
A) 500
B) 333.33
C) 400
D) 666.67

Key Takeaway
When the original pawned item perishes, the increase becomes intended and is redeemed by paying its proportionate share of the debt.

Ruling on Original Mortgaged Item Destroyed but Offspring Survives
Explaining debt allocation when original asset perishes but its offspring remains

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of apportioning debt when the original mortgaged asset is destroyed and its offspring remains, calculating the amounts to be cancelled and paid.

Core Idea
The offspring becomes a price against the debt only when intended for redemption; the debt is apportioned proportionally to values.

In mortgage (rahn), when the original asset is lost but its offspring survives, a precise method is needed to determine how much debt is cancelled and how much remains to be paid for the offspring. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on the principle that a dependent (tabi') can become the intended object (maqsud). This lesson walks through the legal reasoning and calculation using concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the assets and parties
Recognise the mortgagor (Zayd), mortgagee (Khalid), the original asset (buffalo), and its offspring (calf). The offspring is initially a dependent (tabi').
The values of the assets are given at possession for the original and at redemption for the offspring.
2
Determine the legal shift
The offspring becomes the intended object (maqsud) when the mortgagor intends to redeem it. Until then, it is not a price (thaman) against the debt.
This shift is crucial because it changes the allocation of the debt.
3
Apply proportional apportionment
Divide the debt according to the ratio of the values of the original asset and the offspring at their respective valuation dates.
The ratio is based on the values at the time of possession for the original and at redemption for the offspring.
4
Calculate for the first example
Buffalo value 1000, calf value 500, ratio 2:1. Debt 900 is split 2/3 to buffalo (600) and 1/3 to calf (300). Thus 600 cancelled, 300 to be paid.
The proportion is straightforward: value buffalo / (value buffalo + value calf) = 1000/1500 = 2/3.
5
Handle the exception
If the offspring dies before redemption, it never becomes maqsud, so the entire debt is allocated to the original asset and cancelled.
This prevents unfairness if the offspring is lost before it can be redeemed.

سیہ قاعدہ کلیہ کئی مسائل کے حل میں معاون ہے
وصور المسائل على هذا الاصل تخرج وقد ذكرنا بعضها فى كفاية المنتهى وتمامه في الجامع والزيادات ترجمہ اور اس قاعدہ کلیہ پر مسائل کی بہت صورتوں کی تخریج ہوتی ہے اور ان میں بعض کو ہم کفایہ انٹی میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں اور اس کی پوری بحث جامع کبیر اور زیادات میں ہے۔ تشریح یہ ایسا قاعدہ کلیہ ہے جس پر بہت کی جزئیات متفرع ہوتی ہیں جس کی تفصیلی بحث تو جامع کبیر اور زیادات میں ہے ان میں سے کچھ جزئیات ہم نے کفایتہ المنتہی میں ذکر کر دی ہیں۔
It is not a price against it, but if the dependent becomes the intended object, then it will be price against it. For example, in the said example, before delivery, the buffalo died and the calf remains, which the buyer wants to take, so he can take the calf by paying as much price as falls to its share, because now it has become the intended object of delivery. After this detail, understand that in the first case the growth (nama') was destroyed; here it is the opposite, i.e., the growth remains and the original is destroyed. So now the growth, which was dependent, has become the intended object because the mortgagor intends to take possession of it, so it will be property against it. Its form is that Zayd mortgaged a buffalo to Khalid for a loan of nine hundred rupees, and it gave birth to a calf (lawara?). The value of the buffalo is one thousand rupees, and now the value of the calf is five hundred rupees, so the value of the original is double that of the dependent. Now the buffalo is destroyed and the calf remains. Now the mortgagor wishes to redeem the calf. The method is to see the proportion between the two values, i.e., between one thousand and five hundred. When seen, it is known that one thousand is twice five hundred. So on this calculation, the amount of debt that corresponds to the value of the buffalo is deducted; i.e., that much debt is cancelled, and the amount that falls to the share of the calf, the mortgagor gives it to the mortgagee and redeems the calf from the mortgagee. Therefore, in the mentioned case, the debt will be divided into three parts: six hundred are against the buffalo and three hundred are against the calf. So six hundred are cancelled due to the destruction of the buffalo, and three hundred remain which are against the calf. So the mortgagor will pay three hundred and redeem the calf. Second example: if in the said case, the value of the buffalo is also one thousand and the value of the calf is also one thousand, and the debt is for example five hundred, then the buffalo's share of five hundred rupees will be cancelled, and he will pay five hundred for the calf and redeem it. Also keep in mind that the value of the buffalo will be assessed as it was on the day of possession, and the value of the calf will be assessed as it is on the day of redemption, because the buffalo is under guarantee from the day of possession, and the calf became the intended object due to redemption. And all this detail applies when at the time of redemption the calf is present. If it dies before, then the entire debt will be cancelled and the entire debt will be against the buffalo; nothing will be against the calf because it died before becoming the intended object. This general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) helps in solving many issues. Explanation: This is such a general principle from which many particulars are derived. Its detailed discussion is in al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat. We have mentioned some particulars in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Hanafi fiqh of mortgage (rahn). It addresses a scenario where the original mortgaged item (asl) is destroyed but its offspring (nama') survives. The text explains that initially, the offspring is not considered a price (thaman) against the debt, but if it becomes the intended object (maqsud) for redemption, then it does become a price. The key shift is when the mortgagor intends to take possession of the offspring, making it maqsud. The passage then provides a concrete example: a buffalo worth 1000 rupees is mortgaged for a 900 rupee loan, and it gives birth to a calf worth 500 rupees. When the buffalo dies, the calf remains. The debt is apportioned proportionally based on the values at the time of possession for the buffalo and at redemption for the calf. In this case, the buffalo's value is double the calf's, so 2/3 of the debt (600) is allocated to the buffalo and cancelled, while 1/3 (300) remains against the calf and must be paid to redeem it. A second example shows equal values leading to half the debt being cancelled. The text emphasizes valuation dates: the buffalo's value is at possession (since it is under guarantee from then), the calf's value is at redemption (since it becomes maqsud only then). If the calf dies before redemption, it never becomes maqsud, so the entire debt is allocated to the buffalo and cancelled. The passage concludes by stating this as a general principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) that applies to many cases, and directs readers to Kifayat al-Muntaha and the more detailed works al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat for further particulars.

Key Terms
نماء (nama'): Growth or increase that arises from the mortgaged property, such as offspring, fruit, or product.
تابع (tabi'): A thing that is dependent on another; the offspring is tabi' to the original asset.
قاعدہ کلیہ (qa'idah kulliyyah): A general jurisprudential principle from which multiple specific rulings are derived.

Key Takeaway
The offspring of a mortgaged asset becomes a price against the debt only when intended for redemption; the debt is apportioned proportionally to values, with different valuation timings.

Conditional Permission to Consume Mortgaged Property
Ruling on conditional permission to consume milk of mortgaged goat with distinction between ibahah and tamlik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional permission to consume milk of a mortgaged goat and distinguish ibahah from tamlik in the context of ta'liq.

Core Idea
Conditional permission (ibahah) is valid because it releases, not transfers, ownership.

This passage addresses a practical scenario in mortgage (rahn) where the mortgagor gives permission to the mortgagee to drink the milk of a mortgaged goat, but with a conditional phrase like 'whatever you milk is yours.' A student might wonder if such a conditional permission is valid, since conditional transfers of ownership are void in Hanafi law. The text clarifies that this is not a transfer of ownership (tamlik) but a mere permission (ibahah), which can be validly suspended on a condition. The ruling has important implications for liability and debt reduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and identify the core ruling: when the mortgagor gives permission to milk and drink, the mortgagee bears no liability (daman) and no part of the debt is reduced.
The ruling is unconditional regarding the permissibility of consumption.
2
Locate the Objection
Note the hypothetical objection: the permission is conditional ('whatever you milk is lawful'), and conditional transfers of ownership are invalid. This introduces the key distinction.
The objection assumes the permission is a transfer of ownership.
3
Understand the Hanafi Distinction
The answer explains that this is not tamlik (ownership transfer) but ibahah (permission/release). In Hanafi law, ibahah can be suspended on a condition (ta’liq), unlike tamlik. This is a fundamental principle.
Ibahah is an 'itlaq' (release), not a tamlik.
4
Apply the Distinction
Apply the distinction to the scenario: since the mortgagee consumed with the owner's ibahah, he is not liable and the debt remains unchanged. The permission is valid despite being conditional.
The condition does not affect the validity of ibahah.
5
Consider the Death Scenario
If the goat dies unredeemed, the debt is divided proportionally between the value of the goat and the value of the milk consumed. The goat portion is cancelled, and the milk portion must be paid by the mortgagee because the milk was destroyed by his act, albeit with permission.
This shows the interplay of liability and debt cancellation.

اگر راہن مرتہن کو مر ہو نہ بکری سے دودھ دوہنے اور پینے کی اجازت دیدے تو مرتہن پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا
ولو رهن شاة بعشرة وقيمتها عشرة وقال الراهن للمرتهن أحلب الشاة فما حلبت فهو لك حلال فحلب وشرب فلاضمان عليه فى شى من ذالك اما الاباحة فيصح تعليقها بالشرط والخطر لانها اطلاق وليس بتملیک فتصح مع الخطر ولا يسقط شي من الدين لانه اتلفه باذن المالک ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے ایک بکری رہن رکھی دس درہم میں اور اس کی قیمت دس درہم ہے اور راہن نے مرتہن سے کہا کہ تو بکری کا دودھ دوھ لیا کر پس جو تو دو ھے وہ تیرے لئے حلال ہے پس مرتبین نے دوھا اور پی لیا تو اس پر کچھ ضمان نہیں ہے، بہر حال اباحت پس اس کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہے اس لئے کہ اباحت تو اطلاق ( جائز کرنا) ہے اور یہ تملیک نہیں ہے پس اباحت شرط کے ساتھ جائز ہے اور کچھ قرض ساقط نہ ہو گا اس لئے اس کو مرتہن نے مالک کی اجازت سے تلف کیا ہے۔ تشریح زید نے دس روپے قرض کے بدلہ خالد کے پاس اپنی بکری رہن رکھی جس کی قیمت دس روپے ہے اور زید نے خالد کو اس کا دودھ نکال کر پینے کی اجازت دے دی تو اگر خالد نے دودھ نکال کر پیا تو اس پر کچھ ضمان نہ ہوگا اور اس کی وجہ سے قرض میں سے کچھ ساقط نہ ہوگا کیونکہ خالد نے جو کچھ کیا ہے وہ (زید) مالک کی اجازت سے کیا ہے۔
سوال یہ تو اجازت ہی صحیح نہیں ہوئی اس لئے کہ زید نے کہا ہے فما حلبت فھو لک حلال ، اور یہاں ما شرط کے معنی کو متضمن ہے اسی لئے تو اس کی خبر پر فاءداخل ہوتی ہے تو یہ و تعلیق ہوگئی اور تملیک کو کسی شرط پر معلق کرنا باطل ہے۔ جواب تملیک ہی کو شرط پر معلق کرنا باطل ہے مگر یہ تملیک تو نہیں بلکہ یہ تو اباحت واطلاق ہے اور اباحت کو شرط پر مو معلق کرنا درست ہے۔
سوال خطر کے کیا معنی ہیں؟ جواب قاموس اور مغرب میں ہے کہ خطر کے معنی ہیں ہلاکت کے قریب ہونا مگر یہاں اس سے مراد ہے جو وجود اور عدم کا احتمال رکھے یعنی یہ شرط کے معنی میں ہے۔ شامی ص ۳۳۶، ج ۵
راہن نے بکری نہیں چھڑائی کہ مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو گئی تو قرض کو بکری اور جو دودھ پیا اس پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا تو قرض کی جو مقدار بکری کے بدلے آئے گی وہ ساقط ہو جائے گی
فان لم يفتك الشاة حتى ماتت في يد المرتهن قسم الدين على قيمة اللبن الذي شرب وعلى قيمة الشاة فما اصاب الشاة سقط وما اصاب اللبن اخذه المرتهن من الراهن لان اللبن تلف على ملك الراهن بفعل المرتهن والفعل حصل بتسليط من قبله فصار كان الراهن اخذه واتلفه فكان مضمونا عليه فيكون له حصته
If the mortgagor gives permission to the mortgagee to milk and drink from the goat, then there is no liability (daman) on the mortgagee. And if he mortgaged a goat for ten dirhams and its value is ten dirhams, and the mortgagor says to the mortgagee: 'Milk the goat, and whatever you milk is lawful for you,' so he milked and drank, then there is no liability on him for any of that. As for permission (ibahah), it is valid to suspend it upon a condition and risk (khatar) because it is a release (itlaq) and not a transfer of ownership (tamlik), so it is valid with risk. And nothing of the debt is reduced because he destroyed it with the permission of the owner. Translation: And if he mortgaged a goat for ten dirhams and its value is ten dirhams, and the mortgagor said to the mortgagee: 'Milk the goat, and whatever you milk is lawful for you,' so he milked and drank, then there is no liability on him for any of that. In any case, permission (ibahah) is valid to suspend upon a condition because permission is a release and not a transfer of ownership, so it is valid with a condition, and nothing of the debt is reduced because he destroyed it with the owner's permission. Explanation: Zayd mortgaged his goat worth ten rupees to Khalid for a loan of ten rupees, and Zayd gave Khalid permission to extract and drink its milk. So if Khalid extracted and drank the milk, there is no liability on him, and nothing of the debt is reduced, because what Khalid did he did with the permission of the owner (Zayd). Question: But this permission is not valid because Zayd said 'whatever you milk is lawful for you,' and here 'ma' (whatever) includes the meaning of condition, therefore the 'fa' enters its predicate, so this is suspension (ta'liq), and suspending a transfer of ownership on a condition is invalid. Answer: Only suspending a transfer of ownership on a condition is invalid, but this is not a transfer of ownership; rather it is permission and release, and suspending permission on a condition is valid. Question: What is the meaning of 'khatar'? Answer: In Qamus and al-Mughrib, 'khatar' means near destruction, but here it refers to that which has the possibility of existence and non-existence, i.e., it is in the sense of condition. (Shami p.336, vol.5). If the mortgagor did not redeem the goat so that it died in the hand of the mortgagee, then the debt will be divided upon the value of the milk he drank and upon the value of the goat. Then whatever falls to the share of the goat is cancelled, and whatever falls to the share of the milk, the mortgagee will take it from the mortgagor, because the milk was destroyed while being the property of the mortgagor by the act of the mortgagee, and the act occurred with authorization from him, so it is as if the mortgagor took it and destroyed it, so it becomes a liability upon him, so he has its share.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding a mortgaged goat where the mortgagor gives the mortgagee permission to milk and drink the milk. It begins by stating that if such permission is given, the mortgagee is not liable (no daman) for consuming the milk, and the debt is not reduced. The text then provides the original Arabic matn, followed by an Urdu translation and explanation. A question (sual) is raised: the permission is conditional ('whatever you milk is lawful'), and conditional transfer of ownership is invalid. The answer clarifies that this is not a transfer of ownership (tamlik) but a mere permission (ibahah) and release (itlaq). Suspending permission on a condition is valid because it does not convey ownership. The passage then explains the term 'khatar' (risk) as meaning something with potential existence/non-existence, i.e., conditional. Finally, the text addresses a scenario where the goat dies unredeemed: the debt is divided proportionally between the value of the goat and the value of the milk already consumed. The portion allocated to the goat is cancelled, while the portion for the milk must be paid by the mortgagee to the mortgagor, because the milk was destroyed by the mortgagee's act but with the owner's permission, making it as if the mortgagor destroyed it himself and is liable for that share.

Key Terms
اباحت (ibahah): Permission to use without transferring ownership; a release allowing lawful use.
تملیک (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; making something someone's property.
خطر (khatar): Risk; here meaning something that may or may not happen, i.e., conditional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is conditional permission (like 'whatever you milk is yours') valid in Hanafi law?
A) Because the condition is a transfer of ownership.
B) Because it is an ibahah (release), not a tamlik (ownership transfer).
C) Because the mortgagee owns the milk after the condition.
D) Because the debt is reduced.

Key Takeaway
Conditional permission (ibahah) is valid in Hanafi law because it is a release, not a transfer of ownership, so consuming with such permission incurs no liability and does not reduce the debt.

Ruling on Permissibility of Consuming Milk from a Pawned Sheep and Debt Distribution on Death
Ruling on conditional permission and debt apportionment in a pawned sheep case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on consuming the milk of a pawned sheep with permission and apply the debt distribution rule when the sheep dies.

Core Idea
Ibahah (permission) is not tamlik (ownership transfer) so it can be conditional; milk consumed with permission does not reduce the debt until the pawn's death triggers apportionment.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi scenario from the chapter of Rahn. Understanding the distinction between ibahah and tamlik is crucial. We will see how a pawnor's conditional permission affects liability and debt distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The pawnee milks and consumes the milk with the pawnor's permission. The ruling is that there is no liability (daman) on the pawnee for drinking the milk.
The permission is a key element; without it, the pawnee would be liable.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is that this permission is ibahah, which is a release (itlaq) and not a transfer of ownership (tamlik). The text states: 'because it is a release and not a transfer of ownership, so it is valid with a risk (khatar).'
The dalil is based on istihsan, distinguishing ibahah from tamlik.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ibahah can be suspended on a condition because it does not transfer ownership, but merely permits the act. The risk (khatar) inherent in conditional permissions is acceptable for ibahah.
This is a usul principle: ibahah is a lesser right that can be conditional, unlike tamlik which must be unconditional and definitive.
4
Apply the debt distribution rule
If the sheep dies before redemption, the debt is apportioned between the value of the milk consumed and the value of the sheep. The portion corresponding to the sheep is dropped (since the pawn is lost), but the portion for the milk remains due from the pawnor.
The milk was destroyed by the pawnee with the owner's authorization, so it is as if the owner destroyed it, hence liability.
5
Extend by qiyas
The same ruling applies to offspring of the sheep and all similar increases (namaa) consumed with permission. This is by analogy (qiyas) because the illa (effective cause) is the same: increase occurring on pawned property with owner's permission.
The qiyas is based on the concept of increase (namaa) and the authorization (taslit) given by the pawnor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو رهن شاة بعشرة وقيمتها عشرة وقال الراهن للمرتهن أحلب الشاة فما حلبت فهو لك حلال فحلب وشرب فلا ضمان عليه في شيء من ذلك أما الإباحة فيصح تعليقها بالشرط والخطر لأنها إطلاق وليس بتمليك فتصح مع الخطر ولا يسقط شيء من الدين لأنه أتلفه بإذن المالك فإن لم يفتك الشاة حتى ماتت في يد المرتهن قسم الدين على قيمة اللبن الذي شرب وعلى قيمة الشاة فما أصاب الشاة سقط وما أصاب اللبن أخذه المرتهن من الراهن لأن اللبن تلف على ملك الراهن بفعل المرتهن والفعل حصل بتسليط من قبله فصار كأن الراهن أخذه وأتلفه فكان مضمونا عليه فيكون له حصته من الدين فبقى بحصته وكذلك ولد الشاة إذا أذن له الراهن في أكله وكذلك جميع النماء الذي يحدث على هذا القياس
And if he pawned a sheep for ten (dirhams) while its value is ten, and the pawnor said to the pawnee: 'Milk the sheep, and whatever you milk is lawful for you,' and he milked and drank, then there is no liability upon him in any of that. As for permission (ibahah), it is valid to suspend it upon a condition and a risk (khatar) because it is a release (itlaq) and not a transfer of ownership (tamlik), so it is valid with a risk. And nothing of the debt is reduced because he destroyed it with the permission of the owner. If he does not redeem the sheep until it dies in the hand of the pawnee, the debt is divided over the value of the milk he drank and over the value of the sheep. Whatever portion corresponds to the sheep is dropped, and whatever portion corresponds to the milk the pawnee takes from the pawnor because the milk was destroyed while still the property of the pawnor by the act of the pawnee, and the act occurred by authorization (taslit) from him, so it becomes as if the pawnor took it and destroyed it, thus it is a liability on him, so he has his share of the debt, and the remainder is according to his share. Similarly, the offspring of the sheep if the pawnor permits him to eat it, and similarly all increase that occurs, on this analogy.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on two interconnected scenarios involving a pawned sheep. The passage type is a ruling with proof: first, the permission to milk and consume the milk, and second, the distribution of the debt if the sheep dies before redemption. The author begins by stating the case: a sheep is pawned for ten dirhams, equal to its value. The pawnor tells the pawnee to milk the sheep and that the milk is lawful for him. The pawnee milks and drinks. The ruling is that there is no liability (daman) on the pawnee for the milk he consumed. The proof given is that this is a case of ibahah (permission), not tamlik (transfer of ownership). Ibahah is a mere release or permissibility (itlaq), which can validly be suspended on a condition (shart) and a risk (khatar). The term khatar here means possibility of existence or non-existence, i.e., it is conditional. The milk does not reduce the debt because the pawnee destroyed the milk with the owner's permission, so it is as if the owner destroyed it himself. The passage then addresses a second scenario: if the pawnor does not redeem the sheep and it dies in the pawnee's possession, the debt is apportioned between the value of the milk consumed and the value of the sheep. The portion of the debt corresponding to the sheep is dropped (since the pawned property is lost), but the portion corresponding to the milk remains as a debt owed by the pawnor, because the milk was destroyed by the pawnee with the pawnor's authorization, making the pawnor liable for its value. The same ruling applies to the offspring of the sheep if permission was given for consumption, and to all similar increases (namaa) by analogy (qiyas). The teacher should note that the key legal principle here is that ibahah is a lesser right than tamlik, so it can be conditional, and that permission to consume does not affect the principal debt.

Key Terms
إباحة (ibāḥah): Permission or permissibility; a release of restriction without transferring ownership.
خطر (khaṭar): Risk or contingent possibility; here meaning a condition that allows suspension of permission on the possibility of existence or non-existence.
تسليط (taslīṭ): Authorization or empowerment given by the owner to another to act on the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, why is the pawnee not liable when he drinks the milk of a pawned sheep with the pawnor's permission?
A) Because the milk becomes the pawnee's property once milked
B) Because the permission is considered a gift (hiba) which is valid conditionally
C) Because the permission is ibahah (permissibility), not tamlik, and thus can be conditional
D) Because the sheep's value covers any liability

Key Takeaway
Ibahah (permission) is a conditional release not transferring ownership; thus consuming milk with permission does not reduce debt, but on death, debt is apportioned based on relative values.

Increase in Pawn and Debt: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on increasing the pawn or the debt with Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increasing the pawn and debt, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and explain its application to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Increase in pawn is permissible; increase in debt is not according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the relied-upon position.

This lesson examines a concise matn from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on a practical issue in pawn (rahn) contracts. The key question: after a collateral agreement, can you add more property or borrow more money without a new contract? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute, with Abu Yusuf differing from the majority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Find the main ruling: increase in pawn (ziyadah fi al-rahn) is permissible (tajuz), but increase in debt (ziyadah fi al-dayn) is not permissible (la tajuz) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
Memorize this as the mufta bihi position.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Abu Yusuf holds the opposite view: increase in debt is also permissible. This is a valid difference within the school.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the fatwa, as the majority view is followed.
3
Extend to cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Outside the Hanafi school, Zufar and al-Shafi'i disallow increase in both the pawn and the debt. Understand the spectrum of positions.
The dispute extends to analogous cases: price, object of sale, dowry, and wife (in marriage contracts).
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: under the majority Hanafi view, if a pawnor wants to increase the debt, he must provide a new pawn; the existing pawn cannot secure the additional amount.
Under Abu Yusuf, the same pawn can cover the increased debt without a new contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتجوز الزيادة فى الرهن ولا تجوز في الدين عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ولا يصير الرهن رهنا بها وقال أبو يوسف تجوز الزيادة فى الدين أيضا وقال زفر والشافعي لا تجوز فيهما والخلاف معهما في الرهن والثمن والمثمن والمهر والمنكوحة سواء وقد ذكرناه في البيوع
He said: Increase in the pledge (rahn) is permissible, and it is not permissible in the debt according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and the pledge does not become a pledge by means of it. Abu Yusuf said: Increase in the debt is also permissible. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible in either of them. And the dispute with them is the same regarding the pledge, the price (thaman), the object of sale (muthman), the dowry (mahr), and the wife (mankuhah). And we have mentioned it in the Book of Sales.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a matn (from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar) stating positions on increasing the pawn (rahn) and the debt (dayn) after the contract. The ruling: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, it is permissible to increase the pawn (e.g., adding another item as collateral) but not to increase the debt (e.g., adding an additional loan). The increase in pawn does not automatically make the added item a part of the original pawn; it becomes a new pledge. Abu Yusuf disagrees, allowing increase in the debt as well. Outside the Hanafi school, Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i disallow increase in either the pawn or the debt. The same difference applies to analogous cases: increasing the price or the object of sale, the dowry, or the wife (i.e., adding another wife to a marriage contract). The author mentions that this dispute was already discussed in the Book of Sales. The teacher should note that this is a memorization anchor: the student must know the positions of the key imams. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: increase in debt is not permissible, though Abu Yusuf's view is also transmitted.

Key Terms
الزيادة في الرهن (al-ziyādah fī al-rahn): Adding additional property as collateral to an existing pawn contract.
الزيادة في الدين (al-ziyādah fī al-dayn): Increasing the amount of the debt secured by an existing pawn.
الثمن والمثمن (al-thaman wa al-muthman): The price and the object of sale; analogous cases to the pawn and debt dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling on increasing the debt (dayn) after a pawn contract?
A) It is permissible
B) It is not permissible
C) It is permissible only with the pawnee's consent
D) It becomes a new contract automatically

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that increase in pawn is permissible but increase in debt is not, requiring a new pawn for additional borrowing.

Debt Apportionment When Pledged Goat Dies After Consuming Its Milk
Explaining debt apportionment after pledged goat dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that when an increase (nama') of a pledged property is consumed with permission, the debt is apportioned between the principal and the increase upon the property's destruction.

Core Idea
Consuming a pledged increase with permission makes its value a debt, splitting the original obligation.

What happens if a mortgagee drinks the milk of a pledged goat with the pledgor's permission, and then the goat dies? Does the entire debt vanish? This passage clarifies that the milk is treated as if consumed by the pledgor himself, so its value remains due even after the goat perishes. The ruling extends to all increases (nama') of the pledged property, such as offspring or fruit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Case
Read the passage to find the scenario: a pledged goat dies after the mortgagee drank its milk with the pledgor's permission. Determine the ruling: the debt is apportioned between the value of the goat and the value of the milk.
The goat's share of debt is cancelled; the milk's share remains due from the pledgor.
2
Understand the Legal Reasoning
The passage states that because the milk was consumed with permission, it is as if the pledgor himself consumed it. Therefore, its value becomes a guaranteed debt (daman) on the pledgor, not cancelled by the goat's death.
This is qiyas: the permission makes the act attributable to the pledgor.
3
Work Through the Numerical Example
Take the example: goat value = 10, debt = 10, milk value = 10. Total value = 20. Debt is 10, so milk's share of debt = (10/20)*10 = 5. This 5 remains; the goat's share (5) is cancelled. The mortgagee collects 5 from the pledgor.
The proportion depends on the relative values at the time of destruction.
4
Apply Qiyas to Other Increases
The passage explicitly extends the ruling to the goat's young (if eaten with permission) and, by analogy, to all increases (nama') from the pledged property. The same apportionment applies.
The illa is permission to consume the increase, making it as if the pledgor consumed it.
5
Synthesise the Principle
The core principle: any increase from the marhun consumed with the rahin's permission is guaranteed by the rahin. If the marhun is later destroyed, the debt is split proportionally between the marhun and the increase.
This protects the mortgagee from losing both the pledge and the value of the increase.

من الدين فبقى يحصته وكذالك ولد الشاة اذا اذن له الراهن فى اكله وكذالك جميع النماء الذى يحدث على هذا القياس ترجمہ پس اگر راہن نے بکری کو نہیں چھڑایا یہاں تک کہ وہ مرتہن کے قبضہ میں مرگئی تو قرض کو اس دودھ کی قیمت پر جو اس نے پیا ہے اور بکری کی قیمت پر تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا پس قرض کی جو مقدار بکری کے حصہ میں آئے تو وہ ساقط ہو جائے گی اور جو دودھ کے حصہ میں آئے اس کو مرتبین راہن سے لے گا اس لئے کہ دودھ راہن کی ملک پر تلف ہوا ہے مرتہن کے فعل سے اور یہ فعل مرتهن راہن کی جانب سے تسلیط کی وجہ سے حاصل ہوا ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا گویا راہن نے اس کو لے کر تلف کر دیا تو یہ راہن پر مضمون ہوگا تو مرتہن کیلئے دودھ کا حصہ ہو گا قرض میں سے پس قرض دودھ کے حصہ کے بقدر باقی رہے گا اور ایسے ہی بکری کا بچہ جبکہ راہن نے اس کے کھانے کی اجازت دیدی ہو اور ایسے تمام وہ بڑھوتری جو پیدا ہو اسی قیاس پر ہے۔ تشریح اگر راہن نے اس بکری کو ابھی چھڑایا نہیں تھا جس کا دودھ مرتہن نے پیا ہے اور اب وہ مرگئی تو اگر دودھ والا مسئلہ نہ ہوتا تو اسکے مرنے سے مرتہن کا پورا قرض ساقط ہو جاتا لیکن اب دودھ کا بھی حساب ہوگا اور حساب پہلے مسئلہ کی طرح ہوگا مثلاً بکری کی قیمت دس روپے ہے اور قرض بھی دس روپے اور اب تک کے دودھ کی قیمت بھی مثلاً دس روپے ہوگئی اور بکری مرگئی تو مرتہن کے قرض میں سے پانچ روپے باقی ہیں جن کو مرتبن راہن سے وصول کرے گا۔ کیونکہ مرتہن نے جو دودھ پیا ہے راہن کے مسلط کرنے کی وجہ سے پیا ہے تو اس کو ایسا سمجھیں گے گویا راہن نے خود اس دودھ کو لے کر پیا ہے یا ہلاک کیا ہے تو وہ دودھ راہن پر مضمون ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی یہ بھی مضمون ہوگا لہذا قرض میں سے جو رقم دودھ کے حصہ میں آئے گی اتنا قرض راہن کے ذمہ ہوگا، پھر جیسے مثال مذکور میں دودھ کا مسئلہ ہے اسی طرح اگر راہن نے مرتہن کو اجازت دیدی ہو کہ بکری کا بچہ کھالے اور مرتہن نے اس کو ذبح کر کے کھالیا اور اب بکری مرجائے تو اب بھی یہی حکم ہو گا جو مذکور ہوا۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ ہے مرہون سے جو بھی بڑھوتری ہوگی اس کا یہی حکم ہوگا۔
From the debt, it remains with his share, and likewise the young of the goat when the pledgor permits him to eat it, and likewise all the increase that occurs on this analogy. Translation: So if the pledgor did not redeem the goat until it died in the mortgagee's possession, then the debt will be divided according to the price of the milk he drank and the price of the goat. Then whatever portion of the debt corresponds to the goat will be cancelled, and whatever corresponds to the milk he will take from the pledgor? Because the milk was destroyed in the possession of the pledgor by the act of the mortgagee, and this act occurred due to authorization from the pledgor, so it is as if the pledgor took it and destroyed it. Thus it becomes guaranteed upon the pledgor. So the milk's share of the debt remains, and likewise the goat's young when the pledgor permitted him to eat it. And all increase that occurs follows this analogy. Clarification: If the pledgor had not yet redeemed the goat whose milk the mortgagee had drunk, and then the goat died, if it were not for the milk issue, the mortgagee's entire debt would be cancelled. But now the milk also counts. The calculation is similar to the previous example: e.g., the goat's value is ten rupees and the debt is ten rupees, and the value of the milk so far is also ten rupees. When the goat dies, five rupees of the mortgagee's debt remain, which he will collect from the pledgor. Because the mortgagee drank the milk due to the pledgor's authorization, it is considered as if the pledgor himself took and drank or destroyed the milk. So the milk becomes guaranteed against the pledgor, and likewise the young. So whatever amount of debt corresponds to the milk will be owed by the pledgor. Then, like the milk example, if the pledgor permitted the mortgagee to eat the goat's young, and the mortgagee slaughtered and ate it, and then the goat dies, the same ruling applies. Summary: Whatever increase arises from the pledged property, this is its ruling.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the effect of consuming milk (or offspring) from a pledged animal that later dies. The ruling is that if a mortgagee (murtahin) drinks the milk of a pledged goat with the pledgor's (rahin) permission, and then the goat dies, the debt is apportioned between the value of the goat and the value of the milk. The portion corresponding to the goat is cancelled (since the pledged property perished), but the portion corresponding to the milk remains due from the pledgor. This is because the milk was consumed with permission, making it as if the pledgor himself consumed it, so its value becomes a debt. The same applies to the goat's young if permission was given. The proof is based on qiyas: the milk is considered as if consumed by the pledgor, so its value is guaranteed. The example given: goat value 10 rupees, debt 10 rupees, milk value 10 rupees. Upon the goat's death, 5 rupees of debt remain (10 rupees of goat + 10 rupees of milk = 20 rupees total; half corresponds to milk; debt 10 rupees, half=5 remains). Thus the mortgagee collects 5 rupees from the pledgor. The passage concludes that any increase (nama') from the pledged property follows this same ruling.

Key Terms
مرہون (marhun): The property given as pledge/security (the goat in this case).
نماء (nama'): Increase or produce from the pledged property, such as milk, offspring, fruits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledged goat worth 10 rupees and the debt is 10 rupees, and the mortgagee drinks milk worth 10 rupees with permission, then the goat dies. How much of the debt remains?
A) 10 rupees
B) 5 rupees
C) 0 rupees
D) 20 rupees

Key Takeaway
When an increase of a pledged property is consumed with permission, its value is apportioned in the debt and remains due even if the principal perishes.

Ruling on Increase in Pledge and Debt – A Multi-School Dispute
Discussion of permissibility of increase in pawn contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increasing the pledge and the debt in a pawn contract, identify the positions of Abu Yusuf, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i, and explain the practical consequences of the differences.

Core Idea
In a pawn contract, adding more pledged property is allowed, but adding more debt is not – except Abu Yusuf analogizes it to sale.

The classical Hanafi position, as recorded by al-Quduri, permits increasing the pledged property but not the debt. However, this seemingly simple rule is contested both within the Hanafi school and beyond. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the proof offered by Abu Yusuf, and the five extensions where the same disagreement recurs across sale and marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from al-Quduri's matn: increase in the pledge (marhun) is permissible; increase in the debt (dayn) is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Note that the increase does not become part of the original pledge by itself.
2
Map the objections
List the opposing views: Abu Yusuf allows increasing the debt as well; Zufar and al-Shafi'i forbid increasing either the pledge or the debt. Recognise that the disagreement is both intra-Hanafi (Abu Yusuf vs. the two Shaykhs) and inter-madhhab (Zufar/Shafi'i).
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is a strength, not a weakness.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: If a pledgor offers additional collateral, it is valid under Abu Hanifa and Muhammad but invalid under Zufar/Shafi'i. If a mortgagee wants to lend more money under the same pledge, Abu Yusuf allows it but the majority do not.
The difference affects the flexibility of pawn contracts.
4
Analyse Abu Yusuf's qiyas proof
Examine the reasoning: Abu Yusuf compares a pawn to a sale. In a sale, both parties may agree to increase the price or the object. He argues that the debt in a pawn is like the price, and the pledge is like the object of sale. Since increase is allowed in sale by consensus, it should be allowed in pawn. Identify the common cause (jami'): attachment to the original contract due to need and possibility.
This is a classic dalil aqli (rational proof) using qiyas.
5
Recognise the five extensions
The author (al-Marghinani) notes that the same logical disagreement applies to five matters: increase in the pledged property, increase in the price in a sale, increase in the object of sale, increase in the dower in marriage, and increase in the married woman (adding a second wife under the same dower). Understand that the ruling pattern is consistent across these contracts.
This demonstrates the systematic nature of Hanafi legal reasoning.

قال وتجوز الزيادة فى الرهن ولاتجوز في الدين عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد ولا يصير الرهن رهنا بها وقال ابو يوسف تجوز الزيادة فى الدين ايضا وقال زفر والشافعي لاتجوز فيهما والخلاف معهما في الرهن والثمن والمثمن والمهر والمنكوحة سواء وقد ذكرناه في البيوع ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور رہن میں زیادتی جائز ہے اور دین میں جائز نہیںہے اور اما تخفیف اور امام کے نزدیک مرہون زیادتی کے بدلہ میں رہن نہ ہوگا اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ دین کے اندر بھی زیادتی جائز ہے اور فرمایا زفر اور شافعی نے ان دونوں میں زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے اور ان دونوں کے ساتھ اختلاف برابر ہے رہن کی زیادتی میں اور ثمن میں اور مبیع میں اور مہر میں اور منکوحہ میں اور ہم اس کو کتاب البیوع میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح ایک بکری رہن رکھی تھی دس روپے میں راہن نے ایک بکری اور دیدی کہ ان دونوں کو رہن رکھے تو یہ جائز ہے یہ  اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ ۳۳۷ كتاب الرهن مرہون میں زیادتی ہے اور اگر مرتہن نے اس بکری کے عوض دس روپے اور دیدیئے کہ ان میں روپے کے بدلہ یہ بکری رہن ہے تو یہ جائز نہیں یہ طرفین کا مذہب ہے کہ مرہون میں اضافہ جائز اور دین میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف دین میں بھی اضافہ کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں۔ ور امام زفر اور امام شافعی رہن اور دین دونوں کی زیادتی کو ناجائز قرار دیتے ہیں حضرت مصنف فرماتے ہیں اہم شافعی اور از فرکا اختلاف مذکور پانچ چیزوں میں ہے۔ - مرہون کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ بیچ میں شمن کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ -- بیع میں مبیع کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ -۴- نکاح میں مہر کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ -۵- نکاح میں منکوحہ کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ جس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مولی نے اپنی باندی کا نکاح کسی شخص سے کر دیا ہزار روپے مہر میں پھر اسی مہر میں مولی نے اپنی دور کی باندی کا نکاح بھی اسی سے کر دیا اور شوہر نے قبول کر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے اور اب مہر دونوں پر تقسیم ہو جائے گا۔ اس کے بعد مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کتاب البیوع ص ۵۹ ، ج ۳، پر اسکو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تنبیہ لیکن وہاں صرف شمن اور مثمن کی زیادتی اور کمی کا ذکر ہے باقی چیزوں کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ولابی یوسف فى الخلافية الاخرى ان الدين فى باب الرهن كالثمن فى البيع والرهن كالمثمن فتجوز زيادة فيهما كما فى البيع والجامع بينهما الالتحاق باصل العقد للحاجة والامكان ترجمہ اور دوسرے اختلافی مسئلہ میں ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باب رہن میں قرض بیع میں شمن کے مثل ہے اور رہن مثمن کے مثل ہے تو ان دونوں میں زیادتی جائز ہو گی جیسا کہ بیچ میں اور ان دونوں کے درمیان علت جامع اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق ہونا ہے۔ حاجت اور امکان کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے مرہون اور دین کو شمن اور مبیع پر قیاس کیا ہے اور کہا ہے کہ بابا ء رہن میں دین شمن بیچ کے مثل ہے اور مرہون مبیع کے مثل ہے اور ان دونوں کی زیادتی طرفین کے نزدیک بھی جائز ہے لہذا یہاں رہن اور دین کی بھی زیادتی ہونی چاہئے ۔ دونوں کے درمیان علت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں اضافوں کو اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جائے گا جیسے بیع میں شمن اور بیع کی زیادتی کو اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جاتا ہے ۔ جیسے وہاں ضرورت ہے ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ضرورت ہے تا کہ مزید
He (al-Quduri) said: Increase in the pledge is permissible, and increase in the debt is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and the pledge does not become a pledge by it. Abu Yusuf said: Increase in the debt is also permissible. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: Increase is not permissible in either of them. And their disagreement is the same regarding the pledge and the price and the priced object and the dower and the married woman. And we have mentioned it in (the book of) sales. Translation: Al-Quduri stated: Increase in the pledge is permissible, and increase in the debt is not. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the pledge does not become a pledge for the increase. Abu Yusuf said: Increase in the debt is also permissible. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: Increase is not permissible in either. And their disagreement is the same in the pledge, the price, the object of sale, the dower, and the married woman. We have mentioned it in the book of sales. Clarification: A goat was pledged for ten rupees. The pledgor gave another goat saying, 'Keep both as pledge.' This is permissible; this is increase in the pledge. If the mortgagee gave ten more rupees saying, 'This goat is pledge for these rupees,' it is not permissible. That is the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): increase in the pledge is permissible, in the debt not. Imam Abu Yusuf declares increase in debt also permissible. And Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i declare increase in both pledge and debt impermissible. The author (al-Marghinani) says: Their disagreement is in five matters: increase in the pledge, increase in the price in sale, increase in the object of sale, increase in the dower in marriage, increase in the married woman (i.e., adding another woman to the same dower). Example: A master married his slave-girl to a man with a dower of one thousand rupees, then married another slave-girl of his to the same man with the same dower, and the husband accepted. This is permissible, and the dower will be divided between them. Then the author says we mentioned this in the Book of Sales, vol. 3, p. 59. Note: There only the increase and decrease in price and object of sale are mentioned, not the others. Proof of Abu Yusuf: wa li-Abi Yusuf fi al-khilafiyyah al-ukhra: 'The debt in the chapter of pledge is like the price in sale, and the pledge is like the priced object. So increase is permissible in both as in sale. The common cause between them is attachment to the original contract due to need and possibility.' Translation: In another disputed issue, Abu Yusuf's proof is that in pawn, the debt is like the price in sale, and the pledge is like the object of sale. So increase is permissible in both as in sale. The common cause is attachment to the original contract due to need and possibility. Clarification: This is the proof of Abu Yusuf; its gist is that he analogizes pledge and debt to price and object of sale: in pawn, the debt is like the price in sale, the pledge like the object of sale. Increase in both is permissible by agreement (of the other schools?), so here also increase should be permissible. The common cause is that both increases are attached to the original contract, similar to sale, due to need.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute (including intra-Hanafi) concerning the ruling on increasing the pledged property (marhun) or the debt (dayn) in a pawn contract. It quotes Al-Quduri's matn stating: increasing the pledge is permissible, increasing the debt is not, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani). The pledge does not become a pledge for the increase (i.e., the increase itself is not automatically covered by the original pledge). Abu Yusuf disagrees, allowing increase in the debt as well. Zufar and al-Shafi'i forbid increase in both. The author (al-Marghinani) notes that the same disagreement applies to five matters: (1) increase in the pledged property, (2) increase in the price (thaman) in a sale, (3) increase in the object of sale (muthman), (4) increase in the dower (mahr) in marriage, (5) increase in the married woman (mankuhah) – i.e., marrying another woman with the same dower. An example is given: a master marries his slave-girl to a man with a dower of 1000, then marries another slave-girl with the same dower; the husband accepts; it's permissible and the dower is divided. The passage then presents Abu Yusuf's proof: he analogizes pawn to sale, where both parties can agree to increase the price or object. The debt in pawn is like the price, the pledge like the object. Since increase is allowed in sale, it should be allowed here. The common cause (jami') is that the increase is attached to the original contract, and there is a need and possibility for such increase. This proof is given in the context of a different disputed issue (al-khilafiyyah al-ukhra).

Key Terms
زیادتی (ziyadah): Increase or addition to the existing contract; either adding more property to the pledge or more money to the debt.
ثمن (thaman): Price or payment in a sale contract.
مثمن (muthmin): The object of sale (the commodity being sold).
مهر (mahr): Dower in marriage, the gift from husband to wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, which of the following is permissible in a pawn contract?
A) Increasing the debt
B) Increasing the pledged property
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In a pawn contract, the majority Hanafi ruling permits increasing the pledge but prohibits increasing the debt, with Abu Yusuf dissenting via qiyas on sale.

intermediate
8 min
Dispute on Increasing Collateral and Debt in Pledge (Rahn)
Explains Hanafi positions on increasing collateral and debt in pledge with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on increasing collateral and debt in a pledge, explain the proofs of the different scholars, and evaluate the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
In a pledge, increasing the collateral is permissible but increasing the debt is not.

This lesson delves into a classic Hanafi dispute within the school and with other madhhabs regarding what changes are allowed after a pledge (rahn) contract is made. The central issue is whether the parties can increase the amount of debt (dayn) or the pledged property (marhun) after the contract. We will examine the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i, along with their respective proofs based on qiyas (analogy) and the concept of shuyu' (common ownership). Understanding this dispute is crucial for correctly applying rulings in modern financial transactions involving collateral.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the majority Hanafi view as held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: increase in the collateral is permissible, but increase in the debt is not.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing views
Recognize that Abu Yusuf permits both increases, while Zufar and Shafi'i prohibit both. Note the five examples where Hanafis differ from Shafi'i/Zufar (collateral, price, sold commodity, dower, married woman).
These five examples illustrate the broader pattern of disagreement.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's qiyas: debt in pledge is like price in sale, and collateral is like commodity; therefore increasing both is permissible. The common cause is the need and possibility of attaching the increase to the original contract.
This is an example of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Evaluate the response of the two companions
Understand their counter-qiyas: increasing the debt introduces shuyu' in the collateral, which is impermissible; increasing the collateral introduces shuyu' in the debt, which is harmless. They provide the example of pledging a slave for less than the debt to show that shuyu' in debt does not invalidate.
This objection also points out that attachment to the original contract is not possible for debt because the debt pre-exists the contract.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Conclude that in a valid pledge, if the parties try to increase the debt, the pledge becomes void due to shuyu' in the collateral. If they increase the collateral, the pledge remains valid.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the dispute).

Source Text

مرہون میں زیادتی ہے اور اگر مرتہن نے اس بکری کے عوض دس روپے اور دیدیئے کہ ان میں روپے کے بدلہ یہ بکری رہن ہے تو یہ جائز نہیں یہ طرفین کا مذہب ہے کہ مرہون میں اضافہ جائز اور دین میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف دین میں بھی اضافہ کو جائز قرار دیتے ہیں۔
ور امام زفر اور امام شافعی رہن اور دین دونوں کی زیادتی کو ناجائز قرار دیتے ہیں حضرت مصنف فرماتے ہیں اہم شافعی اور از فرکا اختلاف مذکور پانچ چیزوں میں ہے۔

مرہون کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ بیچ میں شمن کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ -- بیع میں مبیع کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ -۴- نکاح میں مہر کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔
-۵- نکاح میں منکوحہ کا اضافہ ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے ان کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔
جس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مولی نے اپنی باندی کا نکاح کسی شخص سے کر دیا ہزار روپے مہر میں پھر اسی مہر میں مولی نے اپنی دور کی باندی کا نکاح بھی اسی سے کر دیا اور شوہر نے قبول کر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے اور اب مہر دونوں پر تقسیم ہو جائے گا۔
اس کے بعد مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کتاب البیوع پر اسکو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تنبیہ لیکن وہاں صرف شمن اور مثمن کی زیادتی اور کمی کا ذکر ہے باقی چیزوں کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل
ولابی یوسف فى الخلافية الاخرى ان الدين فى باب الرهن كالثمن فى البيع والرهن كالمثمن فتجوز زيادة فيهما كما فى البيع والجامع بينهما الالتحاق باصل العقد للحاجة والامكان
ترجمہ اور دوسرے اختلافی مسئلہ میں ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باب رہن میں قرض بیع میں شمن کے مثل ہے اور رہن مثمن کے مثل ہے تو ان دونوں میں زیادتی جائز ہو گی جیسا کہ بیچ میں اور ان دونوں کے درمیان علت جامع اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق ہونا ہے۔ حاجت اور امکان کی وجہ سے۔ تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے مرہون اور دین کو شمن اور مبیع پر قیاس کیا ہے اور کہا ہے کہ بابا ء رہن میں دین شمن بیچ کے مثل ہے اور مرہون مبیع کے مثل ہے اور ان دونوں کی زیادتی طرفین کے نزدیک بھی جائز ہے لہذا یہاں رہن اور دین کی بھی زیادتی ہونی چاہئے ۔ دونوں کے درمیان علت جامعہ یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں اضافوں کو اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جائے گا جیسے بیع میں شمن اور بیع کی زیادتی کو اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا جاتا ہے ۔ جیسے وہاں ضرورت ہے ایسے ہی یہاں بھی ضرورت ہے تا کہ مزید مضبوطی حاصل ہو سکے اور جیسے وہاں امکان ہے یہاں بھی امکان ہے۔ یعنی ابتداء رہن میں یہ جائز ہے کہ مرہون کی قیمت قرض کے برابر یا کم زیادہ ہو، تو اگر التحاق کے بعد بھی یہی نوبت آجائے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ، بہر حال یہاں حاجت اور امکان ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل
ولهما وهو القياس ان الزيادة فى الدين توجب الشيوع في الرهن وهو غير مشروع عندنا والزيادة في الرهن توجب الشيوع في الدين وهو غير مانع من صحة الرهن الا ترى انه لورهن عبدا بخمس مائة من الدين جاز وإن كان الدين أيفا وهذا شيوع في الدين
ترجمہ اور طرفین کی دلیل اور یہی قیاس ہے یہ ہے کہ دین کی زیادتی رہین میں شیون کو واجب کرتی ہے اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک مشروع نہیں ہے اور مرہون میں زیادتی دین میں شیوع واجب کرتی ہے اور یہ شیوع رہن کی صحت سے مانع نہیں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر راہن نے غلام کو قرض کے پانچ سو کے بدلہ رہن رکھا تو جائز ہے اگر چہ قرض ہزار روپے ہو اور یہ قرض میں شیوع ہے۔ تشریح یہ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کے اندر شیوع جائز نہیں ہے اور شیوع اگر قرض میں ہو جائے تو یہ مضر نہیں اور مرہون میں اضافہ کی وجہ سے دین میں شیوع ہوتا ہے جو جائز ہے اور دین میں اضافہ کی وجہ سے مرہون میں شیوع ہوتا ہے جو جائز نہیں اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ مرہون کی زیادتی جائز ہے اور دین کی زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے۔۔
سوال دین کے اضافہ سے مرہون میں شیوع کیسے لازم آئے گا ؟ جواب ... جب غلام دس روپے میں رہن تھا اور پھر مرتہن نے دس کا اضافہ اور کر دیا تو غلام کا نصف غیر معین حصہ اول جس کا بدل ٹھہرا اور نصف غیر معین دوسرے دس کا بدل ٹھہرا تو غلام میں شیوع ہو گیا ہے، اور اگر ایک بکری کے ساتھ دوسری اور رہن رکھدی تو دس میں سے مثلاً پانچ کا بدل اول بکری ہوئی اور باقی پانچ کا بدل دوسری بکری ہوئی تو یہاں مرہون میں تو شیوع نہیں ہے لیکن دین میں شیوع ہے اور دین کا شیوع مصر نہیں ہے۔ پھر اس کو ایک مثال سے واضح کرتے ہیں کہ زید نے ہزار روپے خالد سے لئے اور ایک غلام پانچ سو کے بدلہ رہن رکھا تو یہ جائز ہے حالانکہ یہاں دین میں شیوع ہے مگر دین کا شیوع مصر نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے یہ جائز ہے یہ طرفین کی طرف سے امام ابو یوسف پر اعتراض
والالتحاق بأصل العقد غير ممكن فى طرف الدين لانه غير معقود عليه ولا معقود به بل وجوبه سابق علی الرهن وكذا يبقى بعد انفساخه والالتحاق باصل العقد في بدلي العقد بخلاف البيع لان الثمن بدل يجب بالعقد
Book of Pledge: Increase in the mortgaged property is (permissible?), and if the mortgagee gave ten more rupees in exchange for this goat, saying 'for these rupees this goat is pledged', this is not permissible. This is the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that increase in the pledged property is permissible and increase in the debt is not permissible. Imam Abu Yusuf declares increase in the debt also permissible. And Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i declare increase in both the pledge and the debt impermissible. The author says: The difference between us (Hanafis) and Shafi'i and Zufar is in five matters. (1) Increase in the pledged property is permissible according to us, not according to them. (2) Increase in the price (thaman) in a sale is permissible according to us, not according to them. (3) Increase in the sold commodity (mabi') in a sale is permissible according to us, not according to them. (4) Increase in the dower (mahr) in marriage is permissible according to us, not according to them. (5) Increase in the married woman (mankuha) in marriage is permissible according to us, not according to them. Its example: A master married his slave girl to someone with a dower of one thousand rupees, then in that same dower he married another slave girl to the same man, and the husband accepted; this is permissible, and the dower will be divided between them. Afterwards the author says we have explained this in the Book of Sales. Caution: There only the increase and decrease of price and commodity is mentioned, not the other matters. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf: 'And for Abu Yusuf in the other disputed issue: The debt in the chapter of pledge is like the price in sale, and the pledge is like the commodity; so increase in both is permissible as in sale. The unifying cause between them is attachment to the original contract due to need and possibility.' Translation: In the other disputed issue, Abu Yusuf's proof is that the debt in the chapter of pledge is like the price in sale, and the pledge is like the commodity; so increase in both will be permissible as in sale. The unifying cause between them is attachment to the original contract due to need and possibility. Explanation: This is Abu Yusuf's proof, the gist of which is that he analogized the pledge and debt to price and commodity and said that in the chapter of pledge, the debt is like the price in sale, and the pledge is like the commodity, and increase in both is permissible according to both parties, therefore here too increase in the pledge and debt should be allowed. The common cause is that both increases are attached to the original contract, just as in sale the increase in price and commodity is attached to the original contract. Just as there is a need there, similarly there is a need here for greater security, and just as there is possibility, here too there is possibility. That is, initially in a pledge it is permissible for the value of the pledged property to be equal to, less than, or more than the debt; so if after attachment the same situation occurs, there is no harm. In any case, here there is need and possibility. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): 'And for them two, which is qiyas: Increase in the debt necessitates shuyu' (common ownership) in the pledge, and that is not prescribed according to us. Increase in the pledge necessitates shuyu' in the debt, and that does not prevent the validity of the pledge. Do you not see that if a person pledges a slave for debt of five hundred, it is permissible even if the debt is a thousand, and this is shuyu' in the debt.' Translation: The proof of the two, and this is qiyas, is that increase in the debt necessitates shuyu' in the pledge, and this is not prescribed according to us. Increase in the pledge necessitates shuyu' in the debt, and this shuyu' does not prevent the validity of the pledge. Do you not see that if the pledgor pledges a slave for a debt of five hundred, it is permissible even if the debt is a thousand, and this is shuyu' in the debt. Explanation: This is the proof of the two scholars, the gist of which is that it has passed earlier that shuyu' in the pledged property is not permissible, and if shuyu' occurs in the debt, it is not harmful. Increase in the pledge causes shuyu' in the debt, which is permissible; increase in the debt causes shuyu' in the pledge, which is not permissible. Therefore we say: Increase in the pledge is permissible, and increase in the debt is not permissible. Question: How does increase in the debt necessitate shuyu' in the pledge? Answer: When the slave was pledged for ten rupees and then the mortgagee added another ten, then an undetermined half of the slave becomes the exchange for the first (ten) and an undetermined half for the second ten, so shuyu' occurred in the slave. And if another goat is added as pledge along with the first goat, then for example five out of ten is the exchange for the first goat and the remaining five is the exchange for the second goat, so here there is no shuyu' in the pledged property, but there is shuyu' in the debt, and shuyu' in the debt is not harmful. Then he clarifies with an example: Zaid took one thousand rupees from Khalid and pledged a slave for five hundred – this is permissible, even though there is shuyu' in the debt, but shuyu' in the debt is not harmful, therefore it is permissible. This is an objection from the two against Imam Abu Yusuf: 'And attachment to the original contract is not possible regarding the debt because it is neither that upon which the contract is made nor that by which the contract is made; rather its obligation precedes the pledge, and similarly it remains after the dissolution of the pledge. Attachment to the original contract is concerning the two counterparts of the contract, unlike sale, because the price is a counterpart that becomes obligatory by the contract.'
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the legal ruling on increasing either the debt (dayn) or the collateral (marhun) in a pledge contract (rahn). The author first states the Hanafi position: it is permissible to increase the collateral but not the debt. This is followed by the views of other scholars: Abu Yusuf permits increase in both, while Zufar and Shafi'i forbid increase in either. The author then enumerates five types of increases where Hanafis differ from Shafi'is and Zufar: increase in the collateral, increase in the price in a sale, increase in the sold commodity, increase in the dower, and increase in the married woman. An example is given for the last: a master marries two of his slave girls to the same man for the same dower. The author notes that the discussion of increase in price and commodity has already been covered in the Book of Sales. Next, the proofs are presented. Abu Yusuf's proof is an analogy (qiyas) to a sale contract: in sale, increasing the price or the commodity is permissible; similarly, in a pledge, increasing the debt (which is like the price) and the collateral (which is like the commodity) should be permissible. The common cause is the need to attach these increases to the original contract for benefit and possibility. The two companions (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) offer a counter-qiyas: increasing the debt causes common ownership (shuyu') in the collateral, which is impermissible; however, increasing the collateral causes shuyu' in the debt, which does not harm the validity of the pledge. They illustrate with an example: pledging a slave for less than the debt is valid despite shuyu' in the debt. Finally, they raise an objection against Abu Yusuf: attachment to the original contract is not possible regarding the debt because the debt is not a subject of the contract (ma'qud alayh) nor a means of the contract (ma'qud bihi); its obligation precedes the pledge and continues after dissolution. Attachment is only applicable to the two counterparts of the contract (i.e., the collateral and the debt considered as a counterpart?), unlike sale where the price is a counterpart that arises from the contract. This passage thus clarifies the nuanced Hanafi position through intra-madhhab debate and analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
رہن (رهن) (rahn): A pledge or mortgage; a contract where property is given as security for a debt.
مرہون (مرهون) (marhun): The property that is pledged as collateral.
دین (دين) (dayn): The debt for which the pledge is given.
زیادہ (زيادة) (ziyadah): An increase or addition to either the debt or the collateral after the initial contract.
شیوع (شيوع) (shuyu'): Common ownership or undivided share; here refers to the collateral becoming partially owned for different debts.
طرفین (طرفين) (tarafayn): In this context, refers to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (the two other than Abu Yusuf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), which of the following is permissible in a pledge (rahn) contract?
A) Increasing the debt after the contract is made.
B) Increasing the collateral (mortgaged property) after the contract is made.
C) Both increasing the debt and the collateral.
D) Neither increasing the debt nor the collateral.

Key Takeaway
In a pledge, increasing the collateral is valid, but increasing the debt is not due to shuyu' in the collateral.
