Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
The Sahibayn's Proof: Why Increasing the Debt Invalidates the Pawn
Proof and objection in an intra-Hanafi dispute on pawn increase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Sahibayn's qiyas that increasing the debt creates impermissible shuyu' in the pawn, and evaluate the objection against Imam Abu Yusuf's contrary view.

Core Idea
Increasing the debt creates shuyu' in the pawn (invalid); increasing the pawn creates shuyu' in the debt (harmless).

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) present their proof that after a pawn contract, the parties cannot increase the loan amount, but they can add additional collateral. Their reasoning hinges on the concept of shuyu' (commonality) and what it affects. They also rebut a different view attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf regarding annexation. Let's examine their argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core issue
The dispute is about whether you can increase the debt (loan) after the pawn is already in place, or increase the pawn (collateral) itself. The Sahibayn rule: increase in debt = void; increase in pawn = allowed.
The difference is based on where shuyu' occurs.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's qiyas
They analogize: increasing debt causes shuyu' in the pawn (each portion of the pawn secures part of the old and new debt), which is not legislated. Increasing pawn causes shuyu' in the debt (the debt is split among multiple items), which is harmless.
They illustrate with pawning a slave for 500 of a 1000 debt – valid despite shuyu' in debt.
3
Follow the objection against Abu Yusuf
The objection argues that annexing the additional debt to the original pawn contract is impossible because the debt is neither the object of contract (ma'qud 'alayh) nor the consideration (ma'qud bih). Unlike the price in a sale, the debt's obligation precedes the pawn and survives its dissolution.
This objection refutes the qiyas that would allow debt increase by annexation.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical outcome: if a lender wants to give more money after the pawn, they must make a new contract; they cannot simply add to the existing one. But the borrower can add more collateral, and the debt will be apportioned.
This affects real estate and pawn transactions.

Source Text

ولهما وهو القياس ان الزيادة فى الدين توجب الشيوع في الرهن وهو غير مشروع عندنا والزيادة في الرهن توجب الشيوع في الدين وهو غير مانع من صحة الرهن الا ترى انه لورهن عبدا بخمس مائة من الدين جاز وإن كان الدين ألفا وهذا شيوع في الدين
ترجمہ اور طرفین کی دلیل اور یہی قیاس ہے یہ ہے کہ دین کی زیادتی رہن میں شیوع کو واجب کرتی ہے اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک مشروع نہیں ہے اور مرہون میں زیادتی دین میں شیوع واجب کرتی ہے اور یہ شیوع رہن کی صحت سے مانع نہیں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر راہن نے غلام کو قرض کے پانچ سو کے بدلہ رہن رکھا تو جائز ہے اگر چہ قرض ہزار روپے ہو اور یہ قرض میں شیوع ہے۔ تشریح یہ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کے اندر شیوع جائز نہیں ہے اور شیوع اگر قرض میں ہو جائے تو یہ مضر نہیں اور مرہون میں اضافہ کی وجہ سے دین میں شیوع ہوتا ہے جو جائز ہے اور دین میں اضافہ کی وجہ سے مرہون میں شیوع ہوتا ہے جو جائز نہیں اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ مرہون کی زیادتی جائز ہے اور دین کی زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے۔۔
سوال دین کے اضافہ سے مرہون میں شیوع کیسے لازم آئے گا ؟ جواب ... جب غلام دس روپے میں رہن تھا اور پھر مرتہن نے دس کا اضافہ اور کر دیا تو غلام کا نصف غیر معین حصہ اول جس کا بدل ٹھہرا اور نصف غیر معین دوسرے دس کا بدل ٹھہرا تو غلام میں شیوع ہو گیا ہے، اور اگر ایک بکری کے ساتھ دوسری اور رہن رکھدی تو دس میں سے مثلاً پانچ کا بدل اول بکری ہوئی اور باقی پانچ کا بدل دوسری بکری ہوئی تو یہاں مرہون میں تو شیوع نہیں ہے لیکن دین میں شیوع ہے اور دین کا شیوع مضر نہیں ہے۔ پھر اس کو ایک مثال سے واضح کرتے ہیں کہ زید نے ہزار روپے خالد سے لئے اور ایک غلام پانچ سو کے بدلہ رہن رکھا تو یہ جائز ہے حالانکہ یہاں دین میں شیوع ہے مگر دین کا شیوع مضر نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے یہ جائز ہے یہ
طرفین کی طرف سے امام ابو یوسف پر اعتراض
والالتحاق بأصل العقد غير ممكن فى طرف الدين لانه غير معقود عليه ولا معقود به بل وجوبه سابق علی الرهن وكذا يبقى بعد انفساخه والالتحاق باصل العقد في بدلي العقد بخلاف البيع لان الثمن بدل يجب بالعقد

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴
كتاب الرهن
ترجمہ اور اصل عقد کے ساتھ الحاق ممکن نہیں ہے قرض کی جانب میں اس لئے کہ وہ نہ معقود علیہ اور نہ معقود بہ ہے بلکہ قرض کا وجوب رہن پر مقدم ہے اور ایسے ہی عقد رہن کے فسخ ہونے کے بعد باقی رہے گا اور اصل عقد کے ساتھ الحاق عقد کے دونوں بدلوں میں ہوتا ہے بخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ ثمن ایسا بدل ہے جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح یہ طرفین کی جانب سے امام ابو یوسف پر زبردست اعتراض ہے۔ ہوسکتا۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جناب والا! آپکا قیاس مذکور صحیح نہیں ہے اور باب رہن میں دین کا اضافہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیونکہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ الحاق معقود علیہ یا معقود بہ کا ہوسکتا ہے اور دین نہ معقود علیہ ہے اور نہ معقود بہ ہے اور باب بیع میں ثمن کا اضافہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ اس لئے لاحق ہو سکتا ہے کہ ثمن معقود ہے، معقود علیہ یعنی بیع اور معقود بہ یعنی ثمن اور قرض ان دونوں میں سے کچھ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر قرض معقود بہ ہوتا تو عقد رہن کی وجہ سے قرض واجب ہوتا ہے حالانکہ قرض بغیر عقد رہن کے واجب ہوتا ہے اور قرض کا وجوب پہلے ہو گیا اور عقد رہن بعد میں ہو جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر کسی وجہ سے عقد رہن فسخ ہو جائے تو قرض اب بھی باقی رہتا ہے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ معقود بہ نہیں ہے البتہ ثمن کا وجوب عقد بیع کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور اگر بیع فسخ ہو جائے تو ثمن کا وجوب بھی ختم ہو جاتا ہے لہذا آپکا قیاس ہی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
رہن میں زیادتی کا حکم
ثم اذا صحت الزيادة فى الرهن وتسمى هذه زيادة قصدية يقسم الدين على قيمة الاول يوم القبض وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت حتى لو كانت قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضها خمس مائة وقيمة الأول يوم القبض الفا والدين الفا يقسم الدين اثلاثا فى الزيادة ثلث الدين وفى الاصل ثلثا الدين اعتبار بقيمتهما في وقتى الاعتباراً وهذا لان الضمان فى كل واحد منهما يثبت بالقبض فتعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما وقت القبض ترجمہ پھر جب کہ مرہون میں زیادتی صحیح ہوگئی اور اس زیادتی کا نام قصدی زیادتی رکھا جاتا ہے تو قرض کو تقسیم کیا جائے گا قبضہ کے دن کی اول کی قیمت پر اور قبضہ کے دن کی زیادتی کی قیمت پر یہاں تک کہ اگر زیادتی کی قیمت اس پر قبضہ کے دن پانچ سو ہو اور اول کی قیمت قبضہ کے دن ہزار ہو اور قرض ہزار ہو تو قرض کو تین حصوں پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا زیادتی میں دین کا ثلث اور اصل میں دین کے دو ثلث بوقت اعتبار ان دونوں کی قیمت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ ضمان ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک میں قبضہ کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی قیمت قبضہ کے وقت کی معتبر ہوگی۔ تشریح ہلاکت اصل کی صورت میں جو مسئلہ گذرا ہے یہ مسئلہ بھی بالکل ایسا ہی ہے بس اتنا فرق ہے کہ وہاں بچہ کی قیمت یوم فکاک کی معتبر ہوتی ہے اور یہاں زیادتی کی وہ قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو قبضہ کے دن اس کی قیمت تھی، اگر چہ وہ بھی زیادتی ہے اور یہ بھی زیادتی ہے مگر دونوں میں فرق ہے وہ زیادتی غیر ارادی ہے اور یہ زیادتی ارادی اور قصدی ہے اس وجہ سے دونوں میں فرق کیا گیا ہے، نیز اصل اور یہ زیادتی دونوں قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہوتی ہیں تو دونوں میں قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور غیر ارادی زیادتی چھڑانے کی وجہ سے
Book of Pawn. ... Strength can be obtained, and just as there is possibility there, here also possibility exists. That is, initially in the pawn it is permissible for the value of the pawn to be equal to or less or more than the debt. So if after annexation this situation occurs, there is no harm. In any case, here there is need and possibility.
Proof of the two parties: And for them, and it is the qiyas, that increase in the debt necessitates commonality in the pawn, and that is not legislated according to us. And increase in the pawn necessitates commonality in the debt, and that is not a barrier to the validity of the pawn. Do you not see that if the pawnor pawned a slave for five hundred of the debt, it is valid even if the debt is a thousand, and this is commonality in the debt.
Translation: ... This is the proof of these two persons. The summary is that it has passed before that commonality within the pawn is not permissible, and if commonality occurs in the debt, it is not harmful. Increase in the pawn causes commonality in the debt, which is permissible. Increase in the debt causes commonality in the pawn, which is not permissible. Therefore we said that increase in the pawn is permissible and increase in the debt is not permissible.
Question: How does increase in debt necessitate commonality in the pawn? Answer: When a slave was pawned for ten rupees and then the mortgagee added another ten rupees, then half of the unspecified portion of the slave becomes the consideration for the first, and the other unspecified half becomes the consideration for the second, so commonality occurs in the slave. And if another goat is pawned along with a goat, then for example five out of ten is consideration for the first goat and the remaining five is consideration for the second goat, so here commonality does not occur in the pawn but commonality occurs in the debt, and commonality in the debt is not harmful. Then they clarify this with an example: Zayd took a thousand rupees from Khalid and pawned a slave for five hundred, this is permissible, even though here there is commonality in the debt, but commonality in the debt is not harmful, therefore it is permissible.
Objection from the two parties against Imam Abu Yusuf: And annexation to the original contract is not possible on the side of the debt because it is neither the object of contract nor the consideration. Rather, its obligation precedes the pawn, and similarly it remains after its dissolution. Annexation to the original contract applies to the two counter-values of the contract, unlike sale because the price is a consideration that becomes obligatory by the contract.
Translation: ... Annexation to the original contract is not possible on the side of the loan because it is neither the object of contract nor the consideration. Rather, the obligation of the loan precedes the pawn, and similarly it will remain after the dissolution of the pawn contract, and annexation to the original contract is done in the two counter-values of the contract, contrary to sale because the price is a consideration that becomes obligatory by the contract. Commentary: This is a strong objection from the two parties against Imam Abu Yusuf. Its summary is: Sir! Your mentioned qiyas is not correct, and in the chapter of pawn, increase in debt cannot be annexed to the original contract because annexation to the original contract can only be of the object of contract or the consideration, and the loan is neither the object of contract nor the consideration. In the chapter of sale, increase in the price can be annexed because the price is the consideration. The object of contract (sale) and the consideration (price)—the loan is neither of these. Because if the loan were the consideration, the loan would become obligatory by the pawn contract, whereas the loan is obligatory without the pawn contract, and its obligation occurred earlier, and the pawn contract occurs later. Similarly, if for some reason the pawn contract is dissolved, the loan still remains. So it is clear that it is not the consideration. Rather, the obligation of the price arises from the sale contract, and if the sale is dissolved, the obligation of the price also ends. Therefore, your qiyas itself is not correct.
Ruling on increase in pawn: Then when the increase in the pawn is valid, and this is called intentional increase, the debt is divided based on the value of the original on the day of possession and the value of the increase on the day it was taken into possession. So if the value of the increase on the day of possession is five hundred, and the value of the original on the day of possession is a thousand, and the debt is a thousand, the debt is divided into thirds: one third of the debt is on the increase and two thirds on the original, considering their values at the times of consideration. This is because the liability (daman) in each of them is established by possession, so the value of each at the time of possession is considered.
Translation: ... Then when the increase in the pawn is valid, and this increase is called intentional increase, the debt will be divided based on the value of the original on the day of possession and the value of the increase on the day of possession. So if the value of the increase at the time of its possession is five hundred, and the value of the original at the time of possession is a thousand, and the debt is a thousand, then the debt is divided into three parts: in the increase, one third of the debt, and in the original, two thirds of the debt, considering their values at the times of consideration. And this is because liability in each of them is established by possession, so the value of each at the time of possession is considered. Commentary: This is exactly like the issue that passed regarding the destruction of the original, with the difference that there the value of the young at the time of redemption is considered, and here the value of the increase that was at the time of possession will be considered. Even though that too is an increase and this is an increase, there is a difference: that increase is unintentional and this increase is intentional and deliberate, therefore a distinction is made between them. Also, both the original and this increase become liable due to possession, so the value at the time of possession is considered for both.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling statement from the Book of Pawn (Kitab al-Rahn) in Ashraf al-Hidaya, a commentary on al-Hidaya. The author first presents the proof of the two parties (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the permissibility of increasing the pawn versus increasing the debt. Their qiyas (analogy) states: increasing the debt causes shuyu' (commonality) in the pawn itself, which is not legislated according to the Hanafi school; whereas increasing the pawn causes shuyu' in the debt, which does not harm the validity of the pawn. They illustrate with an example: if a slave is pawned for five hundred while the debt is one thousand, the pawn is valid despite shuyu' in the debt. Then a question-answer section clarifies how increase in debt leads to shuyu' in the pawn (e.g., a slave pawned for ten rupees, then an additional ten rupees creates shuyu' in the slave's portions). Next, an objection is raised by the Sahibayn against Imam Abu Yusuf (though the text is ambiguous; the commentary explicitly states it is an objection from 'the two parties' against Abu Yusuf). The objection argues that annexation (ilhaq) of the additional debt to the original pawn contract is impossible because the debt is neither the object of contract (ma'qud 'alayh) nor the consideration (ma'qud bih). The debt's obligation precedes the pawn and survives its dissolution, unlike the price (thaman) in a sale, which is created by the contract and ceases upon its dissolution. Therefore, the qiyas presented by the opposing view is invalid. Finally, the passage gives the ruling on intentional increase (ziyada qasdiyya) in the pawn: once the increase is valid, the debt is apportioned proportionately based on the values of the original pawn and the increase at the time of possession. For example, if the original was worth 1000 and the increase 500 at possession, with a debt of 1000, the increase covers 1/3 of the debt and the original covers 2/3. This is because liability (daman) is established by possession, so values at that time are considered.

Key Terms
شيوع (shuyūʿ): Commonality or shared ownership; here it refers to one pawn securing multiple debts or one debt being secured by multiple pawns, creating a fractional relationship.
الحاق (ilḥāq): Annexation; attaching an additional element (like an increased debt) to the original contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is increasing the debt in a pawn contract invalid?
A) Because it changes the original agreement without consent.
B) Because it creates commonality in the pawn, which is not legislated.
C) Because the pawn's value must always exceed the debt.
D) Because the borrower cannot afford the interest.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, after a pawn contract, the debt cannot be increased without a new contract, but the pawn can be increased by adding more collateral, as the resulting shuyu' in the debt is harmless.

Intentional Increase in Pawn: Apportioning the Debt by Value at Possession
Ruling on intentional increase in pawn with calculation method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the apportionment of debt when an intentional increase (ziyada qasdiyya) is added to a pawned item, using the values at the time of possession.

Core Idea
For intentional increase in pawn, the debt is divided proportionally based on the values of the original and the increase at the time each was taken into possession.

After establishing that increasing the pawn itself is valid, the author of Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the financial consequences. When a borrower voluntarily adds another item to the existing pawn, the total debt is bifurcated between the original pawn and the new addition according to their respective values when they were physically taken by the lender. This apportionment relies on the principle that liability (daman) is established by possession, not by the contract date. Let's see how the calculation works.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of intentional increase
This is when the borrower deliberately adds a new item to the existing pawn, as opposed to an unintentional increase like the birth of an offspring. The ruling differs.
Intentional increase = ziyada qasdiyya.
2
Identify the two valuations
The debt is divided using: (a) the value of the original pawn on the day the lender took possession of it, and (b) the value of the increase on the day the lender took possession of the new item.
These may be different dates if the increase is added later.
3
Apply the formula
The original and the increase cover the debt in proportion to their values at the respective possession dates. Example: original value = 1000, increase value = 500 at possession, total debt = 1000. Then original covers 2/3 (666.67), increase covers 1/3 (333.33).
The sum of the proportions equals the debt.
4
Note the distinction from unintentional increase
For unintentional increase (e.g., offspring), the value at the time of redemption (fakak) is used, not possession. This is because the offspring was not in existence at possession.
This distinction is critical for correct calculation.

كتاب الرهن
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴ مضبوطی حاصل ہو سکے اور جیسے وہاں امکان ہے یہاں بھی امکان ہے۔ یعنی ابتداء رہن میں یہ جائز ہے کہ مرہون کی قیمت قرض کے برابر یا کم زیادہ ہو، تو اگر الحاق کے بعد بھی یہی نوبت آجائے تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ، بہر حال یہاں حاجت اور امکان ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل
ولهما وهو القياس ان الزيادة فى الدين توجب الشيوع في الرهن وهو غير مشروع عندنا والزيادة في الرهن توجب الشيوع في الدين وهو غير مانع من صحة الرهن الا ترى انه لورهن عبدا بخمس مائة من الدين جاز وإن كان الدين ألفا وهذا شيوع في الدين
ترجمہ اور طرفین کی دلیل اور یہی قیاس ہے یہ ہے کہ دین کی زیادتی رہن میں شیوع کو واجب کرتی ہے اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک مشروع نہیں ہے اور مرہون میں زیادتی دین میں شیوع واجب کرتی ہے اور یہ شیوع رہن کی صحت سے مانع نہیں ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر راہن نے غلام کو قرض کے پانچ سو کے بدلہ رہن رکھا تو جائز ہے اگر چہ قرض ہزار روپے ہو اور یہ قرض میں شیوع ہے۔ تشریح یہ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کے اندر شیوع جائز نہیں ہے اور شیوع اگر قرض میں ہو جائے تو یہ مضر نہیں اور مرہون میں اضافہ کی وجہ سے دین میں شیوع ہوتا ہے جو جائز ہے اور دین میں اضافہ کی وجہ سے مرہون میں شیوع ہوتا ہے جو جائز نہیں اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ مرہون کی زیادتی جائز ہے اور دین کی زیادتی جائز نہیں ہے۔۔
سوال دین کے اضافہ سے مرہون میں شیوع کیسے لازم آئے گا ؟ جواب ... جب غلام دس روپے میں رہن تھا اور پھر مرتہن نے دس کا اضافہ اور کر دیا تو غلام کا نصف غیر معین حصہ اول جس کا بدل ٹھہرا اور نصف غیر معین دوسرے دس کا بدل ٹھہرا تو غلام میں شیوع ہو گیا ہے، اور اگر ایک بکری کے ساتھ دوسری اور رہن رکھدی تو دس میں سے مثلاً پانچ کا بدل اول بکری ہوئی اور باقی پانچ کا بدل دوسری بکری ہوئی تو یہاں مرہون میں تو شیوع نہیں ہے لیکن دین میں شیوع ہے اور دین کا شیوع مضر نہیں ہے۔ پھر اس کو ایک مثال سے واضح کرتے ہیں کہ زید نے ہزار روپے خالد سے لئے اور ایک غلام پانچ سو کے بدلہ رہن رکھا تو یہ جائز ہے حالانکہ یہاں دین میں شیوع ہے مگر دین کا شیوع مضر نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے یہ جائز ہے یہ
طرفین کی طرف سے امام ابو یوسف پر اعتراض
والالتحاق بأصل العقد غير ممكن فى طرف الدين لانه غير معقود عليه ولا معقود به بل وجوبه سابق علی الرهن وكذا يبقى بعد انفساخه والالتحاق باصل العقد في بدلي العقد بخلاف البيع لان الثمن بدل يجب بالعقد

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴
كتاب الرهن
ترجمہ اور اصل عقد کے ساتھ الحاق ممکن نہیں ہے قرض کی جانب میں اس لئے کہ وہ نہ معقود علیہ اور نہ معقود بہ ہے بلکہ قرض کا وجوب رہن پر مقدم ہے اور ایسے ہی عقد رہن کے فسخ ہونے کے بعد باقی رہے گا اور اصل عقد کے ساتھ الحاق عقد کے دونوں بدلوں میں ہوتا ہے بخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ ثمن ایسا بدل ہے جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح یہ طرفین کی جانب سے امام ابو یوسف پر زبردست اعتراض ہے۔ ہوسکتا۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جناب والا! آپکا قیاس مذکور صحیح نہیں ہے اور باب رہن میں دین کا اضافہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیونکہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ الحاق معقود علیہ یا معقود بہ کا ہوسکتا ہے اور دین نہ معقود علیہ ہے اور نہ معقود بہ ہے اور باب بیع میں ثمن کا اضافہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ اس لئے لاحق ہو سکتا ہے کہ ثمن معقود ہے، معقود علیہ یعنی بیع اور معقود بہ یعنی ثمن اور قرض ان دونوں میں سے کچھ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر قرض معقود بہ ہوتا تو عقد رہن کی وجہ سے قرض واجب ہوتا ہے حالانکہ قرض بغیر عقد رہن کے واجب ہوتا ہے اور قرض کا وجوب پہلے ہو گیا اور عقد رہن بعد میں ہو جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر کسی وجہ سے عقد رہن فسخ ہو جائے تو قرض اب بھی باقی رہتا ہے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ معقود بہ نہیں ہے البتہ ثمن کا وجوب عقد بیع کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور اگر بیع فسخ ہو جائے تو ثمن کا وجوب بھی ختم ہو جاتا ہے لہذا آپکا قیاس ہی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
رہن میں زیادتی کا حکم
ثم اذا صحت الزيادة فى الرهن وتسمى هذه زيادة قصدية يقسم الدين على قيمة الاول يوم القبض وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت حتى لو كانت قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضها خمس مائة وقيمة الأول يوم القبض الفا والدين الفا يقسم الدين اثلاثا فى الزيادة ثلث الدين وفى الاصل ثلثا الدين اعتبار بقيمتهما في وقتى الاعتباراً وهذا لان الضمان فى كل واحد منهما يثبت بالقبض فتعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما وقت القبض ترجمہ پھر جب کہ مرہون میں زیادتی صحیح ہوگئی اور اس زیادتی کا نام قصدی زیادتی رکھا جاتا ہے تو قرض کو تقسیم کیا جائے گا قبضہ کے دن کی اول کی قیمت پر اور قبضہ کے دن کی زیادتی کی قیمت پر یہاں تک کہ اگر زیادتی کی قیمت اس پر قبضہ کے دن پانچ سو ہو اور اول کی قیمت قبضہ کے دن ہزار ہو اور قرض ہزار ہو تو قرض کو تین حصوں پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا زیادتی میں دین کا ثلث اور اصل میں دین کے دو ثلث بوقت اعتبار ان دونوں کی قیمت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ ضمان ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک میں قبضہ کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی قیمت قبضہ کے وقت کی معتبر ہوگی۔ تشریح ہلاکت اصل کی صورت میں جو مسئلہ گذرا ہے یہ مسئلہ بھی بالکل ایسا ہی ہے بس اتنا فرق ہے کہ وہاں بچہ کی قیمت یوم فکاک کی معتبر ہوتی ہے اور یہاں زیادتی کی وہ قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو قبضہ کے دن اس کی قیمت تھی، اگر چہ وہ بھی زیادتی ہے اور یہ بھی زیادتی ہے مگر دونوں میں فرق ہے وہ زیادتی غیر ارادی ہے اور یہ زیادتی ارادی اور قصدی ہے اس وجہ سے دونوں میں فرق کیا گیا ہے، نیز اصل اور یہ زیادتی دونوں قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہوتی ہیں تو دونوں میں قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور غیر ارادی زیادتی چھڑانے کی وجہ سے
Book of Pawn. ... Strength can be obtained, and just as there is possibility there, here also possibility exists. That is, initially in the pawn it is permissible for the value of the pawn to be equal to or less or more than the debt. So if after annexation this situation occurs, there is no harm. In any case, here there is need and possibility.
Proof of the two parties: And for them, and it is the qiyas, that increase in the debt necessitates commonality in the pawn, and that is not legislated according to us. And increase in the pawn necessitates commonality in the debt, and that is not a barrier to the validity of the pawn. Do you not see that if the pawnor pawned a slave for five hundred of the debt, it is valid even if the debt is a thousand, and this is commonality in the debt.
Translation: ... This is the proof of these two persons. The summary is that it has passed before that commonality within the pawn is not permissible, and if commonality occurs in the debt, it is not harmful. Increase in the pawn causes commonality in the debt, which is permissible. Increase in the debt causes commonality in the pawn, which is not permissible. Therefore we said that increase in the pawn is permissible and increase in the debt is not permissible.
Question: How does increase in debt necessitate commonality in the pawn? Answer: When a slave was pawned for ten rupees and then the mortgagee added another ten rupees, then half of the unspecified portion of the slave becomes the consideration for the first, and the other unspecified half becomes the consideration for the second, so commonality occurs in the slave. And if another goat is pawned along with a goat, then for example five out of ten is consideration for the first goat and the remaining five is consideration for the second goat, so here commonality does not occur in the pawn but commonality occurs in the debt, and commonality in the debt is not harmful. Then they clarify this with an example: Zayd took a thousand rupees from Khalid and pawned a slave for five hundred, this is permissible, even though here there is commonality in the debt, but commonality in the debt is not harmful, therefore it is permissible.
Objection from the two parties against Imam Abu Yusuf: And annexation to the original contract is not possible on the side of the debt because it is neither the object of contract nor the consideration. Rather, its obligation precedes the pawn, and similarly it remains after its dissolution. Annexation to the original contract applies to the two counter-values of the contract, unlike sale because the price is a consideration that becomes obligatory by the contract.
Translation: ... Annexation to the original contract is not possible on the side of the loan because it is neither the object of contract nor the consideration. Rather, the obligation of the loan precedes the pawn, and similarly it will remain after the dissolution of the pawn contract, and annexation to the original contract is done in the two counter-values of the contract, contrary to sale because the price is a consideration that becomes obligatory by the contract. Commentary: This is a strong objection from the two parties against Imam Abu Yusuf. Its summary is: Sir! Your mentioned qiyas is not correct, and in the chapter of pawn, increase in debt cannot be annexed to the original contract because annexation to the original contract can only be of the object of contract or the consideration, and the loan is neither the object of contract nor the consideration. In the chapter of sale, increase in the price can be annexed because the price is the consideration. The object of contract (sale) and the consideration (price)—the loan is neither of these. Because if the loan were the consideration, the loan would become obligatory by the pawn contract, whereas the loan is obligatory without the pawn contract, and its obligation occurred earlier, and the pawn contract occurs later. Similarly, if for some reason the pawn contract is dissolved, the loan still remains. So it is clear that it is not the consideration. Rather, the obligation of the price arises from the sale contract, and if the sale is dissolved, the obligation of the price also ends. Therefore, your qiyas itself is not correct.
Ruling on increase in pawn: Then when the increase in the pawn is valid, and this is called intentional increase, the debt is divided based on the value of the original on the day of possession and the value of the increase on the day it was taken into possession. So if the value of the increase on the day of possession is five hundred, and the value of the original on the day of possession is a thousand, and the debt is a thousand, the debt is divided into thirds: one third of the debt is on the increase and two thirds on the original, considering their values at the times of consideration. This is because the liability (daman) in each of them is established by possession, so the value of each at the time of possession is considered.
Translation: ... Then when the increase in the pawn is valid, and this increase is called intentional increase, the debt will be divided based on the value of the original on the day of possession and the value of the increase on the day of possession. So if the value of the increase at the time of its possession is five hundred, and the value of the original at the time of possession is a thousand, and the debt is a thousand, then the debt is divided into three parts: in the increase, one third of the debt, and in the original, two thirds of the debt, considering their values at the times of consideration. And this is because liability in each of them is established by possession, so the value of each at the time of possession is considered. Commentary: This is exactly like the issue that passed regarding the destruction of the original, with the difference that there the value of the young at the time of redemption is considered, and here the value of the increase that was at the time of possession will be considered. Even though that too is an increase and this is an increase, there is a difference: that increase is unintentional and this increase is intentional and deliberate, therefore a distinction is made between them. Also, both the original and this increase become liable due to possession, so the value at the time of possession is considered for both.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling statement from the Book of Pawn (Kitab al-Rahn) in Ashraf al-Hidaya, a commentary on al-Hidaya. The author first presents the proof of the two parties (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the permissibility of increasing the pawn versus increasing the debt. Their qiyas (analogy) states: increasing the debt causes shuyu' (commonality) in the pawn itself, which is not legislated according to the Hanafi school; whereas increasing the pawn causes shuyu' in the debt, which does not harm the validity of the pawn. They illustrate with an example: if a slave is pawned for five hundred while the debt is one thousand, the pawn is valid despite shuyu' in the debt. Then a question-answer section clarifies how increase in debt leads to shuyu' in the pawn (e.g., a slave pawned for ten rupees, then an additional ten rupees creates shuyu' in the slave's portions). Next, an objection is raised by the Sahibayn against Imam Abu Yusuf (though the text is ambiguous; the commentary explicitly states it is an objection from 'the two parties' against Abu Yusuf). The objection argues that annexation (ilhaq) of the additional debt to the original pawn contract is impossible because the debt is neither the object of contract (ma'qud 'alayh) nor the consideration (ma'qud bih). The debt's obligation precedes the pawn and survives its dissolution, unlike the price (thaman) in a sale, which is created by the contract and ceases upon its dissolution. Therefore, the qiyas presented by the opposing view is invalid. Finally, the passage gives the ruling on intentional increase (ziyada qasdiyya) in the pawn: once the increase is valid, the debt is apportioned proportionately based on the values of the original pawn and the increase at the time of possession. For example, if the original was worth 1000 and the increase 500 at possession, with a debt of 1000, the increase covers 1/3 of the debt and the original covers 2/3. This is because liability (daman) is established by possession, so values at that time are considered.

Key Terms
زيادة قصدية (ziyāda qaṣdiyya): Intentional increase; an additional item deliberately added to the pawn by the borrower.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability; the pawned item is a trust, and if destroyed, the lender's liability is based on value at possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a borrower intentionally adds a new item to an existing pawn, how is the debt apportioned?
A) The new item covers the entire debt first.
B) The debt is split equally between old and new items.
C) The debt is split proportionally based on values at the time of possession.
D) The debt is split based on values at the time of the original contract.

Key Takeaway
When an intentional increase is added to a pawn, the debt is divided proportionally according to the values of the original and the increase at the times the lender took possession of each.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
8 min
Critique of Abu Yusuf's Qiyas on Annexation of Increase in Rahn
Refutation of Abu Yusuf's analogy for annexing increase in rahn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why, according to the Hanafi critique, an increase in a pledged property cannot be annexed to the original rahn contract, and identify the key distinction from sale.

Core Idea
Debt preexists the pledge contract; price is created by sale—so annexation fails.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute where a view attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf—that an increase in the pledged property (ziyada) should be annexed to the original pledge contract by analogy to sale—is systematically refuted. The critique focuses on the fundamental nature of debt (dayn) in rahn versus price (thaman) in sale. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the structure of security contracts in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Read the passage and determine the specific legal issue: whether an increase in the pledged property can be annexed (ta'alluq) to the original rahn contract.
2
State the opposing qiyas
Identify the qiyas attributed to Abu Yusuf: that just as an increase in price is annexed in sale, an increase in the pledge should be annexed in rahn because the debt is a substitute (badal).
3
Understand the critique's core reasoning
Analyze the critique: the debt is neither ma'qud alayh nor ma'qud bihi of the rahn contract. The debt preexists the contract and survives its dissolution, whereas the price in sale is created by the contract and ceases if the contract is invalidated.
This is the key distinction that breaks the analogy.
4
Apply the distinction to the analogy
Compare the obligations: in sale, the price becomes obligatory due to the contract; in rahn, the debt is obligatory independently. Therefore, the increase cannot be annexed.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
Note that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the increase in the pledged property is not annexed to the original contract, following Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The critique presented in this passage is accepted as sound.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور اصل عقد کے ساتھ التحاق ممکن نہیں ہے قرض کی جانب میں اس لئے کہ وہ نہ معقود علیہ اور نہ معقود بہ ہے بلکہ قرض کا وجوب رہن پر مقدم ہے اور ایسے ہی عقد ر ہن کے فتح ہونے کے بعد باقی رہے گا اور اصل عقد کے ساتھ التحاق عقد کے دونوں بدلوں میں ہوتا ہے بخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ ثمن ایسا بدل ہے جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح یہ طرفین کی جانب سے امام ابو یوسف پر زبردست اعتراض ہے۔ ہوسکتا۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جناب والا! آپکا قیاس مذکور صحیح نہیں ہے اور باب رہن میں دین کا اضافہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیونکہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ التحاق معقود علیہ یا معقود بہ کا ہوسکتا ہے اور دین نہ معقود علیہ ہے اور نہ معقود بہ ہے اور باب بیع میں شمن کا اضافہ اصل عقد کے ساتھ اس لئے لاحق ہو سکتا ہے کہ ثمن معقود ہے، معقود علیہ یعنی بیع اور معقود بہ یعنی شمن اور قرض ان دونوں میں سے کچھ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر قرض معقود یہ ہوتا تو عقد رہن کی وجہ سے قرض واجب ہوتا ہے حالانکہ قرض بغیر عقد رہن کے واجب ہوتا ہے اور قرض کا وجوب پہلے ہو گیا اور عقد رہن بعد میں ہو جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر کسی وجہ سے عقد ربین فسخ ہو جائے تو قرض اب بھی باقی رہتا ہے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ معقود بہ نہیں ہے البتہ من کا وجوب عقد بیع کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور اگر بیع فسخ ہو جائے تو شمن کا وجوب بھی ختم ہو جاتا ہے لہذا آپکا قیاس ہی صحیح نہیں ہے۔
Translation: It is not possible for the debt to be annexed to the original contract, because it is neither the object of contract (ma'qud alayh) nor the subject matter (ma'qud bihi). Rather, the obligation of the debt precedes the pledge, and it will remain after the dissolution of the pledge contract. Annexation to the original contract occurs in both substitutes (badalayn) of the contract, unlike sale, because the price (thaman) is a substitute that becomes obligatory due to the contract. Explanation: This is a strong objection from both sides (the two disciples) against Imam Abu Yusuf. It may be summarized as: O respected one! Your mentioned analogy (qiyas) is not correct. In the chapter of rahn, the increase of the debt cannot be attached to the original contract because attachment to the original contract can only be of the object of contract (ma'qud alayh) or the subject matter (ma'qud bihi). The debt is neither the object of contract nor the subject matter. In the chapter of sale, the increase of the price can be attached to the original contract because the price is the subject matter (ma'qud). The object of contract is the sale and the subject matter is the price. The debt is nothing of these two. If the debt were the subject matter, it would be obligatory due to the pledge contract, whereas the debt is obligatory without the pledge contract, and its obligation occurs first, and the pledge contract comes thereafter. Similarly, if the pledge contract is rescinded for some reason, the debt still remains. Thus it is clear that it is not the subject matter. However, the obligation of the price occurs due to the sale contract, and if the sale is rescinded, the obligation of the price also ceases. Hence your analogy is not correct.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute: a critique of Imam Abu Yusuf's qiyas that the increase in the pledged property (ziyada) can be annexed to the original rahn contract, similar to how an increase in the price (thaman) is annexed in a sale contract. The criticism argues that annexation (ta'alluq) to a contract only applies to the two substitutes (badalayn): the subject matter (ma'qud bihi) and the object of contract (ma'qud alayh). In sale, the price (thaman) is a substitute that becomes obligatory by the contract, so an increase in price can be annexed to the sale. But in rahn, the debt (dayn) is not a substitute created by the contract; rather, the debt preexists the pledge and survives the termination of the contract. Therefore, an increase in the pledged property cannot be annexed to the original pledge contract. The commentator explains that this is a powerful objection raised by the two scholars (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) against some view, or perhaps against a third party. The conclusion: Abu Yusuf's qiyas is invalid. The commentator then provides a detailed logical breakdown: if debt were ma'qud bihi, it would be created by the contract, but it is not; it continues after contract dissolution. In contrast, the price in sale is created by the contract and ceases if the sale is invalidated. Thus the analogy fails.

Key Terms
معقود علیہ (ma'qud alayh): The object of the contract; that which is sold or transferred. In this context, it refers to the thing being sold in a sale contract.
معقود بہ (ma'qud bihi): The subject matter or consideration that becomes obligatory by the contract. In sale, it is the price (thaman); in rahn, the debt is not considered ma'qud bihi because it preexists.
بدل (badal): Substitute; the consideration exchanged in a contract. In sale, the price is a badal; in rahn, the debt is not a badal created by the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why, according to the critique against Abu Yusuf, can an increase in a pledge (rahn) not be annexed to the original contract, unlike an increase in price in a sale?
A) Because the debt in rahn is created by the pledge contract.
B) Because the debt preexists the pledge contract and remains after its dissolution.
C) Because the pledged property is not a valid subject matter.
D) Because the increase is not known at the time of contract.

Key Takeaway
An increase in the pledged property cannot be annexed to the original rahn contract because the debt is not a substitute created by the contract; it preexists and survives independently.

Intentional Increase in Pledge and Division of Debt
Ruling on intentional increase in pledge and debt division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentional increase in a pledge and calculate the division of debt based on values at the time of possession.

Core Idea
Intentional increase in a pledge is valid; debt divides proportionally by values at possession, not at redemption.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on a pledgor voluntarily adding extra property to an existing pledge. The school has a detailed method for dividing the debt between the original and the addition based on their values at the time each was taken into possession. We will also contrast this with the rule for unintentional increase, like the birth of a child from a pledged animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is intentional increase (ziyāda qasdiyya) in a pledge. The Hanafi ruling: it is valid (sahih) and the debt is divided proportionally based on values at the time of possession.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage states: 'This is because liability (ḍamān) is established for each of them by possession.' Possession is the basis for liability, so valuation at possession is used.
The proof is a causal reasoning (talil).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The causal link: possession creates liability, so the moment of possession is when the value matters. For intentional increase, each item is possessed at a different time, so valued at its own possession time.
This contrasts with unintentional increase, where liability arises from redemption.
4
Apply to a numerical example
If original value at possession = 1000, increase value at possession = 500, debt = 1000. Then debt is divided: 2/3 (666.67) on original, 1/3 (333.33) on increase.
The fraction is based on proportionate values at possession.
5
Distinguish from unintentional increase
Unintentional increase (e.g., offspring) is valued at redemption time, not possession. This is because the offspring is an accessory intended for redemption, not separately pledged.
The key difference: intentional vs. unintentional changes the valuation time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اذا صحت الزيادة فى الرهن وتسمى هذه زيادة قصدية يقسم الدين على قيمة الاول يوم القبض وعلى قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضت حتى لو كانت قيمة الزيادة يوم قبضها خمس مائة وقيمة الأول يوم القبض الفا والدين الفايقسم الدين اثلاثا فى الزيادة ثلث الدين وفى الاصل ثلثا الدين اعتبار بقيمتهما في وقتى الاعتباراً وهذا لان الضمان فى كل واحد منهما يثبت بالقبض فتعتبر قيمة كل واحد منهما وقت القبض ترجمہ پھر جب کہ مرہون میں زیادتی صحیح ہوگئی اور اس زیادتی کا نام قصدی زیادتی رکھا جاتا ہے تو قرض کو تقسیم کیا جائے گا قبضہ کے دن کی اول کی قیمت پر اور قبضہ کے دن کی زیادتی کی قیمت پر یہاں تک کہ اگر زیادتی کی قیمت اس پر قبضہ کے دن پانچ سو ہو اور اول کی قیمت قبضہ کے دن ہزار ہو اور قرض ہزار ہو تو قرض کو تین حصوں پر تقسیم کیا جائے گا زیادتی میں دین کا تکث اور اصل میں دین کے دو ثلث بوقت اعتبار ان دونوں کی قیمت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ ضمان ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک میں قبضہ کی وجہ سے ثابت ہوتا ہے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی قیمت قبضہ کے وقت کی معتبر ہوگی۔ تشریح ہلاکت اصل کی صورت میں جو مسئلہ گذرا ہے یہ مسئلہ بھی بالکل ایسا ہی ہے بس اتنا فرق ہے کہ وہاں بچہ کی قیمت یوم فکاک کی معتبر ہوتی ہے اور یہاں زیادتی کی وہ قیمت معتبر ہوگی جو قبضہ کے دن اس کی قیمت تھی، اگر چہ وہ بھی زیادتی ہے اور یہ بھی زیادتی ہے مگر دونوں میں فرق ہے وہ زیادتی غیر ارادی ہے اور یہ زیادتی ارادی اور قصدی ہے اس وجہ سے دونوں میں فرق کیا گیا ہے، نیز اصل اور یہ زیادتی دونوں قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہوتی ہیں تو دونوں میں قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا اور غیر ارادی زیادتی چھڑانے کی وجہ سے مقصود بنتی ہے تو اس میں یوم فکاک کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی۔ الہذا اگر زید نے ہزار روپے خالد سے قرض لئے اور ایک غلام رہن رکھا جس کی قیمت ہزار روپے ہے پھر ایک غلام اور رہن رکھ دیا اسی ہزار کے بدلہ میں تو یہ جائز ہے۔ تو حسب تفصیل مذکور ۶۶۶ راول کے حصہ میں آئے اور ۳۳۳ روپے زیادتی کے حصہ میں آئے اب اگر اول ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا حصہ ہو جائے گا اور اگر ثانی ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کے حصہ کا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ غیر ارادی زیادتی اس کے مقصود ہونے کی وجہ سے یوم نکاک کی قیمت معتبر ہوتی ہے
When the increase in the pledge is valid, and this is called intentional increase (ziyāda qasdiyya), the debt is divided according to the value of the first (original) on the day of possession and according to the value of the increase on the day it was taken. So if the value of the increase on the day of taking was five hundred, and the value of the first on the day of possession was one thousand, and the debt is one thousand, then the debt is divided into thirds: one third of the debt is on the increase, and two thirds are on the original, considering their values at the times of consideration. This is because liability (ḍamān) is established for each of them by possession, so the value of each at the time of possession is considered. Urdu translation: Then when the increase in the pledge is valid, and this increase is called intentional increase, the debt will be divided based on the value of the first on the day of possession and the value of the increase on the day of possession. For example, if the value of the increase on the day of its possession is five hundred, and the value of the first on the day of possession is one thousand, and the debt is one thousand, then the debt is divided into three parts: one third of the debt is on the increase, and two thirds are on the original, considering their values at the time of consideration. This is because liability for each of them is established by possession, so the value of each at the time of possession is considered. Explanation: The previous issue concerning destruction of the original is very similar, with the difference that there the value of the child at the time of redemption (yawm al-fakāk) is considered, while here the value of the increase at the time of possession is considered. Although both are increases, there is a difference: that increase is unintentional, while this increase is intentional and volitional. For this reason, the two are distinguished. Also, the original and this increase are both liable (maḍmūn) due to possession, so the value at the time of possession is considered. The unintentional increase, because it is intended for redemption, the value at the time of redemption is considered. Thus, if Zayd borrowed one thousand rupees from Khalid and pledged one slave worth one thousand rupees, then added another slave as a pledge for the same thousand, it is permissible. According to the mentioned detail, 666.67 rupees fall to the share of the first, and 333.33 rupees to the share of the increase. If the first is destroyed, that share is lost; if the second is destroyed, that share of the debt is cancelled. For unintentional increase, because it is intended, the value at the time of redemption is considered.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on intentional increase (ziyāda qasdiyya) in a pledge. When a pledgor voluntarily adds another property to an existing pledge for the same debt, the debt is divided proportionally between the original and the addition based on their values at the time they were taken into possession (qabḍ). The reason is that the liability (ḍamān) for each is established by possession, so the value at the time of possession is the relevant standard. The commentator clarifies the distinction between this intentional increase and the unintentional increase (like a child born to a pledged female slave). In the case of unintentional increase, the value at the time of redemption (yawm al-fakāk) is considered, because the child is an accessory intended for redemption. But here, since the pledgor deliberately adds property, the time of possession is used. The example illustrates: if the original pledged item is worth 1000, the added item is worth 500, and the debt is 1000, then 2/3 of the debt (666.67) is secured by the original, and 1/3 (333.33) by the addition. If either is destroyed, the corresponding portion of the debt is affected accordingly.

Key Terms
زیادہ قصدی (ziyāda qasdiyya): An intentional increase voluntarily added by the pledgor to the existing pledge for the same debt.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or responsibility; here meaning that the pledged property is liable to satisfy the debt if the pledgor defaults.
قبض (qabḍ): Possession; taking physical control of the pledged property by the creditor (murtahin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for dividing the debt between the original pledge and an intentional increase?
A) The values at the time of the contract.
B) The values at the time of redemption (yawm al-fakāk).
C) The values at the time of possession (qabḍ) of each.
D) The values at the time the debt falls due.

Key Takeaway
Intentional increase in a pledge is valid, and the debt is divided proportionally based on the values of each item at the time of possession.

Combined Unintentional and Intentional Increase in Pledge (Rahn)
Ruling on combined increases in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for dividing debt when an intentional increase is added to a pledged female slave that has given birth, and state the consequence of the child's death on the additional pledge.

Core Idea
The pledgor's specification determines whether an additional pledge follows the child or the mother; tab'iyya governs its fate.

This passage from a classical Hanafi fiqh text examines a nuanced scenario where a pledged female slave gives birth (unintentional increase) and the pledgor intentionally adds another slave as a pledge (intentional increase). The ruling hinges on how the pledgor specifies the addition—whether with the child or with the mother. The division of the debt and the fate of the additional slave if the child dies illustrate key principles of rahn (pledge) and subordination (tab'iyya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of increase
First, recognize that the child born to a pledged female slave is an unintentional increase (ziyāda ghayr qasdiyya), while the additional slave added by the pledgor is an intentional increase (ziyāda qasdiyya).
Unintentional increase is valued at redemption (yawm al-fakāk); intentional increase is valued at possession.
2
Understand the pledgor's specification
The pledgor may add the intentional increase together with the child (as in the main scenario) or together with the mother. The ruling follows the pledgor's explicit intention.
If added with the child, the additional slave is pledged only with the child. If added with the mother, it is pledged with the mother.
3
Apply the division of debt
First divide the total debt between the mother and the original child based on their values. Then divide the child's share between the child and the additional slave (if added with the child). If added with the mother, the debt is divided between mother and child after considering the intentional increase.
In the example: mother value 1000, child value 1000, debt 1000 → mother 500, child 500. Adding slave with child (value 1000) → child's 500 split 250 each.
4
Analyze the effect of the child's death
If the child dies after the addition, it perishes without liability because it is an unintentional increase not yet valued at redemption. The additional slave, being subordinate (tābiʿ) to the child, also ceases to be a pledge. The mother becomes the sole security for the full debt.
This illustrates the principle of tab'iyya: a subordinate follows the principal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مطلب یہ ہوا کہ قرض میں سے پانچ سو روپے کا عوض باندی ہے اور ۲۵۰ کا عوض بچہ ہے اور ۰ ۲۵ کا عوض غلام ہے۔ لیکن جب غلام کا اضافہ کر دیا تو بچہ (پو ) مر گیا تو چونکہ یہ ابھی مضمون نہیں بنا ہے اس لئے وہ بغیر حکم میں بچہ کے تابع ہے، لہذا اب پورے قرض کا بدل باندی ہوگی ، یہاں اصل یہی بات سمجھانی تھی باقی بات ہم نے آسانی کی غرض سے عرض کر دی ہے۔
When the pledged female slave gives birth to a child, then the pledgor adds a slave together with the child, each valued at one thousand, then the slave is a pledge only with the child. The amount of debt on the child is divided between the child and the additional slave, because he made the increase with the child, not with the mother. If the increase was with the mother, the debt would be divided upon the value of the mother on the day of the contract and upon the value of the increase on the day of possession. Then whatever part falls to the mother is divided between her and her child, because the increase entered upon the mother. Urdu translation: And when the pledged female slave gives birth to a child, then the pledgor adds a slave together with the child, each valued at one thousand, then the slave is a pledge only with the child. The amount of debt that falls to the child's share is divided between the child and the additional slave, because the pledgor added the slave with the child, not with the mother. If the increase was with the mother, the debt would be divided based on the value of the mother on the day of the contract and on the value of the increase on the day of possession. Then whatever amount falls to the mother's share is divided between her and her child, because the increase entered upon the mother. Explanation: It has passed earlier that for unintentional increase (child), due to it being intended, the value at the time of redemption (yawm al-fakāk) is considered. Now listen. Zayd borrowed one thousand rupees from Khalid and pledged a female slave worth one thousand rupees, it is valid. Then the female slave gave birth to a child at the mortgagee's side, and incidentally the child's value is also one thousand, so it becomes a pledge as well. Zayd then added a slave as an increase to the pledge, its value also one thousand. But Zayd specifically added this slave with the child, saying, 'Take this slave as a pledge with the child.' So in the mentioned scenario, the additional slave is a pledge only with the child. The one thousand rupee debt, which was divided equally between the mother and child because their values are equal, now the child's portion is further divided equally between the child and the slave. Thus the result is: 500 rupees' security from the slave-girl, 250 from the child, and 250 from the additional slave. But if the child dies after the addition of the slave, since the child was not yet liable (maḍmūn) in the sense of being a separate pledge? Actually, the child is unintentional increase and its valuation at redemption hasn't occurred yet; it is still subject to the rule of unintentional increase. When the child dies, it perishes without liability because it was not yet secured? The commentary says: because the child was not yet made liable (maḍmūn), it perishes without any compensation, i.e., as if it never existed. And since the slave is subordinate (tābiʿ) to the child, and the principal (child) has exited the pledge, the subordinate (additional slave) also exits. The increase becomes void because it is subordinate to the child in ruling. Hence the full debt is now secured by the slave-girl only. The main point to understand was this; the rest has been explained for ease.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage deals with a complex scenario: a pledged female slave gives birth (unintentional increase), and then the pledgor intentionally adds a slave specifically as an increase alongside the child (not the mother). The ruling depends on whether the intentional increase is added together with the mother or with the child. If added with the child, the additional slave is pledged only with the child. The debt is first divided between the mother and the original child based on their values (here equal, so 500 each). Then the child's share (500) is divided between the child and the additional slave (250 each). If the child dies, since it was an unintentional increase not yet valued at redemption, it perishes without affecting the mother's liability. The additional slave, being subordinate to the child, also ceases to be a pledge. The commentator emphasizes the distinction between intentional and unintentional increases and how their interaction modifies the division of debt. The key principle: the ruling follows the specific intention of the pledgor (whether increase is with mother or child).

Key Terms
زیادہ غیر قصدی (ziyāda ghayr qasdiyya): Unintentional increase; for example, a child born to a pledged female slave. The value is considered at the time of redemption (yawm al-fakāk).
تبعی (tab'iyya): Subordination; the additional slave is subordinate to the child. If the child ceases to be a pledge, the subordinate also ceases.
مضمون (maḍmūn): Liable, guaranteed; the child is said to be not yet 'maḍmūn' because its valuation at redemption had not occurred, so it perishes without liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling, if a pledged female slave gives birth and the pledgor adds a slave specifically with the child, what happens to the additional slave if the child dies before the debt is repaid?
A) The additional slave remains pledged for the child's share of the debt.
B) The additional slave is released from the pledge because it was subordinate to the child.
C) The additional slave becomes pledged with the mother instead.
D) The debt is reduced by the value of the child and the additional slave.

Key Takeaway
The pledgor's specification in adding an intentional increase to a pledged item determines the division of debt, and the principle of subordination (tab'iyya) causes the additional item to follow the fate of the item it was added to.

Valuation of Involuntary Increase and Addition of a Slave in Rahn
Ruling with proof on valuation of increase and addition in pawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that involuntary increase (child) is valued at the day of redemption, and apply the distribution rules when a pledgor adds a slave specifically with the child or with the mother.

Core Idea
Involuntary increase is valued at redemption; the pledgor's intent in adding a slave determines the distribution of debt.

This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir, with its Urdu commentary, establishes the Hanafi position on how to value increase in a pawned property and how to distribute the debt when additional property is pledged. The key distinction is between involuntary increase (e.g., a child born to a slave-girl) valued at redemption, and voluntary increase (e.g., adding another slave) valued at possession. The pledgor's specification of adding the slave 'with the child' or 'with the mother' determines the allocation of debt and the consequences of loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of increase
Determine if the increase is involuntary (child) or voluntary (added slave). Involuntary increase is automatically included but valued at redemption; voluntary increase is valued at possession.
Involuntary increase is treated as 'intended' to secure the debt, hence valuation at redemption reflects its purpose.
2
State the valuation time
Involuntary increase is valued at yawm al-fikak (day of redemption); voluntary increase at yawm al-qabd (day of possession). This is based on the Hanafi principle that what is intended to secure the debt is valued at the time of redemption.
3
Analyze the addition scenario
When the pledgor adds a slave 'with the child', the added slave is paired only with the child in securing the debt; the debt on the child is divided between child and added slave proportionally. When added 'with the mother', the debt is first divided between mother (at contract value) and added slave (at possession value), then the mother's share is further divided with her child.
The difference in valuation for the mother (contract) and added slave (possession) reflects the distinction between original pledge and voluntary addition.
4
Consider the effect of loss
If the child dies after addition (with the child case), since the child's liability was not guaranteed (madhmun), the child is deemed never to have been part of the pledge, and the added slave, being subordinate, also leaves the pledge, so the entire debt falls on the mother. If the mother dies (with the mother case), her share of debt is canceled (because the mortgagee implicitly guarantees it), but the added slave and child's shares remain.
The subordination relationship depends on the pledgor's specification: the added slave is subordinate to the child when added 'with the child', but independent when added 'with the mother'.

اور اگر راہن نے غلام کا اضافہ خصوصاً ماں کے ساتھ کیا ہے تو اب کے نوعیت کچھ اور ہو جائے گی پورا قرض ماں اور غلام پر حسب سابق تقسیم ہوگا پھر ماں کا حصہ حسب تفصیل سابق ماں اور بچہ پر تقسیم ہو گا یعنی بچہ ماں کے حصہ میں داخل ہوگا اور اگر زیادتی کے بعد ماں مر جائے تو ماں کے حصہ میں جو کچھ آیا تھا اتنا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا ، اور غلام اور بچہ کے حصہ میں جو آیا تھا اتنا قرض مرتہن کا راہن پر برقرار رہیگا۔
کیونکہ ماں کے ہلاک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اس کے حصہ کا ضمان مرتہن پر پڑ چکا ہے لہذا زیادتی (غلام ) کا حکم باطل نہ ہو گا بخلاف پہلی صورت کے جس میں غلام بچہ کے تابع تھا، اور اگر اس صورت میں زیادتی کے بعد بچہ مر جائے تو مفت مریگا اور پورا قرض ام اور غلام کا بدل ہوگا گویا کہ بغیر بچہ کے راہن نے غلام کا اضافہ کیا ہے۔
It becomes intended, so the value on the day of redemption is considered. Hence if Zayd borrowed one thousand rupees from Khalid and pawned a slave worth one thousand rupees, then pawned another slave for the same thousand, it is valid. According to the mentioned detail, 666 [rupees] come to the first's share and 333 rupees come to the increase's share. If the first perishes, its share [of debt] is canceled; if the second perishes, the debt on its share is canceled. Involuntary increase, due to its being intended, is valued at the day of redemption. And if the pawned [slave-girl] gave birth to a child, then the pledgor added a slave with the child, each worth one thousand, then the slave is a pledge specifically with the child. The portion of debt that is on the child is divided between the child and the added slave, because he made the increase with the child, not with the mother. If the increase was with the mother, the debt is divided based on the mother's value on the day of contract and the value of the increase on the day of possession; whatever falls on the mother is divided between her and her child, because the increase entered upon the mother. Explanation: It has passed previously that involuntary increase (in the child, due to its being intended) is valued at the day of redemption. Now listen: Zayd borrowed one thousand rupees from Khalid and pawned a slave-girl worth one thousand rupees; it is valid. Then this slave-girl gave birth at the mortgagee's, and coincidentally the child is also worth one thousand, so it also becomes pledged. Zayd added another slave worth one thousand, but Zayd made the addition specifically with the child, i.e., he said 'I pawn this slave with the child.' So in this case, the added slave is a pledge only with the child. The one thousand rupee debt, due to equal value, is half on the mother and half on the child. The child's half is then divided half between the child and the slave, since their values are equal. So the meaning is: of the debt, five hundred rupees are secured by the slave-girl, 250 by the child, and 250 by the added slave. But if after adding the slave, the child dies, since it has not become a liability (madhmun), it perishes without compensation, as if it never existed. Since the slave is subordinate to it, and the principal has left the pledge, the subordinate (the added slave) also leaves the pledge, and the increase becomes void because it is subordinate in ruling to the child. Hence the entire debt is now secured by the slave-girl alone. This was the main point; the rest we have stated for ease. And if the pledgor added the slave specifically with the mother, then the situation differs. The entire debt is divided between the mother and the slave as before. Then the mother's share is divided between her and the child as before, i.e., the child enters into the mother's share. If after the increase the mother dies, the portion of debt that fell on the mother is canceled, and the portion on the slave and child remains due from the pledgor to the mortgagee. Because due to the mother's death, the liability for her share falls upon the mortgagee, so the ruling of the increase (the slave) is not void, unlike the first case where the slave was subordinate to the child. And if in this case the child dies after the increase, it perishes without compensation, and the entire debt is secured by the mother and the slave, as if the pledgor added the slave without the child.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the valuation of increases in a pawned property and the effect of adding a third property specifically with either the mother or the child. The text first establishes that involuntary increase (such as a child born to a pawned slave-girl) is valued at the time of redemption (yawm al-fikak) because it is intended to secure the debt. It then presents a scenario: Zayd borrows 1000 rupees and pawns a slave worth 1000. He later pawns another slave for the same debt; this is valid. The debt is distributed proportionally based on values. If the first slave perishes, the debt secured by it is canceled; if the second perishes, the debt allocated to it is canceled. The core Arabic text (from al-Jami' al-Saghir) then addresses a more specific case: a pawned slave-girl gives birth, and the pledgor adds another slave. If the addition is specifically with the child ('with the child' means the pledgor says 'I add this slave as a pledge together with the child'), then the added slave becomes a pledge only with the child, not the mother. The debt on the child is divided between the child and the added slave proportionally. If the addition is with the mother, then the debt is divided between mother and the added slave based on their values at different times (mother at contract, added slave at possession), and then the mother's share is further divided between her and her child. The Urdu commentary elaborates with examples and explains the consequences of death: if the child dies after addition, since the child's liability was not fully established (it was a non-voluntary increase that became a pledge automatically), the added slave, being subordinate to the child, also falls out of pledge, and the entire debt reverts to the mother. If the mother dies, her share is canceled (since the mortgagee implicitly guarantees it), but the added slave's share remains. The passage highlights the Hanafi principle that the intention of the pledgor in the addition determines the distribution, and the subordinate follows the principal in liability.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract of pledge or mortgage where property is given as security for a debt.
زيادة (ziyādah): Increase or addition to the pledged property, either involuntary (e.g., child) or voluntary (e.g., adding another slave).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, involuntary increase in pawn is valued at redemption, and the pledgor's specification in adding additional property determines the distribution and effect of loss.

Replacement of a Pawned Slave: Condition of Return
Ruling on pawn replacement with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on replacing a pawned item with another and apply the condition that the original must be returned for substitution to take effect.

Core Idea
A replacement pawn does not take effect until the original is physically returned; until then, the substitute is a trust.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir on the substitution of a pawned slave. The key principle is that the mortgagee's liability (daman) over the original pledge continues until the original is returned, preventing the new item from becoming a pledge until that moment. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the rules of rahn in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction
The pledgor (rahn) has already pawned a slave worth 1000. He then gives another slave of equal value to the mortgagee (murtahin) intending to replace the first.
The second slave is given 'in place of the first' (makana al-awwal).
2
Determine the immediate legal status
Until the mortgagee physically returns the original slave to the pledgor, the original remains a pledge (rahn), and the second slave is a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hands.
The mortgagee is liable for the original as a pledge, but not for the second unless negligent.
3
Analyse the reasoning
The original entered the mortgagee's liability (daman) through possession and the existence of the debt. Both possession and debt remain, so liability cannot cease until possession is dissolved by returning the original.
The parties only agreed to have one item in liability at a time, not both.
4
Apply the consequences
If the original perishes while in the mortgagee's possession, the debt is cancelled (since it was in his daman). If the second perishes, it is lost without compensation (as a trust).
This shows the practical difference between daman and amanah.
5
Summarise the condition for effective substitution
Substitution is not effective by mere agreement or delivery of the new item; the original must be returned first. Only then does the second enter into the mortgagee's liability.
This condition is specific to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
راہن نے ایسا غلام رکھا جس کی قیمت ہزار ہے پھر اس کی جگہ دوسرا غلام اتنی ہی قیمت کا رکھا تو مرتہن جب تک پہلے کو لوٹا نہ دے پہلا رہن ہے اور دوسرا غلام امانت ہے
قال فان رهن عبدا يساوى الفا بالف ثم اعطاه عبداً آخر قيمته الف رهنا مكان الاول فالاول رهن حتى يرده الى الراهن والمرتهن فى الأخرامين حتى يجعله مكان الاول لان الاول انما دخل في ضمانه بالقبض والدين وهما باقيان فلا يخرج عن الضمان الابنقض القبض مادام الدين باقيا واذا بقى الاول في ضمانه لا يدخل الثانى فى ضمانه لانهما رضيا بدخول احدهما فيه لابدخولهما فاذا رد الاول دخل الثاني في ضمانه
ترجمہ 4 مہ نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ پس اگر رہن رکھا ایسا غلام جو ہزار کے برابر ہے ہزار کے بدلہ میں پھر راہن نے مرتہن کو دوسرا غلام دیا بطور ر ہن کے جس کی قیمت ہزار ہے اول کی جگہ تو اول رہن رہے گا یہاں تک کہ مرتہن اس کو راہن کو لوٹا دے اور مرتہن دوسرے غلام کے بدلہ میں امین ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کو اول کی جگہ کر ہے اس لئے پہلا غلام مرتہن کے ضمان میں قبضہ اور قرض کی وجہ سے داخل ہوا تھا اور یہ دونوں چیزیں باقی ہیں تو وہ ضمان سے خارج نہ ہوگا مگر قبضہ کو توڑنے کے ساتھ جب تک کہ قرض باقی ہے اور پھر جب اول غلام مرتہن کے زیر ضمان داخل ہے تو دوسرا اس کے ضمان میں داخل نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں ( راہن مرتہن ) ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے ضمان میں داخل ہونے پر راضی ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ ان دونوں کے دخول سے پس جب مرتہن نے اول کو واپس کر دیا تو دوسرا اس کے ضمان میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح زید نے خالد سے ہزار روپے قرض لئے اور ہزار روپے کی قیمت کا ایک غلام خالد کے پاس رہن رکھ دیا ، زید کے پاس ایک نے خالد سے ہزار لئے اور کی دیا کے پاس غلام اور ہے اس کی قیمت بھی ہزار روپے ہے اب زید چاہتا ہے کہ پہلا غلام خالد کے پاس سے لیلوں اور یہ دوسرا اس کی جگہ رکھدوں تو یہ جائز ہے لہذا کھدیا اور ابھی خالد نے پہلا غلام واپس نہیں کیا تھا تو جب تک وہ واپس نہ ہو گا جب تک اول ہی کو مرہون شمار کیا جائے گا لہذا اگر اس صورت میں اول ہلاک ہو جائے تو قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اگر ثانی ہلاک ہو تو چونکہ امانت ہے اس لئے مفت ہلاک ہو گا وجہ اس
The pledgor pawned a slave worth one thousand, then replaced it with another slave of equal value. As long as the mortgagee does not return the first, the first remains a pledge and the second slave is a trust. He (Imam Muhammad) said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If he pawned a slave worth one thousand for one thousand, then gave another slave worth one thousand as a pledge in place of the first, the first remains a pledge until he returns it to the pledgor, and the mortgagee is a trustee for the second until he makes it take the place of the first. Because the first entered into his liability by possession and debt, and both remain, so it does not leave liability except by dissolving possession as long as the debt remains. And when the first remains in his liability, the second does not enter into his liability because both (the pledgor and mortgagee) agreed on the entry of one of them, not both. So when he returns the first, the second enters into his liability. Explanation: Zayd borrowed one thousand rupees from Khalid and pawned a slave worth one thousand with him. Zayd has another slave also worth one thousand. Now Zayd wants to take the first slave from Khalid and put this second in its place; this is permissible. So he said this, but Khalid has not yet returned the first slave. As long as he does not return it, the first is considered the pledged property. So if in this case the first perishes, the debt is canceled; if the second perishes, since it is a trust, it perishes without compensation. The reason is...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on replacing a pawned item with another of equal value. The text is from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad, a core book of the Zahir al-Riwayah. The ruling: If a pledgor pawns a slave worth 1000 for a debt of 1000, then gives another slave of equal value to the mortgagee with the intention of replacing the first, the first slave remains a pledge until the mortgagee physically returns it to the pledgor. The second slave, in the meantime, is held as a trust (amanah) by the mortgagee, meaning the mortgagee is not liable for its destruction unless by negligence. The reason given is that the first slave entered into the mortgagee's liability (daman) through possession and the debt; both the possession and the debt continue. Therefore, the first slave cannot leave liability except by ending possession (i.e., returning it). As long as the first is still in liability, the second cannot enter into liability because both parties agreed to only one being in liability at a time. Once the first is returned, the second automatically becomes a pledge with full liability. The Urdu commentary illustrates with an example: Zayd owes Khalid 1000 and has pawned a slave worth 1000. Zayd wants to replace it with another slave of equal value. If Zayd gives the new slave but Khalid hasn't returned the old one, the old one is still the pledge. If the old slave dies, the debt is canceled (because it was in liability). If the new slave dies, it is lost without compensation to the mortgagee, as it was merely a trust. The passage emphasizes that substitution requires actual return of the original to take effect.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or surety; here it refers to the mortgagee's liability to return the pledged property or compensate for its loss if in his possession as a pledge.
أمانة (amānah): Trust; property held without liability for loss unless caused by negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pledgor gives a mortgagee a new slave to replace an existing pawned slave, but the mortgagee does not return the original, what is the status of the original slave?
A) It is no longer a pledge; the new slave becomes the pledge.
B) It remains a pledge until the mortgagee returns it.
C) Both slaves become pledges jointly.
D) The mortgagee can choose which to keep as pledge.

Key Takeaway
A replacement pledge only becomes effective when the original is physically returned; before that, the new item is held in trust without liability.
