Adding a Slave Specifically with the Mother in Pledge
Ruling on adding a slave specifically with a pregnant mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distribution of debt when a pledgor adds a slave specifically with a pregnant mother slave, and explain the consequences of the mother's or child's death.

Core Idea
Specification changes how debt is distributed among collaterals and who bears the loss when a collateral perishes.

When a pledgor adds an additional item to a pledge, the way the debt is distributed depends on how the addition is specified. This lesson examines a case where a slave is added specifically with a pregnant mother slave. The ruling shows how the specification affects the division of debt and the liability when the mother or child dies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the addition and its specification
Note that the slave is added specifically with the mother (not generally or subordinate to the child). This sets the distribution rule.
The word 'خصوصاً' (specifically) in the Arabic denotes a clear specification that alters the outcome.
2
Trace the initial distribution
The entire debt is divided between mother and slave based on their values. Then the mother's share is further divided between the mother and the unborn child (the child is part of the mother's share).
The child enters into the mother's share as per the previous detail.
3
Analyze the effect of the mother's death
If the mother dies, the debt allocated to her share is cancelled (the mortgagee bears the loss). The remaining debt on the slave and child continues to be owed by the pledgor.
The guarantee of the mother's share falls on the mortgagee because the collateral perished in his possession.
4
Analyze the effect of the child's death
If the child dies, it is gratuitous (no liability). The debt is then owed entirely by mother and slave, as if the child never existed.
The child's death does not affect the validity of the addition.
5
Contrast with the case of subordinate addition
The passage references a previous case where the slave was added as subordinate to the child; there the outcome differs. Understanding this contrast is key to grasping the importance of specification.
The previous case likely had the slave as tābi‘ (subordinate) to the child, leading to different distribution upon death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر راہن نے غلام کا اضافہ خصوصاً ماں کے ساتھ کیا ہے تو اب کے نوعیت کچھ اور ہو جائے گی پورا قرض ماں اور غلام پر حسب سابق تقسیم ہوگا پھر ماں کا حصہ حسب تفصیل سابق ماں اور بچہ پر تقسیم ہو گا یعنی بچہ ماں کے حصہ میں داخل ہوگا اور اگر زیادتی کے بعد ماں مر جائے تو ماں کے حصہ میں جو کچھ آیا تھا اتنا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا ، اور غلام اور بچہ کے حصہ میں جو آیا تھا اتنا قرض مرتہن کا راہن پر برقرار رہیگا۔ کیونکہ ماں کے ہلاک ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اس کے حصہ کا ضمان مرتہن پر پڑ چکا ہے لہذا زیادتی (غلام ) کا حکم باطل نہ ہو گا بخلاف پہلی صورت کے جس میں غلام بچہ کے تابع تھا، اور اگر اس صورت میں زیادتی کے بعد بچہ مر جائے تو مفت مریگا اور پورا قرض ام اور غلام کا بدل ہوگا گویا کہ بغیر بچہ کے راہن نے غلام کا اضافہ کیا ہے۔
And if the pledgor has added a slave specifically with the mother, then now the nature becomes something else. The entire debt will be divided between the mother and the slave as before. Then the mother's share will be divided between the mother and the child according to the previous detail, i.e., the child enters into the mother's share. And if after the addition the mother dies, then whatever came into the mother's share is cancelled from the debt, and whatever came into the share of the slave and the child remains as the mortgagee's debt on the pledgor. Because due to the mother's death, the guarantee of her share has fallen upon the mortgagee, so the ruling of the addition (the slave) does not become void, unlike the first case where the slave was subordinate to the child. And if in this case after the addition the child dies, then it dies gratuitously and the entire debt is replaced by the mother and the slave, as if the pledgor added the slave without the child.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from a Hanafi commentary on the book of Rahn. It discusses a specific scenario: the pledgor (rahin) has added a slave (ghulam) as additional collateral specifically with a pregnant mother slave (the original collateral). The ruling explains the effect of this specification. First, the total debt is divided between the mother and the slave proportionally. Then, the mother's portion is further divided between the mother and her unborn child (the child is considered part of the mother's share). If the mother dies after the addition, the portion of the debt allocated to her is cancelled (the mortgagee bears the loss), and the remaining debt is recoverable from the slave and the child (the child's portion was in the mother's share). This differs from an earlier case where the slave was added as subordinate to the child (i.e., without specification), where the outcome would be different. If instead the child dies, it dies as a free loss (gratuitous), and the entire debt is replaced by the mother and the slave, as if the child were never there. The reasoning is that the mother's death imposes a guarantee on the mortgagee (since the collateral perishes while in his possession), so the addition remains valid. This ruling underscores the importance of the pledgor's specification in determining distribution of liability when multiple collaterals are involved.

Key Terms
اضافہ (idāfah): Addition of an additional item to the existing pledge, with or without specification.
تابع (tābi‘): Subordinate; here it means the added slave is attached as a subsidiary to the child's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire debt becomes due immediately.
B) The debt is cancelled proportionally from the mother's share and remains on the slave and child.
C) The addition becomes void and the original pledge is restored.
D) The debt is divided equally among all heirs.

Key Takeaway
Specification of addition in a pledge determines how debt is distributed and which losses are borne by the mortgagee.

Substitution of Pledged Property and Renewing Possession
Ruling on substitution of pledged property with proof and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on substituting a pledged item to determine the legal status of the original and substitute, and evaluate the two opinions on the requirement of renewing possession.

Core Idea
Replacing a pledge does not release the original; the substitute is a trust until the original is returned.

This lesson examines a common scenario in the law of pledge (rahn): when a pledgor wants to replace the collateral with another asset. The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling from the foundational texts, but later scholars differ on whether the substitute must be physically re-possessed as a pledge. We will unpack the ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir and the subsequent debate among the mashayikh.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the ruling
Identify the act: a pledgor gives a second slave to replace the first pledged slave. State the ruling: the first remains a pledge (marhun), the second is a trust (amana) until the first is returned.
This is from the matn of al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Analyze the proof (dalil)
Read the Arabic text from Imam Muhammad. Understand the underlying principle: the first slave entered the mortgagee's liability (daman) through possession (qabd) and the debt. Both persist, so the liability continues. The second cannot enter liability because only one pledge is intended.
Key phrase: 'لا يخرج عن الضمان إلا بنقض القبض'
3
Examine the tanbih (note) on ibra'
The author adds 'as long as the debt remains' to exclude cases of remission (ibra'), where liability ends even if possession continues. Understand the exception.
Ibra' nullifies the debt, hence liability ends.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf on tajdid al-qabd
Two opinions among later Hanafi scholars: (1) Renewal of possession is required; (2) Not required. Note the analogies each group uses.
The first group compares to the case of receiving good dirhams after counterfeits; the second compares pledge to a gift.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Until the first is returned, the second does not become a pledge. If the first perishes, it's a loss for the mortgagee; if the second perishes, it's gratuitous. After return, the second enters liability, but whether a new possession is needed is debated.
In practice, renewal is often recommended as a precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قبض العين
ترجمہ پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ قبضہ کی تجدید شرط ہے اس لئے کہ ثانی غلام پر مرتین کا قبضہ امانت کا قبضہ ہے اور رہن کا قبضہ وصولیابی اور ضمان کا قبضہ ہوتا ہے تو قبضہ نیابت قبضہ ضمانت کی نیابت نہیں کرے گا جیسے وہ شخص جس کے دوسرے عمدہ دراہم ہوں پس اس نے کھوٹے وصول کئے جن کو عمدہ سمجھا تھا پھر کھوٹے ہونے کو جانا اور اس سے عمدہ طلب کئے اور عمدہ لے لئے تو عمدہ اس کے قبضہ میں امانت ہوں گے جب تک کہ وہ کھوٹوں کو واپس نہ کر دے اور قبضہ کی تجدید نہ کرے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ قبضہ کی تجدید شرط نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ رہن مثل سبد کے تبرع ہے جیسا کہ ہم ماقبل میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور امانت کا قبضہ ہبہ کے قبضہ کی نیابت کرتا ہے اور اس لئے کہ مین رہن تو امانت ہے اور قبضہ معین پر وارد ہوتا ہے تو امانت کا قبضہ عین کے قبضہ کی جانب سے نیابت کرے گا۔
تشریح بہر حال جب تک مرتین پہلے غلام سے اپنا قبضہ نہیں ہٹائیگا جب تک دوسر ا غلام اس کی ضمانت میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اس پر یہ سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ دوسرے غلام پر جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی یا وہی پہلا قبضہ کافی ہو جائے گا۔ اس میں ہمارے مشائخ کے دو گروہ ہیں ایک گروہ کہتا ہے کہ قبضہ کی تجدید ضروری ہے اور دوسرا فریق کہتا ہے کہ جدید قبضہ کی شرط نہیں ہے فریق اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسرے غلام پر مرتین کا قبضہ قبضہ ، امانت ہے اور مرہون پر مرتین کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمانت اور قبضہ استیفاء ہوتا ہے اور قبضہ امانت قبضہ ضمانت کی نیابت نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے تجدید قبضہ کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے کہ زید کے خالد کے ذمہ مثلاً ہزار درہم عمدہ کھرے واجب ہیں اور زید نے اس کو ہزار درہم کھوٹے دیئے زید نے لاعلمی میں لے لئے بعد میں اس کو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ کھوئے ہیں تو زید کو حق ہے کہ وہ خالد سے اپنے عمدہ درہم کا مطالبہ کرے اور لے لہذا خالد نے زید کو عمدہ درہم دیئے تو جب تک زید اول کھوٹے در اہموں کو خالد کے حوالہ کر کے پھر عمدہ درہموں پر جدید قبضہ نہ کرے جب تک عمدہ دراہم زید کے پاس
The pledgor placed a slave worth one thousand, then replaced it with another slave of equal value. So the first remains a pledge until the mortgagee returns it, and the second slave is a trust.
He (Imam Muhammad) said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'If he pledges a slave worth one thousand for one thousand, then he gives another slave of value one thousand as a pledge in place of the first, then the first remains a pledge until he returns it to the pledgor, and the mortgagee is a trustee for the other until he makes it in place of the first. Because the first entered into his liability by possession and debt, and both remain, so it does not exit from liability except by breaking the possession as long as the debt remains. And when the first remains in his liability, the second does not enter into his liability because both parties agreed to the entry of one of them, not both. So when he returns the first, the second enters into his liability.'
Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'So if he pledges a slave equal to one thousand for one thousand, then the pledgor gives the mortgagee another slave as a pledge in place of the first, then the first remains a pledge until the mortgagee returns it to the pledgor, and the mortgagee is a trustee for the second slave until he makes it in place of the first. Because the first slave entered into the mortgagee's liability due to possession and debt, and these two remain, so it does not exit from liability except by breaking the possession as long as the debt remains. And when the first slave is under the mortgagee's liability, the second does not enter his liability because both parties (pledgor and mortgagee) agree to the entry of one of them, not the entry of both. So when the mortgagee returns the first, then the second enters his liability.'
Explanation: Zaid borrowed one thousand rupees from Khalid and pledged a slave worth one thousand. Zaid has another slave also worth one thousand. Now Zaid wants to take the first slave from Khalid and place the second in its place. This is permissible. But if Khalid has not yet returned the first, then as long as it is not returned, the first is considered the pledge. So if in this case the first is destroyed, the debt is cancelled; and if the second is destroyed, because it is a trust, it is destroyed gratuitously. The reason is that the first slave entered the mortgagee's liability due to possession and debt, and possession is present, so it remains under liability. If the possession is terminated, then it is no longer liable. And when the first is under liability, the second does not enter liability because, by agreement of the parties, the pledge is one of them, not both. In any case, when the first slave is returned, then the second enters liability.
Note: 'As long as the debt remains...' i.e., as long as the debt remains and possession is not terminated, the pledge remains liable. The author added this phrase to avoid the case of ibra' (remission of debt), because in ibra' the liability ends even though possession remains (as in similar issues). Then it is said: Is the condition of renewal of possession required or not?
Then it was said: Renewal of possession is required because the mortgagee's hand on the second is a hand of trust, and the hand of pledge is a hand of fulfillment and liability, so one cannot substitute for the other. Like a person who has good dirhams owed to another, so he receives counterfeit dirhams thinking they are good, then learns they are counterfeit, demands the good ones, and takes them; then the good ones are a trust in his hand until he returns the counterfeits and renews possession. And it was said: Renewal is not required because pledge is a gratuitous contract like gift, as we explained before, and possession of trust substitutes for possession of gift; and because the pledge itself is a trust, and possession applies to the substance, so the possession of trust substitutes for possession of the substance.
Explanation: In any case, as long as the mortgagee has not lifted his possession from the first slave, the second slave does not enter his liability. But a question arises: does the second slave require a new possession, or is the first possession sufficient? Our mashayikh have two groups: one group says renewal of possession is necessary, the other says it is not. The first group's evidence: the mortgagee's possession of the second is a possession of trust, while the mortgagee's possession of the pledge is a possession of liability and fulfillment, and a possession of trust cannot substitute for a possession of liability. Their analogy: Zaid has one thousand good dirhams owed by Khalid. Zaid gives him one thousand counterfeit dirhams, takes them unknowingly, then learns they are counterfeit and demands the good ones. Khalid gives him good dirhams; then the good dirhams are a trust in Zaid's hand until he returns the counterfeits and renews possession.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the substitution of a pledged item. It begins by stating the ruling: if a pledgor wants to replace a pledged slave with another of equal value, the original pledge remains valid until the mortgagee returns the first slave. The second slave is held as a trust (amana) only, not as a pledge, until the first is returned. The proof is given in the Arabic matn from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad: the first slave entered the mortgagee's liability (daman) through possession (qabd) and the debt. Both possession and debt remain, so the first does not exit liability unless possession is terminated while the debt remains. Since the first remains in liability, the second cannot enter liability because both parties agreed to only one pledge, not two. When the first is returned, the second enters liability. The Urdu commentary explains with an example: Zaid pledges a slave to Khalid for a debt of 1000, then wants to replace it with another slave. As long as Khalid does not return the first, the first is the pledged item. If the first perishes, the debt is cancelled (the mortgagee bears the loss). If the second perishes, it dies gratuitously (no loss to either party). Then a note (tanbih) clarifies that the phrase 'as long as the debt remains' excludes the case of ibra' (remission), where liability ends despite possession. Then the passage discusses a ikhtilaf among later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) on whether renewal of possession (tajdid al-qabd) is required for the second slave to become a pledge. Two opinions are presented: one requires renewal, comparing it to the case of receiving good dirhams after returning counterfeit ones; the other does not require renewal, arguing that pledge is a gratuitous contract like gift, and trust possession can substitute for pledge possession. Both views are recorded without a clear tarjih in this text, but the ruling as practiced may require renewal as a precaution. The passage demonstrates Hanafi methodology: reliance on the foundational texts (Zahir al-Riwayah) and later scholarly ijtihad within the school.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession; physical takeover of the pledged item, which establishes the mortgagee's liability.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the mortgagee becomes liable for the pledged item as a security for the debt.
امانت (amana): Trust; an item held without liability for loss unless negligence is proven.
استیفاء (istifa'): Fulfillment; the mortgagee's hand on the pledge is also a hand of istifa' to recover the debt from the collateral.
تجديد قبض (tajdid al-qabd): Renewal of possession; physically taking the new collateral again with the intention of making it a pledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn from al-Jami' al-Saghir, when does the second slave enter into the mortgagee's liability (daman)?
A) Immediately upon being handed over.
B) Only after the first slave is returned to the pledgor.
C) Only after the mortgagee renews possession of the second slave.
D) After the debt is paid.

Key Takeaway
The original pledge remains binding until its possession is surrendered; the substitute enters liability only after the first is returned, and later scholars debate whether physical renewal of possession is required.

Rahn — Pledge
intermediate
6 min
Renewal of Possession When Pledged Item is Substituted
Discusses two Hanafi opinions on whether qabd must be renewed when a different item replaces the original pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi views on whether renewal of possession is required when a pledged item is substituted, and identify the preferred view according to Al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
When a pledged item is replaced, does trust possession suffice for guarantee? The Hanafi mashayikh differ.

In this lesson, we examine a specific intra-Hanafi dispute among later scholars (mashayikh) concerning the renewal of possession when a pledged item is substituted. The key distinction is between trust possession (qabd al-amanah) and guarantee possession (qabd al-daman). Two analogies are presented, one requiring renewal and one not. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to apply qiyas in pledge contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The case: a pledged item (e.g., a slave) is substituted with another item while the debt remains. The question is whether the pledgee (murtahin) must take a new possession (qabd) of the substitute to make it a valid pledge, or whether the existing trust possession suffices.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf among later scholars, not between the founding imams.
2
Identify the first view and its proof
First group (Qadhi Khan): renewal of possession is required. Their proof: trust possession (qabd al-amanah) cannot substitute for guarantee possession (qabd al-daman). Analogy: a creditor who unknowingly accepts counterfeit dirhams holds the good dirhams he later receives as trust until he returns the counterfeit and takes new possession.
This analogy emphasizes the functional difference between trust and guarantee possession.
3
Identify the second view and its proof
Second group (preferred by author of Al-Hidayah): renewal is not required. Two proofs: (1) Pledge is a gratuitous contract (tabarru‘) like a gift; in gift, existing trust possession suffices for validity. (2) The substance ('ayn) of the pledge is a trust, and possession (whether trust or guarantee) applies to the substance itself, so trust possession substitutes for guarantee possession.
This reasoning sees the possession of the substance as common to both types, making renewal unnecessary.
4
Note the tarjih
The author of Al-Hidayah (Al-Marghinani) prefers the second view. However, Qadhi Khan preferred the first view, and some later authorities follow him. The mufta bihi according to Al-Hidayah is that renewal is not required.
This illustrates that even within the Hanafi school, later scholars may hold differing positions.
5
Understand the practical implication
If a creditor already holds a replacement item as a trust (e.g., the debtor gave the item for safekeeping), according to the second view it becomes a valid pledge without a new formal qabd. The debt remains secured.
This avoids unnecessary formalities and protects the creditor's interest.

تشریح بہر حال جب تک مرتین پہلے غلام سے اپنا قبضہ نہیں ہٹائیگا جب تک دوسر ا غلام اس کی ضمانت میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اس پر یہ سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ دوسرے غلام پر جدید قبضہ کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی یا وہی پہلا قبضہ کافی ہو جائے گا۔ اس میں ہمارے مشائخ کے دو گروہ ہیں ایک گروہ کہتا ہے کہ قبضہ کی تجدید ضروری ہے اور دوسرا فریق کہتا ہے کہ جدید قبضہ کی شرط نہیں ہے فریق اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسرے غلام پر مرتین کا قبضہ قبضہ ، امانت ہے اور مرہون پر مرتین کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمانت اور قبضہ استیفاء ہوتا ہے اور قبضہ امانت قبضہ ضمانت کی نیابت نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے تجدید قبضہ کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے کہ زید کے خالد کے ذمہ مثلاً ہزار درہم عمدہ کھرے واجب ہیں اور زید نے اس کو ہزار درہم کھوٹے دیئے زید نے لاعلمی میں لے لئے بعد میں اس کو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ کھوئے ہیں تو زید کو حق ہے کہ وہ خالد سے اپنے عمدہ درہم کا مطالبہ کرے اور لے لہذا خالد نے زید کو عمدہ درہم دیئے تو جب تک زید اول کھوٹے در اہموں کو خالد کے حوالہ کر کے پھر عمدہ درہموں پر جدید قبضہ نہ کرے جب تک عمدہ دراہم زید کے پاس امانت ہوں گے اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکور میں بھی ہوگا۔ لہذا اگر جدید سے پہلے عمدہ دراہم ہلاک ہو جائیں تو خالد کا مال ہلاک ہوگا کیونکہ یہ زید کے پاس امانت تھے ۔
مثلاً زید نے دہلی میں کھرے درہم وصول کر کے رکھے اور دیوبند میں جا کر کھوٹے درہم واپس کئے اور زیدا بھی لوٹ کر دہلی نہیں آیا اور جدید قبضہ نہیں کیا تھا کہ کھرے درہم ضائع ہو گئے تو یہ مدیون ( خالد ) کا مال گیا اسی طرح امانتی غلام رہن میں سمجھنا چاہیے۔ دوسرے فریق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح ہبہ تبرع ہے اسی طرح عقد رہن بھی تبرع ہے ، اوائل کتاب الرہن میں جس کا بیان گزر چکا ہے اور اگر زید نے خالد کے پاس اپنا کوئی مال امانت رکھا ہو اور پھر وہی مال خالد کو ہبہ کر دیا ہو جس میں قبضہ شرط ہے تو وہی پہلا قبضہ امانت قبضہ ہبہ سمجھا جائے گا اور جدید قبضہ کی حاجت پیش نہیں آئے گی یہ فریق ثانی کی پہلی دلیل ہے ۔ اور فریق ثانی کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماقبل میں متعددجگہ گزر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کا عین مرتہن کے پاس امانت ہوتا ہے اور مرہون کی مالیت ہی مضمون ہوتی ہے، اور جب مرتہن نے دوسرے غلام پر قبضہ کیا ہے تو اس کے عین پر قبضہ کیا ہے بہر حال قبضہ امانت ہو یا قبضہ ضمانت ہو دونوں کے اندراصل قبضہ عین پر ہوتا ہے اور اس کی بیعت میں مالیت پر قبضہ ہوتا ہے تو جب قبضہ امانت میں ( جب کہ دوسرے غلام پر قبضہ کیا ہے ) قبضہ مین موجود ہے اور یہی عین کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمانت میں بھی ہوگا تو تجدید قبضہ تحصیل حاصل ہو گا لہذا ہم نے کہا کہ قبضہ امانت اس قبضہ مین کی جانب سے نیابت کرے گا جو کہ قبضہ ضمانت میں ہوتا ہے۔
تنبیہ صاحب ہدایہ کے اسلوب سے یہ بات واضح ہوتی ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک ثانی مختار ہے اور علامہ قہستانی نے کہا ہے کہ قاضی خان کے نزدیک اول مختار ہے شامی ص ۳۳۸ ج ۵ ۔
The point is that the first slave had entered into the pledgee's guarantee due to possession and debt, and he is still in possession, so this slave will also remain under guarantee. Yes, if he ends possession, then he will not be guaranteed. And when the first is still under guarantee, the second has not entered into guarantee because, by agreement of both parties, the pawned item is one of them, not both. In any case, when he returns the first slave, then the second slave will enter into his guarantee.
Caution: As long as the debt remains and possession is not terminated, the pawned item remains guaranteed. The author added this phrase to avoid the case of immunity (ibra'), because in ibra' the guarantee ends despite possession. (Kama sabaqa) Is renewal of possession necessary or not?
Then it was said: Renewal of possession is a condition because the pledgee's possession over the second (slave) is a possession of trust, while the possession of a pledge is a possession for recovery and guarantee, so it does not serve as a substitute. Like a person who has good dirhams owed to him, then he receives counterfeit (dirhams) thinking they were good, then learns of the counterfeitness, demands the good ones, and takes them. The good ones are in his hand as trust until he returns the counterfeit and renews possession. And it was said: Renewal is not a condition because a pledge is a gratuitous contract like a gift, as we explained before, and possession of trust serves as possession of a gift. And because the pledged item itself is a trust, and possession applies to the substance, so the trust possession serves as possession of the substance.
Translation: Then it was said that renewal of possession is a condition because the pledgee's possession of the second slave is a possession of trust, and the possession of a pledge is a possession for recovery and guarantee. Possession (of trust) cannot substitute for possession of guarantee, like in the example of the good dirhams... And it was said that renewal is not a condition because a pledge is gratuitous like a gift, as stated earlier, and the possession of trust substitutes for the possession of a gift, and because the substance of the pledge is trust, and possession applies to the substance, so trust possession substitutes for possession of the substance.
Explanation: In any case, as long as the pledgee does not remove his possession from the first slave, the second slave will not enter his guarantee. But then the question arises: is a new possession of the second slave required, or will the same first possession suffice? There are two groups among our scholars: one group says renewal of possession is necessary; the other says it is not required. The first group's proof: the pledgee's possession of the second slave is a possession of trust, while possession of a pawned item is a possession of guarantee and recovery, so trust possession cannot substitute for guarantee possession, therefore renewal is needed. Their exact example: Zayd has, say, one thousand good dirhams due from Khalid. Zayd gives him a thousand counterfeit dirhams, and Zayd unknowingly takes them. Later he discovers they are counterfeit and demands good dirhams from Khalid. Then Khalid gives good dirhams to Zayd. As long as Zayd does not first return the counterfeit dirhams to Khalid and then take new possession of the good dirhams, the good dirhams will be in Zayd's possession as a trust. If the good dirhams are destroyed before new possession, the loss falls on Khalid (the debtor) because they were a trust with Zayd. For example, Zayd took possession of good dirhams in Delhi, then went to Deoband and returned the counterfeit dirhams, and did not return to Delhi to take new possession, and the good dirhams were lost — that is the debtor (Khalid)'s property lost. Similarly, the trust slave in pledge should be understood. The second group's proof: just as a gift is gratuitous, the contract of pledge is also gratuitous, as described in the beginning of the Book of Pledge. And if Zayd placed some property as trust with Khalid and then gave that same property as a gift to Khalid, which requires possession, then that same trust possession will be considered possession for the gift, and no new possession is needed. That is the first proof. The second proof: it has been mentioned in many places before that the substance of the pawned item is a trust with the pledgee, and only its value is guaranteed. When the pledgee takes possession of the second slave, he has taken possession of its substance. Whether it is trust possession or guarantee possession, both fundamentally involve possession of the substance. In guarantee possession, it is the possession of the value; but since trust possession already exists (when he took possession of the second slave), and this possession of the substance would also be present in guarantee possession, requiring renewal would be obtaining something already obtained. Therefore, we say that trust possession substitutes for the possession that occurs in guarantee possession.
Note: From the style of the author of Al-Hidayah, it is clear that the second view is preferred according to him. Allama Qahastani said that according to Qadhi Khan the first view is preferred. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 338)
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling on what happens when a pledged item (first slave) is replaced by another (second slave) while the debt remains. The issue is whether the pledgee (murtahin) must take a new, formal possession of the second slave to make it a valid pledge, or whether his existing possession (as an amanah/trust) suffices. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute among the later scholars (mashayikh), not between the founding imams. Both views are based on analogical reasoning (qiyas). The first view (preferred by Qadhi Khan) says new possession is required because the nature of possession in pledge is different from trust possession: pledge possession implies guarantee and the right to recover the debt, while trust possession implies merely safe-keeping. Analogous to the case of counterfeit dirhams: if someone pays a debt with bad coins, the creditor who unknowingly accepts them holds them as trust until he returns them and takes new possession of good coins. Similarly, the second slave is currently held as trust, not as a guarantee, so a new qabd is needed. The second view (preferred by the author of Al-Hidayah) says no renewal is needed because the pledge contract itself is gratuitous (tabarru') like a gift; in gift, existing trust possession suffices for validity. Also, the substance ('ayn) of the pledge is a trust, and possession (whether trust or guarantee) applies to the substance, so trust possession substitutes for guarantee possession. The note clarifies that the later authoritative view (mufta bihi) is the second view according to the author of Al-Hidayah, though Qadhi Khan preferred the first.

Key Terms
قبض الضمان (qabd al-daman): Possession that creates guarantee (daman) for the pledgee; the pledged item is held as security for the debt.
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous contract (like gift or pledge) done without direct exchange; in pledge, the pledgee does not pay for the right to hold the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi dispute over substituting a pledged item, which view does the author of Al-Hidayah prefer?
A) That renewal of possession is required, because trust possession cannot substitute for guarantee possession.
B) That renewal of possession is not required, because pledge is a gift-like gratuitous contract and trust possession suffices.
C) That renewal of possession is required only if the second item is of lower value.
D) That the matter is left to the pledgee's discretion.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a pledged item is substituted, the preferred view is that no new possession is required, as trust possession suffices by analogy to gift and to possession of the substance.

Debt Release and Pledge: Liability after Ibra'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability after ibra'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on liability for a pledged item that perishes after debt release (ibra'), distinguish the positions of the majority and Imam Zufar, and apply the condition of withholding (man') to determine liability.

Core Idea
When the debt is released, the pledge loses its guarantee; the pledgee holds as trustee and is not liable for loss.

This passage addresses a scenario where a pledgee forgives the debt (ibra') and then the pledged item is lost. The Hanafi school uses istihsan to rule that the pledgee is not liable, contrary to Zufar who applies strict qiyas. We will dissect the reasoning and the exception for wrongful withholding.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the two positions
Identify the facts: the pledgee releases the debt, then the pledged item perishes in his hands. The Hanafi position (istihsan) says no liability; Zufar says liability.
The text explicitly says 'khilafan li Zufar' – this is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Analyse the Hanafi istihsan argument
The Hanafi reasoning: the pledge is guaranteed only by the debt or its cause (jiha). When the debt is nullified by ibra' or hiba, the guarantee ceases, so the item is held as an amanah (trust). Loss without negligence incurs no liability.
Istihsan here relaxes the strict analogy that the pledgee should always be liable because he has possession.
3
Consider Zufar's qiyas argument
Although the text does not detail Zufar's reasoning, we infer that he held the pledgee liable because the item remains in his possession and the original contract of pledge might still imply guarantee. The Hanafi rebuttal is that guarantee is conditional on the debt, not mere possession.
Zufar's view is based on strict qiyas (analogy) that possession creates liability unless returned.
4
Apply the exception: wrongful withholding (man')
If the pledgee refuses to return the item after debt release, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and is liable for loss. This is because he no longer has the right to detain it.
The key condition: if the pledgee actively prevents return, liability attaches.
5
Synthesise with the example
Using the horse/mare example: Zayd forgives the debt; the mare perishes. Zayd is not liable. But if Zayd had withheld the mare, he would be liable. This illustrates the rule.
The example demonstrates the practical difference between the two views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أبرأ المرتهن الراهن عن الدين او وهبه منه ثم هلك الرهن فى يد المرتهن يهلک بغير شئ استحسانا خلافا لزفر لان الرهن مضمون بالدين او بجهته عند توهم الوجود كما فى الدين الموعود ولم يبق الدين بالا برا او الهبة ولا جهته لسقوطه الا اذا احدث منعا لانه يصير به غاصبا اذلم يبق له ولاية المنع
ترجمہ اور اگر مرتہن نے راہن کو قرض سے بری کر دیا یا مرتبین نے قرض راہن کو ہبہ کر دیا پھر مرہون مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو گیا تو استحسانا بغیر کسی شئی کے ہلاک ہو گا۔ اختلاف ہے زفر کا ( ہماری دلیل ) اس لئے کہ رہن مضمون ہوتا ہے قرض کی وجہ سے یا جہت دین کی وجہ سے وجود قرض کے متوہم ہونے کے وقت جیسے دین موعود میں اور ابراء یا ہبہ کی وجہ سے نہ قرض باقی رہا اور نہ اس کی جہت باقی رہی قرض کے ساقط ہو جانے کی وجہ سے مگر جب کہ مرتہن نے انکار کا احدث کیا ہو اس لئے کہ مرتہن انکار کی وجہ سے غاصب ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ مرتہن کے لئے انکار کرنے کی ولایت باقی نہیں رہی۔
تشریح زید کے خالد کے ذمہ ہزار روپے قرض تھا خالد نے اس کے بدلہ میں اپنی گھوڑی جو ہزار روپے کی ہے زید کے پاس رہن رکھی تھی ۔ اب صورت یہ ہوئی کہ زید نے اپنا قرض معاف کر دیا یا ہبہ کر دیا تو اب زید کو چاہیے کہ خالد کی گھوڑی واپس کرتا لیکن ابھی واپس کرنے کی
And if the pledgee releases the pawn-giver from the debt, or gifts the debt to him, then the pledge perishes in the hands of the pledgee, it perishes without liability, by istihsan, contrary to Zufar. Because the pledge is guaranteed by the debt or its cause at the time of presumptive existence, as in a promised debt. And through release or gift, neither the debt nor its cause remains due to its nullification, except if he (the pledgee) creates opposition (man') because then he becomes a usurper (ghasib), as he no longer has authority to oppose.
Translation: And if the pledgee releases the pawn-giver from the debt, or gifts the debt to him, then the pledge perishes in the pledgee's possession, it perishes without anything (i.e., no liability) by istihsan, contrary to Zufar. (Our proof) because the pledge is guaranteed by the debt or its cause at the time of presumptive existence, like in a promised debt. And through release or gift, neither the debt nor its cause remains due to its nullification. Except if he creates opposition, because then he becomes a usurper, as he no longer has authority to oppose.
Explanation: Zayd had a debt of one thousand rupees from Khalid. Khalid gave his mare, worth one thousand rupees, as a pledge to Zayd. Now the scenario is that Zayd forgave his debt or gifted it. Now Zayd should return Khalid's mare, but before returning...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling (by istihsan) that when the pledgee (murtahin) releases the pawner (rahin) from the debt (ibra') or gifts the debt back to him (hiba), and the pledged item perishes in the pledgee's hands, the pledgee is not liable. This is contrary to Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam who disagreed). The reasoning: the pledge is guaranteed only by the existence of the debt or its cause (the jiha of the debt). Once the debt is extinguished (by ibra' or hiba), there is no longer any debt or cause to justify the guarantee. However, if the pledgee wrongfully withholds the item (i.e., refuses to return it after the debt is cancelled), he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and will be liable for its value if it perishes, because he no longer has the right to detain it. The example clarifies: Zayd lends money and takes a mare as pledge; if he forgives the debt, the mare should be returned. If it is destroyed before return, Zayd is not liable (since no debt remains), unless he actively prevented return (then he is a usurper). This shows the Hanafi application of istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas, and the distinction between guarantee based on debt and liability based on usurpation.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibra'): Release or forgiveness of a debt by the creditor; extinguishes the debt without payment.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of legal reasoning where a weaker analogy is set aside in favor of a stronger one or public interest; here, it allows that the pledgee is not liable despite the item being in his hands.
منع (man'): Prevention or withholding; here, the pledgee's wrongful refusal to return the pledged item after debt release.
غاصب (ghasib): Usurper; one who wrongfully takes or detains another's property; liable for the value if it perishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition does the pledgee become liable for a pledged item that perishes after debt release?
A) If the debt was forgiven but not yet accepted by the debtor.
B) If the pledgee wrongfully withholds the item (man') after the debt is released.
C) If the item perishes within a year of the debt release.
D) The pledgee is always liable regardless of conditions.

Key Takeaway
After ibra' (debt release), the pledgee holds the pledged item as a trust and is not liable for its loss unless he wrongfully withholds it.

8 min
Replacement of Pledged Property: Is New Possession Required?
Ruling on trust property replaced with defective goods in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether new possession is required when the pledged object is replaced, and apply the analogy to gift to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
When the pledged object is replaced, trust possession suffices as pledge possession — renewing it would achieve the already achieved.

This lesson examines a nuanced issue in the law of pledge (rahn): when the mortgaged property is substituted with other goods, does the mortgagee need to take fresh possession, or does the existing trust possession carry over? The passage from al-Hidayah presents two arguments from the second party (the view that trust possession suffices), based on a qiyas to gift and an analysis of the nature of possession. We will unpack the reasoning and note the internal Hanafi preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and loss
The passage begins by stating that if trust property (the original pledged goods) is replaced with defective goods before new possession, the loss of the original falls on the debtor. Work through the example: Zaid receives genuine dirhams in Delhi, goes to Deoband, returns counterfeit dirhams, and the genuine ones are lost before Zaid takes new possession. The loss is on Khalid (the debtor) because the genuine dirhams were still a trust.
This sets the factual context for the legal question.
2
State the second party's first argument: analogy to gift
The second party argues that pledge is like gift (both tabarru'). In gift, if the donee already has trust possession of the object, that same possession suffices for the gift; no new possession is needed. Similarly, in pledge, trust possession should suffice for pledge possession.
The qiyas is based on the shared characteristic of gratuitousness.
3
State the second party's second argument: possession of the 'ayn
The pledged object is a trust with the mortgagee regarding its specific object ('ayn), while only its value is guaranteed. When the mortgagee takes possession of the replacement, he already has possession of the specific object via trust. Since possession of the 'ayn is common to both trust and guarantee, renewing it would be superfluous (tahsil al-hasil).
This argument focuses on the nature of possession itself.
4
Identify the ruling and its basis
Based on these arguments, the Hanafi position is that trust possession deputizes for pledge possession. Therefore, when the pledged property is replaced, the mortgagee does not need to take new possession; the existing trust possession is sufficient to validate the pledge.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The author of al-Hidayah prefers the second view (trust suffices), while Qadhi Khan prefers the first view (new possession required). In practice, the mufta bihi is the chosen view of al-Hidayah, though both are valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امانت ہوں گے اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکور میں بھی ہوگا۔ لہذا اگر جدید سے پہلے عمدہ دراہم ہلاک ہو جائیں تو خالد کا مال ہلاک ہوگا کیونکہ یہ زید کے پاس امانت تھے ۔
مثلاً زید نے دہلی میں کھرے درہم وصول کر کے رکھے اور دیوبند میں جا کر کھوٹے درہم واپس کئے اور زیدا بھی لوٹ کر دہلی نہیں آیا اور جدید قبضہ نہیں کیا تھا کہ کھرے درہم ضائع ہو گئے تو یہ مدیون ( خالد ) کا مال گیا اسی طرح امانتی غلام رہن میں سمجھنا چاہیے۔ دوسرے فریق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح ہبہ تبرع ہے اسی طرح عقد رہن بھی تبرع ہے ، اوائل کتاب الرہن میں جس کا بیان گزر چکا ہے اور اگر زید نے خالد کے پاس اپنا کوئی مال امانت رکھا ہو اور پھر وہی مال خالد کو ہبہ کر دیا ہو جس میں قبضہ شرط ہے تو وہی پہلا قبضہ امانت قبضہ ہبہ سمجھا جائے گا اور جدید قبضہ کی حاجت پیش نہیں آئے گی یہ فریق ثانی کی پہلی دلیل ہے ۔ اور فریق ثانی کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماقبل میں متعددجگہ گزر چکا ہے کہ مرہون کا عین مرتہن کے پاس امانت ہوتا ہے اور مرہون کی مالیت ہی مضمون ہوتی ہے، اور جب مرتہن نے دوسرے غلام پر قبضہ کیا ہے تو اس کے عین پر قبضہ کیا ہے بہر حال قبضہ امانت ہو یا قبضہ ضمانت ہو دونوں کے اندراصل قبضہ عین پر ہوتا ہے اور اس کی بیعت میں مالیت پر قبضہ ہوتا ہے تو جب قبضہ امانت میں ( جب کہ دوسرے غلام پر قبضہ کیا ہے ) قبضہ مین موجود ہے اور یہی عین کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمانت میں بھی ہوگا تو تجدید قبضہ تحصیل حاصل ہو گا لہذا ہم نے کہا کہ قبضہ امانت اس قبضہ مین کی جانب سے نیابت کرے گا جو کہ قبضہ ضمانت میں ہوتا ہے۔
تنبیہ صاحب ہدایہ کے اسلوب سے یہ بات واضح ہوتی ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک ثانی مختار ہے اور علامہ قہستائی نے کہا ہے کہ قاضی خان کے نزدیک اول مختار ہے شامی ص ۳۳۸ ج ۵ ۔
They will be trusts. Similarly, in the mentioned issue it will also be. Therefore, if before the new (possession) the good dirhams are destroyed, then Khalid's property is destroyed because they were a trust with Zaid. For example, Zaid received genuine dirhams in Delhi and kept them, and went to Deoband and returned counterfeit dirhams, and Zaid did not return to Delhi and had not taken new possession when the genuine dirhams were lost, so this is the debtor's (Khalid's) property that went. Similarly, a trust slave should be understood in pledge. The second party's argument is that just as gift is a gratuitous contract, similarly the contract of pledge is also gratuitous, as has been mentioned at the beginning of the book of pledge. And if Zaid had placed some of his property as a trust with Khalid, and then gifted that same property to Khalid, wherein possession is a condition, then the first possession of trust will be considered as possession of gift and there will be no need for new possession. This is the first argument of the second party. And the second argument of the second party is that it has passed in multiple places before that the specific object of the pledge is a trust with the mortgagee, and only the value of the pledged property is guaranteed. And when the mortgagee took possession of the second slave, he took possession of its specific object. In any case, whether it is possession of trust or possession of guarantee, the original possession in both is over the specific object, and in its sale, possession is over the value. So when in possession of trust (when he took possession of the second slave), the possession of the specific object is present, and this same possession of the specific object will also be in possession of guarantee, so renewing possession would be achieving what is already achieved. Therefore we said that the possession of trust will deputize on behalf of this possession which occurs in possession of guarantee. Note: From the style of the author of al-Hidayah, it is clear that according to him the second is chosen, and Allamah Qahistani said that according to Qadhi Khan the first is chosen. (Shami, vol. 5, p. 338)
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on replacement of pledged property and the necessity of new possession. The author begins by stating that if trust property is replaced with defective goods before new possession, the loss falls on the debtor (the original owner) because the goods were still a trust until new possession. The example clarifies: Zaid receives genuine dirhams as a trust, replaces them with counterfeit ones while away, and the genuine ones are lost before Zaid returns and takes new possession – the loss is on Khalid. The second party (opponent) presents two arguments: (1) Pledge is like a gift, both gratuitous; in gift, trust possession suffices for gift possession, so in pledge also, trust possession should suffice. (2) The pledged object is a trust with the mortgagee regarding its specific object, and only its value is guaranteed; possession of the specific object is common to both trust and guarantee, so when the mortgagee takes possession of the second slave, he already has possession of the specific object via trust, and renewing it would be superfluous. Therefore, the Hanafi ruling is that trust possession acts as a deputy for pledge possession. The author then notes a point of internal Hanafi preference: according to al-Hidayah's style, the second opinion (that trust possession suffices) is chosen, while Qahistani reports that Qadhi Khan prefers the first opinion (requiring new possession). This passage is a typical sharh expansion, analyzing the basis of possession in pledge and analogy to gift.

Key Terms
امانت (amanah): Property held in trust, not guaranteeing its value if destroyed without negligence.
قبضہ (qabdah): Possession, a condition for the validity of contracts like gift and pledge.
تبرع (tabarru'): Gratuitous disposition, i.e., a contract not primarily for exchange of value.
عین ('ayn): The specific object itself, as opposed to its value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view in al-Hidayah, when the pledged property is replaced with another item that the mortgagee already holds as a trust, what is required for the new pledge to be valid?
A) The mortgagee must take new physical possession of the replacement.
B) The mortgagee must write a new contract.
C) The existing trust possession suffices; no new possession is needed.
D) The replacement must be of equal value.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the pledged object is replaced, if the mortgagee already holds the replacement as a trust, that trust possession suffices for the pledge without new possession.
